# Capabilities ŌĆö the loop's only success metric

Append-only inventory of **real, user-exercisable** Muse
capabilities. One line per capability: what the user can do, the
exact command/surface, and the executable check that proves it.

Rules (enforced by `.claude/rules/iteration-loop.md`):

- Every shipped outward goal MUST append exactly one new line here.
  The `<check>` MUST be a concrete automated test or smoke id that
  actually runs green under `pnpm check` / `pnpm smoke:broad` /
  `pnpm smoke:live` and asserts the *capability* end-to-end (not
  that code compiles). Prose with no runnable id is not a check.
- **Cross-time falsification:** every iteration's first action is
  to run the newest line's check and prove it still passes. A
  faked/broken line = the next iteration's whole job is to fix it.
- **Regression sweep:** every 10th iteration re-runs ALL checks;
  any regression = next iteration must restore it.
- A request/response-path capability whose `smoke:live` did NOT
  actually run is tagged `[UNVERIFIED-LIVE]`; it does not count
  until a later iteration runs the live check and drops the tag.
- Append-only. Never delete or weaken a line.
- **The success metric is NOT this line count.** It is
  `OUTWARD-TARGETS.md` bullets flipped `[ ]`ŌåÆ`[x]`. A line here is
  the *evidence* for a flip (cite the bullet it delivers); a line
  that adds no bullet flip is thin and does not satisfy the metric.
  No bullet flipped in the last 5 iterations ŌćÆ next iteration's
  sole mandate is to flip one end-to-end. Flat bullets =
  degeneration; act on it ŌĆö never stop, never ask a human.

Format: `- [<axis>] <capability> ŌĆö <command/surface> ŌĆö <runnable check id> ŌĆö P<n> bullet`
axis Ōłł Reach | Anticipation | Autonomy | Presence

## Inventory

P0ŌĆōP21's full verified ledger is preserved in
`archive/CAPABILITIES-through-2026-05-27.md` (human reset
2026-05-27 to keep the loop-facing file lean ŌĆö history intact, not
deleted). The lines below are the delivered foundation that the
active P22 target extends; new P22 lines append here.

- [Anticipation] Proactive notice loop (upcoming events / reminders) ŌĆö `apps/api` proactive daemon tick ŌĆö `apps/api` proactive-tick tests
- [Anticipation] Self-queued follow-up promises fire later ŌĆö followups daemon tick ŌĆö `runDueFollowups` tests
- [Autonomy] Standing-objective evaluation fires its actuator ŌĆö objectives daemon tick ŌĆö `runDueObjectives` tests
- [Anticipation] Ambient OS signal drives a proactive notice ŌĆö `runAmbientNoticeTick` + `MacOsActiveWindowSource` ŌĆö ambient-notice-loop tests
- [Anticipation] Page-change web-watch fires an edge-triggered notice ŌĆö `createWebWatchRunner` (HTTP + Chrome source) ŌĆö web-watch-runner / web-watch-chrome tests
- [Anticipation] Proactive notice delivered to a real channel ŌĆö `ProactiveNoticeSink` over the messaging registry (Telegram) ŌĆö `sendWithRetry` + proactive-notice-loop tests
- [Anticipation] One-process daemon launcher fires a real proactive tick ŌĆö `muse daemon --once` ŌĆö `apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.test.ts` (imminent task delivered to a contract-faithful messaging sink; quiet tick sends nothing; unknown provider fails closed) ŌĆö P22-1a bullet
- [Presence] Episode forgetting is now importance-aware ŌĆö a pivotal old session resists being vacuumed away while a trivial recent one fades (FadeMem, arXiv 2601.18642: biologically-inspired forgetting, decay modulated by importance) ŌĆö `vacuumEpisodes` dropped purely-oldest-by-`endedAt` at the cap; now `computeEpisodeRetention` scores each episode `exp(-ageDays / (halfLife┬Ę(1 + w┬Ęimportance/10)))` so importance EXTENDS the half-life (importance-10 ŌćÆ ~3├Ś slower fade), and `selectRetainedEpisodes` keeps the highest-retention `cap` (newest-then-id tie-break). Back-compatible: an UNSCORED corpus reduces to recency ordering, so chronological vacuum is byte-identical until importance is present ŌĆö `@muse/mcp` episode-retention.test.ts (age decay; importance slows fade; unscoredŌåÆrecency; unparseableŌåÆ0; importance tips comparable ages: a 35-day importance-10 session out-retains a 25-day importance-1 one at the cap; deterministic ties) + existing vacuum suite stays green (unscored episodes still pruned oldest-first) ŌĆö research-applied slice (no new dep, deterministic/local; builds on the importance arc)
- [Presence] Auto-extracted memory now resolves each fact with an explicit operation instead of blind-overwriting (Mem0, arXiv 2504.19413: per-candidate ADD/UPDATE/DELETE/NOOP) ŌĆö `classifyMemoryOperation(existing, incoming)` is deterministic over the extractor's output (no extra model call): NOOP when a value re-confirms what's stored ŌåÆ SKIPS the redundant write + provenance entry (a re-mention no longer logs a fresh "learned" event); DELETE when the value is a no-value/retraction token (none/n/a/unknown/ņŚåņØī/ļ¬©ļ”ä/ŌĆ”) ŌåÆ the key is FORGOTTEN via the store's `forget` instead of storing junk like "unknown"; ADD/UPDATE upsert + record provenance as before; the auto-extract persist reads existing memory once and routes each fact/preference through it ŌĆö `@muse/memory` memory-operation.test.ts (classifier: add/noop/update/delete EN+KO tokens; auto-extract integration: re-confirm ŌåÆ no new provenance, changed ŌåÆ upsert+provenance, retraction ŌåÆ key forgotten) + full memory suite 213 green (new facts still ADD as before, back-compatible) ŌĆö research-applied slice (arXiv id cited in code; deterministic, no new dep, no extra LLM call)
- [Reach] A natural-language tool-selection path is available + measured against the native one (Natural Language Tools, arXiv 2510.14453: stating the tool choice in prose + parsing it deterministically beats forcing JSON on small/open-weight models) ŌĆö `parseNaturalLanguageToolSelection(text, toolNames)` deterministically maps a model's prose answer to one known tool (earliest-named wins; whole-token match so `time_now` ŌēĀ `my_time_now_helper`; explicit no-tool/none/ņŚåņØī ŌåÆ none) and `pnpm eval:tools:nl` compares NATIVE (Hermes JSON tool-call) vs NL one-shot accuracy on the confusable time set ŌĆö `@muse/tools` nl-tool-selection.test.ts (single pick, "use A not B"ŌåÆA, no-tool EN+KO, embedded-name not matched, empty) + LIVE qwen3:8b: native 7/7 (100%) AND NL 7/7 (100%) on the confusable time set ŌĆö verified finding: Muse's tuned tool names are ALREADY at the selection ceiling, so the NL path is kept as a reusable parser + comparison gate rather than wired (evidence-based: add NL complexity only when a confusable set's native accuracy drops below ceiling) ŌĆö research-applied slice (arXiv id cited in code; no new dep, core tool path untouched)
- [Presence] Muse applies LEARNED STRATEGIES from past feedback, not just avoidances ŌĆö a self-improving playbook (ACE ŌĆö Agentic Context Engineering, arXiv 2510.04618: a frozen model improves by accumulating small strategy deltas in an evolving context, no fine-tuning) ŌĆö the POSITIVE counterpart to veto-avoidance: `applyPlaybook` injects a `[Learned Strategies]` system block (mirrors the veto-avoidance seam; conservative ŌĆö zero strategies/no userId ŌćÆ exact no-op; fail-open) wired into the live agent-runtime context pipeline behind a duck-typed `PlaybookProvider`; the durable `~/.muse/playbook.json` store (`@muse/mcp`, atomic/tolerant/capped) is adapted by `buildPlaybookProvider` (MUSE_PLAYBOOK default-on) and populated via `muse playbook add|list|remove` ŌĆö `@muse/agent-core` playbook.test.ts (conservative/fail-open/inject + injection-collapse + LIVE-runtime wiring: a recorded strategy reaches a real createAgentRuntime run's system prompt, none ŌåÆ no-op) + LIVE qwen3:8b EFFECT MEASUREMENT: with the strategy "answer in at most 6 words" injected, a question that drew a long multi-paragraph reply WITHOUT it returned a 7-word "Paris. Famous for art, fashion, and culture." WITH it ŌĆö the learned strategy measurably changed the model's output ŌĆö research-applied slice (arXiv id cited in code; no new dep; mirrors the proven veto-avoidance pattern end-to-end)

- [Presence] Muse auto-LEARNS a strategy from a correction the user made ŌĆö at session end it distills a generalised `[Learned Strategies]` entry from a corrected exchange into the SAME `~/.muse/playbook.json` (ReasoningBank, arXiv 2509.25140: a self-evolving agent distills reusable strategies from its own experience; the outcome signal is the RELIABLE explicit correction, NOT small-model self-judgement per arXiv 2404.17140) ŌĆö auto at REPL exit (`MUSE_PLAYBOOK_DISTILL_ENABLED`, default off) + manual `muse playbook distill`; pipeline = `detectCorrections` (EN+KO, precision-first rule pass) ŌåÆ `distillStrategyFromCorrection` (one LLM call, secret-redacted, fail-soft) ŌåÆ `strategyTextSimilarity` dedup (Ōēź0.6, makes re-runs idempotent) ŌåÆ `recordPlaybookStrategy` ŌĆö `packages/agent-core/test/correction-distiller.test.ts` (detector EN+KO + false-positive guard + no-prior-assistant + cap; distiller parse/omit-tag/fail-soft) + `playbook.test.ts` (similarity) + `apps/cli/src/chat-distill-corrections.test.ts` (records from a corrected session, skips no-correction, dedups, skips no-userId) + `commands-playbook.test.ts` (distill subcommand); LIVE qwen3:8b: the Korean correction "ĻĘĖĻ▓ī ņĢäļŗłļØ╝ ļČłļ”┐ ĒÅ¼ņØĖĒŖĖļĪ£ ņĀĢļ”¼ĒĢ┤ņżś" distilled "when asked to summarise, use bullet points not prose" into the playbook end-to-end via `muse playbook distill` ŌĆö research-applied slice (arXiv ids cited in code; deterministic detection+dedup, single offline LLM call, no new dep; completes ReasoningBank retrievalŌåÆdistillation)
- [Knowledge] knowledge_search grades retrieval confidence and FRAMES weak grounding as low-confidence instead of telling the small local model to cite it (CRAG, arXiv 2401.15884: a lightweight retrieval evaluator scores evidence quality) ŌĆö `classifyRetrievalConfidence` over the TOP match's ABSOLUTE cosine (surfaced as `KnowledgeMatch.cosine`, separate from the hybrid RRF `score`): confidentŌåÆ"cite the [source]", ambiguousŌåÆ"Possibly-related (LOW confidence ŌĆö verify, don't cite as fact)", noneŌåÆno passages; `renderKnowledgeMatches` (the agent `knowledge_search` + notes corpus-search tools) and the ambient `createKnowledgeEnricher` (Related line only when confident) gate on it ŌĆö `packages/agent-core/test/knowledge-recall-agent.test.ts` (verdict none/ambiguous/confident; cosine surfaced in both paths; render header by verdict) + `knowledge-render-litm.test.ts` + `packages/autoconfigure/test/knowledge-enricher*.test.ts` (weak match ŌåÆ no Related line) ŌĆö research-applied slice. HONEST scope: live-calibrated on nomic-embed (relevant ~0.61 vs personal distractors ~0.44ŌĆō0.51 ŌåÆ `confidentAt` 0.55), but nomic's cosine space is compressed (unrelated encyclopedic text can score ~0.54), so this is a BEST-EFFORT low-confidence flag for personal corpora, not a hard relevant/irrelevant separator (same honesty class as the P24-2 MMR nudge). No web fallback (deferred); deterministic, no new dep, no extra round

- [Autonomy] Muse runs REINFORCEMENT LEARNING over its learned-strategy playbook (model is fixed ŌåÆ RL on the MEMORY, not the weights): each strategy carries a clamped `reward` that reward-weighted `rankPlaybookStrategies` blends into selection, so a proven strategy surfaces first and one that keeps getting corrected DECAYS out of the injected top-K; the signal is AUTOMATIC ŌĆö at session end the strategy a correction implicates (most similar to the corrected request) is docked via `adjustPlaybookReward`, alongside ReasoningBank distillation of the new lesson. - [Autonomy] The RL reward signal is now BIDIRECTIONAL ŌĆö an explicit user APPROVAL reinforces the strategy that applied, the mirror of correction-driven decay, so the playbook learns from both "you got it right" and "you got it wrong" (not just absence-of-negative). `detectApprovals` (agent-core) is a precision-first EN+KO detector mirroring `detectCorrections` (fires on "perfect"/"exactly right"/"nailed it"/"ņÖäļ▓ĮĒĢ┤"/"ļö▒ ņóŗņĢä"/"ļ░öļĪ£ ĻĘĖĻ▒░ņĢ╝" ŌĆö NOT bare "ok"/"thanks"/"ņóŗņĢä"/"Ļ│Āļ¦łņøī", which acknowledge but don't endorse); at session end `distillSessionCorrections` credit-assigns each approval to the existing strategy most similar to its request and REINFORCES it (+1, `adjustPlaybookReward`), once per strategy (never both decayed and reinforced in one session), alongside correction-decay + distillation. `muse playbook distill` now reports both Ōåæ reinforced and Ōåō decayed ŌĆö `packages/agent-core/test/correction-distiller.test.ts` (detectApprovals: 13 EN+KO endorsements fire, 9 bare-acknowledgement phrases do NOT, assistantŌåÆuser pairing + request backfill + maxExchanges cap) + `apps/cli/src/chat-distill-corrections.test.ts` (an approval session with no correction lifts the applied strategy to +1, unrelated untouched, status still "skipped"-for-distillation). agent-core 1068 / cli 1548 tests pass + `pnpm lint` 0/0 ŌĆö P33-2 RL slice (bidirectional reward from explicit feedback)
- [Autonomy] LEARNED AVOIDANCE closes the RL extinction loop ŌĆö a strategy corrected into the floor (reward Ōēż `PLAYBOOK_AVOID_BELOW` = ŌłÆ4, ~4 implicating corrections) is EXCLUDED from injection ENTIRELY, not merely deranked: `rankPlaybookStrategies` filters it out before selection even when the bank is Ōēż topK (where ranking otherwise returns everything, so a deeply-negative strategy would still slip into a small bank). Soft + reversible (the veto-store parallel): it stays in the bank, shows in `muse playbook` as "┬Ę avoided (not injected)", and a later approval can lift its reward back above the line. `isAvoidedStrategy` is the shared predicate ŌĆö `packages/agent-core/test/playbook.test.ts` (an avoided strategy is dropped even at bank Ōēż topK; reward ŌłÆ3 still injects ranked last; all-avoided ŌåÆ empty; `isAvoidedStrategy` boundary incl. absent=not-avoided). - [Knowledge/Edge] `muse ask` no longer FALSE-REFUSES a question its corpus answers when the answer note's embedding cosine ranks below near-misses ŌĆö the headline chat-only recall path is now HYBRID (embedding-cosine + lexical keyword RRF), the same fusion the `knowledge_search` agent path already used (P23, RRF: Cormack et al. SIGIR 2009), but it was never applied to the headline `muse ask` path, which ranked notes by PURE cosine. On nomic's compressed embedding space a query with strong distinctive terms ("WireGuard", "MTU") ranked the one answer-bearing note ~5th, so the default top-3 excluded it and Muse honestly-but-WRONGLY said "I'm not sure" ŌĆö the "GUARD THE EDGE" failure mode (a false refusal turns honest into useless). `diversifyAskChunks` gains an optional `query`: when present it fuses the cosine rank with a lexical-overlap rank (reusing agent-core's now-exported `lexicalTokens`/`lexicalOverlap`/`fuseByReciprocalRank`) via RRF, normalises the fused relevance to [0,1] so MMR's diversity term stays comparable, and selects the top-K from that ŌĆö WITHOUT re-embedding (index embeddings reused) and KEEPING each chunk's absolute cosine `score` so the CRAG confidence framing is unchanged; a stopword-only query falls back to the prior cosine MMR ŌĆö `apps/cli/src/commands-ask-mmr.test.ts` (hybrid: a keyword-matching answer note that pure-cosine top-3 EXCLUDES is rescued into the top-3; the rescued chunk keeps its absolute cosine 0.50; a stopword-only query is byte-identical to cosine selection). - [Self-learning] Learned strategies now FADE when you stop reinforcing them (B1 Slice 2, continuous RL disuse-decay) ŌĆö a one-off thumbs-up no longer steers Muse forever. A positive-reward strategy left unreinforced past 30 days loses reward toward NEUTRAL 0 on the idle daemon (clamped at 0 ŌĆö disuse fades trust, never punishes; only a real correction drives a strategy negative), so it sinks out of the injected `[Learned Strategies]` block on its own; `muse learned` shows "Ōåō fading (last reinforced Nd ago)" a few days BEFORE the reward drops so the user SEES trust ebbing. `adjustPlaybookReward` stamps `lastReinforcedAt` on a positive reinforce only (a penalty/decay never refreshes it); new `decayStalePlaybookRewards` (mcp) runs as an idle RL phase in `consolidate-tick` behind ALL the brakes (cheap + local, no LLM), wired in `tick-daemons`. Proof: unit tests in `packages/mcp/test/playbook-store.test.ts` (decays one step toward 0; clamps at neutral; fresh/neutral/negative/probation untouched; createdAt fallback; lastReinforcedAt stamped on reinforce not penalty), `apps/api/src/consolidate-tick.test.ts` (decay phase fires only when idle/unbraked), `apps/cli/src/commands-learned.test.ts` (Ōåō fading render past the window) + a LIVE end-to-end run on this box (HOME-isolated mock playbook, never real ~/.muse): a stale +2 strategy decayed +2ŌåÆ+1ŌåÆ0 across idle ticks while a fresh +3 stayed, a 2nd tick at 0 decayed nothing (clamp proven), and the faded one LEFT `muse learned`'s Trusted list. mcp 1222 / api 816 / cli 1615 tests + `pnpm lint` 0/0 ŌĆö the grows-with-you loop now self-corrects in BOTH directions (learns AND forgets stale trust) ŌĆö P36-11 bullet
- [Self-learning] A reinforced strategy is no longer forgotten just for being old (B1 Slice 3 ŌĆö reward-/recency-weighted eviction). When the learned-strategy playbook overflows its 100-entry cap, eviction was blind FIFO (drop the oldest regardless of value), so a strategy you reinforced repeatedly could be evicted while a never-used newer one survived. New `retainPlaybookEntries` (mcp) keeps the highest-value entries instead ŌĆö value = reward, then recency: a high-reward OLD strategy beats a low-reward NEW one, reward ties break toward the newer, negative/avoided entries are evicted first, and survivors keep their original insertion order (the recency proxy `rankPlaybookStrategies` relies on). `recordPlaybookStrategy` now caps via this helper instead of `.slice(-MAX)`. Proof: unit tests in `packages/mcp/test/playbook-store.test.ts` (at/under cap returned unchanged; high-reward-old kept over low-reward-new with order preserved; reward-tieŌåÆrecency; avoided evicted before neutral/positive; record-path overflow of 120 neutral fillers keeps a +5 champion) + a LIVE end-to-end run on this box (HOME-isolated mock playbook, never real ~/.muse): a `+5` champion recorded FIRST then buried under 120 newer neutral records survived the cap and `muse playbook list` shows `[champion] Ō¤©reward +5Ō¤®` still present, total capped at 100 (blind FIFO would have dropped it as oldest). mcp 1227 tests + `pnpm lint` 0/0 ŌĆö the bank now keeps what you've proven matters, not merely what's newest ŌĆö P36-12 bullet
- [Self-learning] `muse learned` now shows the WHY behind each learned strategy (B1 Slice 4 ŌĆö provenance + legibility). A strategy used to be just a sentence; now each carries its ORIGIN (`grounded` = distilled from a real correction, `reflected` = synthetic, `manual` = you typed it) and the `source` correction that taught it, so `muse learned` prints "Ōå│ learned from your correction: '<the exact thing you said>'" under both trusted and probation strategies ŌĆö the legibility precondition to trusting unattended learning (you can judge whether to keep what Muse learned). PlaybookEntry/PlaybookStrategy gain `origin`/`source`; both correction-distill writers (idle daemon `distill-queue.ts` + chat-exit `chat-distill-corrections.ts`) stamp `origin: "grounded"` + the correction; `renderLearnedDigest` renders the why line; and a small ranking tie-break (`REFLECTED_RANK_PENALTY`, far below a reward step or relevance point) makes a `reflected` strategy never outrank an otherwise-equal `grounded` one ŌĆö evidence beats synthesis at a dead heat. Proof: unit tests in `packages/mcp/test/playbook-store.test.ts` (origin/source round-trip + non-string-drops), `packages/agent-core/test/playbook.test.ts` (grounded outranks equal reflected; penalty is tie-break-only, a more-relevant reflected still wins), `apps/cli/src/commands-learned.test.ts` (why line for grounded incl. probation; reflected flagged synthetic; long source truncated; legacy/manual gets no line) + a LIVE full chain on qwen3:8b (HOME-isolated, never real ~/.muse): enqueue "no, that is not what I meant ŌĆö give me bullet points, not prose" ŌåÆ idle `distillQueuedCorrections` ŌåÆ `muse learned` printed the probation strategy WITH "Ōå│ learned from your correction: '<that correction>'". agent-core 1238 / mcp 1229 / api 817 / cli 1618 tests + `pnpm lint` 0/0 ŌĆö the user can now SEE why Muse believes each learned thing ŌĆö P36-13 bullet
- [Self-learning] `muse playbook undo <id>` now makes Muse forget a learned strategy AND not re-learn it (B1 Slice 5 ŌĆö undo that TEACHES; `--pause` deferred). Plain `remove` only deletes a strategy, so the idle distiller re-learns the same lesson the next time the user gives a similar correction. `undo` removes the strategy AND records a suppressed-lesson veto keyed on its SOURCE correction (the provenance captured by P36-13), so the idle daemon distiller skips that signal BEFORE the LLM call and bumps the veto's blocked counter. Keying on the stable correction signal (not the LLM's run-to-run paraphrase of the strategy) is what makes the suppression actually stick ŌĆö a flaw the live test caught and drove the redesign. - [Recall/Edge] `muse ask` now omits empty grounding sections from the prompt ŌĆö tighter context for the small model + fewer spurious citations (edge hardening). With ~10 grounding sources injected, every turn previously carried an empty "(no pending reminders)" / "(no matching contacts)" block for each source the user had nothing in, which both bloated qwen3:8b's context (worsening lost-in-the-middle) and invited it to parrot a spurious "[reminder: none]"-style citation (the gate strips it, but it still flashes on the streaming path). - [Honesty/Agent] `muse ask` never falsely claims to act ŌĆö even in a MIXED question+action request (P39-8). P39-6 short-circuits a PURE imperative ("remind me to ŌĆ”"), but a MIXED request that OPENS with a question ŌĆö "what is my rent and remind me to pay it tomorrow" ŌĆö flowed through the normal path: Muse answered the rent (correctly cited) and then tacked on "I will remind you to pay it tomorrow", a false promise on the no-tools path (and fabricated a `[reminder: ŌĆ”]` citation the gate stripped). A new `answerPromisesAction` (agent-core) detects the false promise in the ANSWER itself (not the query, so it catches mixed/compound requests the start-anchored classifyActionRequest misses): it matches an action-TOOL claim ŌĆö "I'll remind you / set a reminder / add a task / event / schedule / book / email", "I've set/added/scheduled/booked/emailed" ŌĆö but NOT a conversational "I'll explain", a plain cited answer, or a recall "you have a reminder to pay rent". On the chat-only path, when it fires, Muse appends an honest correction: "(Heads up: I can't actually set reminders, tasks, or events on this path ŌĆö re-run with --with-tools to do that.)". The --with-tools path is untouched ŌĆö there the claim is TRUE (it really acted). Proof: detector unit tests in `packages/agent-core/test/casual-prompt.test.ts` (six action-claim forms incl. mixed ŌåÆ true; cited answer / "I'll explain" / "I'm not sure" / "you have a reminder" ŌåÆ false) + a LIVE `muse ask "what is my rent and remind me to pay it tomorrow"` ŌåÆ "Your rent is 1,250,000 KRW [from lease.md]" then "(Heads up: I can't actually set reminders ŌĆ” re-run with --with-tools)". agent-core 1357 / cli 1710 + `pnpm lint` 0/0 ŌĆö Muse's "I'll do X" is now always true or always corrected, never a bare false promise ŌĆö P39-8 bullet

Probing ņ¦äņĢł's core "knows you" flow: `muse remember "ļé┤ ņ░© ļ▓łĒśĖĒīÉņØĆ 12Ļ░Ć 3456ņØ┤ņĢ╝"` stored fact.car_license_plate = "12Ļ░Ć 3456" fine, but `muse ask "ļé┤ ņ░© ļ▓łĒśĖĒīÉ ļŁÉņĢ╝?"` answered correctly ("ļŗ╣ņŗĀņØś ņ░© ļ▓łĒśĖĒīÉņØĆ 12Ļ░Ć 3456ņØ┤ņŚÉņÜö") yet cited it `[from car_license_plate]` ŌĆö the NOTE citation verb with the memory KEY ŌĆö which the exact-match note gate then false-stripped with a "Removed 1 citation ŌĆ” treat those claims as unverified" warning on a TRUE recalled fact. - [Grounding edge/Perception] A Korean task / reminder / event recall now keeps its citation instead of being false-stripped ŌĆö the lexical citation gate tokenizes Unicode, and a coverage-only miss is routed to the judge, not hard-failed (P38-18). Probing ņ¦äņĢł's real Korean actuationŌåÆrecall loop: `muse remind add "ļé┤ņØ╝ ņśżĒøä 3ņŗ£" "ņ╣śĻ│╝ ņśłņĢĮ Ļ░ĆĻĖ░"` + `muse tasks add "ļČäĻĖ░ ļ│┤Ļ│Āņä£ ņ×æņä▒ĒĢśĻĖ░"` both stored fine, but `muse ask "ļé┤Ļ░Ć ĒĢ┤ņĢ╝ ĒĢĀ ņØ╝ņØ┤ ļŁÉĻ░Ć ņ×łņ¢┤?"` answered correctly and cited `[task: ļČäĻĖ░ ļ│┤Ļ│Āņä£ ņ×æņä▒ĒĢśĻĖ░]` / `[reminder: ņ╣śĻ│╝ ņśłņĢĮ Ļ░ĆĻĖ░]` (the EXACT Korean titles) ŌĆö yet the citation gate STRIPPED both ("Removed 2 citations") and the rubric verdict false-flagged the answer. Root cause: `lexicalTokens` ŌĆö the token-overlap basis that `resolvesByOverlap` uses to validate the non-note citation classes (tasks / reminders / events / sessions / contacts / commands / commits / memories / actions) ŌĆö split on `/[^a-z0-9]+/` (ASCII only), so "ļČäĻĖ░ ļ│┤Ļ│Āņä£ ņ×æņä▒ĒĢśĻĖ░" tokenized to `[]` (empty) ŌåÆ zero overlap with the Korean title ŌåÆ a perfectly valid Korean citation looked unresolvable and was dropped. Two coordinated fixes in packages/agent-core/src/knowledge-recall.ts: (1) `lexicalTokens` now splits on Unicode `/[^\p{L}\p{N}]+/u` and KEEPS single-character CJK tokens (a 1-char Hanja/Hangul/Kana carries meaning) while still dropping 1-char Latin ŌĆö ASCII English tokenization is byte-for-byte unchanged (so no English regression); (2) because Unicode coverage of a CORRECT cross-lingual answer (Korean prose over English evidence) can legitimately dip below the coverage floor, `verifyGroundingWithReverify` now ESCALATES a confident, validly-cited coverage-only failure to the re-verification judge instead of hard-failing it ŌĆö the judge stays in the loop, so a WRONG cross-lingual value is still rejected, and a judge error fail-closes to ungrounded. Proof: 6 new agent-core unit tests (lexicalTokens tokenizes "ļČäĻĖ░ ļ│┤Ļ│Āņä£ ņ×æņä▒ĒĢśĻĖ░" ŌåÆ {ļČäĻĖ░, ļ│┤Ļ│Āņä£, ņ×æņä▒ĒĢśĻĖ░}, keeps single-char CJK "ņ░©"/"ļ▓łĒśĖĒīÉ" but drops 1-char Latin x/y; the coverage-escalation upholds a correct cross-lingual answer to GROUNDED, keeps a wrong value UNGROUNDED when the judge rejects, fail-closes on a judge error, and does NOT escalate a coverage miss whose citation is INVALID) + the verify-claim-grounding battery still 6/6 on two consecutive runs (the cross-lingual correct/wrong cases route through the new branch) + LIVE on qwen3:8b: the Korean task/reminder recall above is now clean (no "Removed citation", no "treat as unverified"); the cross-lingual WiFi recall (P38-16) is unregressed; and a Korean absent-fact "ļé┤ ņŚ¼ĻČī ļ▓łĒśĖ ļŁÉņĢ╝?" still refuses ("ņĀĢļ│┤ņŚÉļŖö ņŚ¼ĻČī ļ▓łĒśĖņŚÉ ļīĆĒĢ£ ļé┤ņÜ®ņØ┤ ņŚåņŖĄļŗłļŗż") with no fabrication. agent-core 112 files / 1383 tests + cli 165 files / 1755 tests + cited-recall 6/6 + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a Korean-speaking user (or anyone whose tasks, reminders, and events are titled in their own language) now sees those recalls cited and un-warned instead of false-stripped as fabrications ŌĆö P38-18 bullet
- [Grounding edge] The grounding DRIFT verdict now runs under `muse ask --with-tools` too ŌĆö the agent (tool-using) recall path gets the same "treat as unverified" protection as chat-only, closing the one surface where "shows its work" was silent (P38-19). The recall edge's post-hoc rubric verdict (`groundingVerdictNotice` + the weak-band MaTTS reverify judge + the `--repair` offer) was gated `!options.withTools`, so a `muse ask --with-tools` answer that DRIFTED (asserted a value present in no source) printed confidently with NO grounding signal ŌĆö fabrication=0's "one deterministic grounding gate under EVERY surface" promise was literally false for the agent recall path. It had been skipped for a real reason: the verdict scores the answer against the CLI's pre-retrieval top-K notes (`scored`), but the `--with-tools` agent can pull a chunk via `knowledge_search` (often on a REFORMULATED query) that the top-K didn't include ŌĆö so scoring against `scored` alone would false-flag a legitimately grounded agent answer "treat as unverified". Fixed in apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts: the verdict guard drops from `!options.json && !options.withTools` to `!options.json` (so it runs on both paths), and a new pure, exported `augmentNoteEvidenceWithCited(baseNotes, citedSources, liveNotes)` augments the verdict's note evidence with the FULL text of every note the answer ACTUALLY cites (each already gate-validated against the live corpus by the citation gate above) ŌĆö so a note the agent retrieved outside the top-K is always covered. The augmentation is ADDITIVE ONLY: it can only prevent a false "ungrounded", never cause a false "grounded" ŌĆö a drifted value that appears in no cited note still scores uncovered ŌåÆ ungrounded. Proof: 6 new unit tests in apps/cli/src/commands-ask-verdict-withtools.test.ts (pulls in a cited note's full chunks when the top-K missed it; ignores a note the answer never cited; never duplicates a chunk already in the base set; is a no-op when nothing or an invalid/stale source is cited; the additive-only invariant ŌĆö base evidence is never dropped or rewritten) + the existing verdict-source / grounding-verdict tests green + LIVE on qwen3:8b: a `muse ask --with-tools` answer asserting "WireGuard default MTU is 1420 [from net.md]" against a note that never states an MTU now fires "ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ Grounding check: this answer's claims aren't fully backed by your notes (low coverage rejected by re-verification) ŌĆö treat as unverified" + the `--repair` nudge (it was SILENT before this change); two grounded `--with-tools` answers (garage door code 4417, home wifi password) do NOT false-flag; and the chat-only path is byte-for-byte unchanged (only the `options.withTools && index` branch is new). cli 166 files / 1761 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a user who runs `muse ask --with-tools` for a recall question now gets the same honest drift warning (and constructive --repair) as the plain ask, so the agent path can no longer present a fabricated value as a confident sourced fact ŌĆö P38-19 bullet
- [Grounding edge/Perception] `muse ask` no longer auto-saves the model's own answer as a durable "fact you told me" ŌĆö closing a provenance fabrication on the memory surface (P38-20). DISCOVERED live in P38-19's iteration and confirmed here: a `muse ask --with-tools` general-knowledge answer ("WireGuard default MTU is 1420") was silently persisted to `~/.muse/user-memory.json` as `wireguard_default_mtu: "1420"`, and the NEXT recall cited it `[memory: wireguard_default_mtu]` with the receipt "­¤¦Ā from what you told me" ŌĆö i.e. Muse asserting the USER had stated a fact the MODEL fabricated from general knowledge. Root cause: the shared user-memory auto-extract HOOK (`createUserMemoryAutoExtractHook.afterComplete`) mines the ASSISTANT output (not just the user's statements), and it was installed globally so it ran on EVERY agent run including one-shot `muse ask` recall ŌĆö so a question-answer turn distilled the model's own assertion as a user fact (a second, latent vector also existed: the `remember_fact` write tool was exposed on the recall agent). Fixed by making recall read-only for durable memory: in apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts the `--with-tools` agent run now sets `metadata.skipUserMemoryAutoExtract: true` (a new per-run opt-out the hook honors via a new exported `readSkipAutoExtract(context)` in packages/memory/src/memory-auto-extract.ts ŌĆö early-returns before any extraction) AND `metadata.forbiddenToolNames: ["remember_fact"]` (defense in depth, via the existing exposure-layer block). Durable memory authoring stays with the explicit `muse remember` command (user-directed) and the conversational chat surface, whose auto-extraction is unchanged. Proof: 3 new memory unit tests in packages/memory/test/auto-extract-skip.test.ts (readSkipAutoExtract is true only when the flag is explicitly set; the hook writes NOTHING on an opted-out recall turn even when the extractor stub returns a fact-bearing payload; a normal/chat turn STILL extracts the fact ŌĆö so the skip is the ONLY behavior change, no chat regression) + LIVE on qwen3:8b: the exact `muse ask --with-tools` WireGuard probe that wrote `wireguard_default_mtu` before now leaves NO memory file across two runs, while P38-19's drift verdict still fires ("treat as unverified"). memory 30 files / 312 tests + autoconfigure 73 files / 484 tests + cli 166 files / 1761 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a user who asks Muse a question can no longer have its general-knowledge answer silently turned into a fabricated "fact about you" that later recall presents as your own words ŌĆö P38-20 bullet
- [Grounding edge/Perception] Chat auto-memory no longer stores a fact the MODEL asserted as "what you told me" ŌĆö the provenance gate now covers the conversational surface (P38-21). P38-20 closed this on one-shot `muse ask` (by skipping extraction), and flagged the residual: the SAME leak lives on `muse chat`, through a SEPARATE extractor (`extractMemoryFromTurn` in apps/cli/src/chat-auto-memory.ts) that also mines the assistant reply ŌĆö so a user who ASKS "what's WireGuard's default MTU?" and gets "1420" would have `wireguard_default_mtu: 1420` silently saved as their OWN fact, which a later recall cites "­¤¦Ā from what you told me" (a fabricated provenance the user never stated). Fixed with a deterministic provenance gate (the same code-not-prompt shape as the citation gate): a new pure, exported `dropModelAssertedValues(record, userTurn, assistantOutput)` in packages/memory/src/memory-auto-extract.ts drops a fact/preference iff ALL of its DISTINCTIVE value tokens appear in the assistant's reply and NONE appear in the user's own turn ŌĆö i.e. the value was demonstrably the model's assertion, not the user's words. A value the user actually stated (its token is in their turn) survives; an inferred boolean like `allergy_penicillin: yes` survives because "yes" carries no distinctive token (fail-open ŌĆö un-attributable values are kept, not dropped); a malformed array-shaped payload is left untouched for the existing sanitizer. Applied in BOTH auto-extraction paths ŌĆö the chat `extractMemoryFromTurn` and the agent-runtime auto-extract hook (`createUserMemoryAutoExtractHook.afterComplete`). - [Perception/Grounding edge] `muse ask --file` refuses a BINARY file instead of hallucinating content from its garbled bytes (P37-14). Probing the ad-hoc `--file` perception source with a real-shaped binary PDF: `muse ask --file resume.pdf "what is this person's job title?"` read the PDF's raw bytes as UTF-8 (the handler did `readFile(path, "utf8")`), injected the garbage as note-class grounding, and the local model HALLUCINATED a confident answer ŌĆö "The resume file mentions 'Senior Software Engineer' [from resume.pdf]" ŌĆö citing a value that appears NOWHERE in the file (it was pure binary stream bytes). A sourced fabrication on the perception surface, exactly what the "shows its work" edge forbids. Fixed in apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts: a new pure, exported `looksLikeBinaryContent(bytes)` (deterministic, zero deps ŌĆö a NUL byte is the canonical text-vs-binary signal; failing that, a >10% U+FFFD replacement-char ratio from a lossy UTF-8 decode of the first 8 KB) classifies the `--file` payload BEFORE it is grounded. A binary file is NOT injected as evidence; instead the user gets a clear "--file <path> looks like a binary file (PDF, image, office doc, ŌĆ”), not text ŌĆö I won't ground on it ŌĆ” extract the text first" message, and the answer honestly refuses rather than fabricating. A real text file is unaffected and still grounds + cites normally. Proof: 6 new unit tests in apps/cli/src/commands-ask-file.test.ts (a NUL byte, a PDF magic header + stream bytes, and an invalid-UTF-8 run all classify as binary; ASCII, valid UTF-8 Korean+emoji, and an empty file classify as text) + LIVE on qwen3:8b: the identical binary-PDF probe now prints the refusal message and answers "I don't have enough information to determine this person's job title" (the fabricated "Senior Software Engineer" is GONE), while `muse ask --file resume.txt` still cites `[from resume.txt]` with the real value. cli 166 files / 1767 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a user who points `--file` at a PDF/image/doc now gets an honest "I can't read that as text" instead of a confidently fabricated answer attributed to their file ŌĆö P37-14 bullet
- [Perception/Knowledge] `muse ask --file <pdf>` now READS the PDF and answers from its real text ŌĆö a user can ask Muse about a PDF directly, grounded + cited (P37-15). P37-14 made a binary `--file` refuse rather than hallucinate; this upgrades the most common "binary" case ŌĆö a PDF ŌĆö into a real capability. The `--file` handler now detects a PDF (`isPdfDocument`: a `.pdf` extension OR the `%PDF-` magic header) and extracts its text via `pdf-parse` (the SAME MIT, pure-JS reader `muse read` already ships ŌĆö no new dependency, and it's dynamically imported so it loads only when a PDF is actually read), then grounds + cites it `[from <file>.pdf]` like any note. A non-PDF binary (image, archive, office doc) still hits the P37-14 binary refusal; a scanned/empty-text PDF or a malformed PDF refuses honestly (no fabrication from garbage bytes); a plain text/markdown file is unchanged. To avoid an import cycle (`commands-read.ts` already imports `consumeAskStream` from `commands-ask.ts`), the shared document extractor was moved to a new leaf module `apps/cli/src/document-reader.ts` (`parsePdfBuffer` / `isPdfDocument` / `isLikelyBinary` / `extractDocumentText` / `PdfParsed`) and re-exported from `commands-read.ts` so its existing consumers (notes-rag, watch-folder, their tests) are untouched. Proof: a new `apps/cli/src/document-reader.test.ts` with 6 tests INCLUDING a real `pdf-parse` extraction of a generated valid single-page PDF (genuine PDF-parsing coverage the old tests lacked ŌĆö they only checked the magic-byte/binary helpers), plus the existing commands-read / notes-rag / watch-folder suites still green (the extraction move is behaviour-preserving) + LIVE on qwen3:8b: `muse ask --file resume.pdf "what is this person's job title?"` ŌåÆ "The person's job title is Staff Data Scientist at Acme Corp [from resume.pdf]" (extracted straight from the PDF's text layer), an off-topic "what is their phone number?" honestly refuses ("does not include any information about a phone number"), and the regression cases all hold (malformed PDF ŌåÆ "could not be read as a PDF", a PNG ŌåÆ binary refusal, a `.txt` ŌåÆ grounds + cites). cli 167 files / 1773 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a user can now point `muse ask --file` at a PDF (a resume, a lease, a contract) and get a cited answer from its actual contents instead of a refusal ŌĆö P37-15 bullet
- [Actuation] `muse remind`/`tasks`/`calendar` now understand colloquial Korean times ŌĆö ņĢäņ╣© (morning) / ņĀĆļģü (evening) / ļ░ż (night) / ņāłļ▓Į (dawn), not just the formal ņśżņĀä/ņśżĒøä (P40-8). - [Felt] The "empty notes" first-run on-ramp no longer contradicts itself for a user who has OTHER personal data (P35-9). - [Actuation] `muse remind`/`tasks`/`calendar` understand an English day-part word + a specific hour ŌĆö "tonight at 8", "tomorrow morning at 9", "this evening at 7" (P40-9). The English counterpart of P40-8 (which fixed the Korean ņĢäņ╣©/ņĀĆļģü/ļ░ż): a colloquial day-part word combined with an explicit hour was REJECTED. `muse remind add "tonight at 8"`, `"this evening at 7"`, `"tomorrow morning at 9"`, `"tomorrow evening at 6"`, `"tomorrow night at 10"`, and `"this morning at 8"` ALL failed with "dueAt must be an ISO-8601 timestamp or a supported relative phrase" ŌĆö everyday phrasings rejected ŌĆö even though the bare `"tomorrow morning"` resolved to 09:00. Fixed with a new `dayPartBiasedTime(part, spec)` that lets the day-part word supply the AM/PM for a bare 1-12 hour (morning/this-morning ŌåÆ AM; afternoon/evening/night/tonight ŌåÆ PM), with the night edge handled (`tonight at 12` ŌåÆ 00:00 midnight, vs afternoon/evening at 12 ŌåÆ noon); it is wired through a new `standaloneDayPartTime` for the today-anchored forms ("this morning at 8" ŌåÆ 08:00, "tonight at 8" ŌåÆ 20:00) and a new day-part branch inside `parseTimeOfDay` for the day-headed forms ("tomorrow morning at 9", "monday evening at 6"). - [Perception/Knowledge] An HTML file is grounded on its readable TEXT (tags + script/style stripped, entities decoded), not raw tag-soup ŌĆö so `muse ask --file resume.html` / `muse read article.html` / `--file <folder-of-html>` work on HTML the way they do on text and PDFs (P37-17). Probing `--file` with an `.html` file exposed a real correctness defect: `muse ask --file resume.html "what is the email address?"` returned "jane&#64;globex.com" ŌĆö the HTML numeric entity `&#64;` (which is `@`) was never decoded, so the user got a MANGLED email ŌĆö and the ­¤ōÄ receipt showed raw `<html><head><style>ŌĆ”</style><script>ŌĆ”</script>` markup as the "source" (noisy, and it wastes the small model's context on tags/scripts). Root cause: every non-PDF `--file`/ingest path read the file bytes as UTF-8 verbatim, markup and all ŌĆö qwen coped with simple cases but the entities stayed mangled and large pages would bury the real content under markup. Fixed in apps/cli/src/document-reader.ts with a new pure, exported `htmlToText(html)` (regex-based, no DOM/parser dependency): it removes `<script>`/`<style>` blocks and HTML comments, strips the remaining tags, decodes the entities that actually corrupt grounded values (numeric `&#64;`, hex `&#x26;`, and the common named ones ŌĆö `&amp;`/`&lt;`/`&gt;`/`&quot;`/`&nbsp;`/`&mdash;`ŌĆ”), and collapses whitespace. `extractDocumentText` now routes `.html`/`.htm` through it, `.html`/`.htm` were added to `SUPPORTED_DOC_EXT` (so the directory walk for `muse read <dir>` / `muse ask --file <dir>` / `watch-folder --ingest` picks them up), and the single-`--file` path in commands-ask got the same branch (it has its own inline reader, applied AFTER the robust binary-refusal so a non-text binary is still refused). Proof: 4 new unit tests in apps/cli/src/document-reader.test.ts (`isHtmlDocument` matches .html/.htm not .txt; tags + `<script>`/`<style>` bodies stripped and whitespace collapsed; numeric/hex/named entities decoded ŌĆö `jane&#64;globex.com` ŌåÆ `jane@globex.com`, `a&#x26;b` ŌåÆ `a&b`, `Globex &amp; Co &mdash; 2026` ŌåÆ `Globex & Co ŌĆö 2026`; `extractDocumentText` reads an `.html` buffer as decoded text with no `<`) + the existing document-reader / read / notes-rag suites green + LIVE on qwen3:8b: `muse ask --file resume.html "what is the email address?"` now ŌåÆ "jane@globex.com" with a CLEAN text receipt ("Jane Doe Email: jane@globex.com Job title: Principal Engineer at Globex & Co."), `muse read article.html --save-to-notes` saves "VPN Setup The MTU should be set to 1380 for WireGuard." (clean, no tags), and `muse ask --file <dir>` over a folder containing the HTML grounds on it and cites `[from article.html]`. cli 167 files / 1782 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a user can now point Muse at an HTML file or a folder of them (a saved web article, an exported resume) and get a cited answer from its actual readable text with values intact, instead of a markup-polluted, entity-mangled one ŌĆö P37-17 bullet
- [Grounding edge/Perception] A `[from <class>: ŌĆ”]` structured citation (commit / task / event / reminder / ŌĆ”) is no longer false-stripped ŌĆö the model's "from "-prefixed citation now survives the gate (P38-23). Probing the git-perception source (P37-11): `muse ask --git "what have I been working on recently?"` grounded on the user's real commits and answered correctly, citing a commit as `[from commit: feat(perception): muse ask grounds on the action log ŌĆ”]` ŌĆö but the citation gate then STRIPPED it with "ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ Removed 1 citation(s) to source(s) you don't have (commit: ŌĆ”) ŌĆö treat those claims as unverified" on a TRUE recall, making a correct git answer look unverified. Root cause: the local model frequently prepends the NOTE verb "from " to a STRUCTURED citation, but `enforceAnswerCitations`'s class regexes anchor on `[commit:` / `[task:` / `[event:` (with no "from "), and the note regex `[from <X>]` runs FIRST and mis-catches `[from commit: ŌĆ”]` as a non-existent note, stripping it before the commit handler ever sees it. Same defect class as P38-22 (contacts) and P38-17 (memory), now generalised across every structured citation class. Fixed with a new pure, exported `normalizeFromPrefixedCitations(answer)` in packages/agent-core/src/knowledge-recall.ts that drops the redundant "from " before any known class keyword ŌĆö task / event / reminder / session / feed / contact / command / commit / memory / action ŌĆö rewriting `[from commit: X]` ŌåÆ `[commit: X]` etc.; it is applied in apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts BEFORE the contact/memory normalizers (so they see the de-prefixed form) and a real `[from note.md]` (no class keyword + ":") is never touched. - [Perception/Reach] `muse ask --url <url>` ŌĆö a user can now ask Muse about a public WEB PAGE, grounded on its readable text and cited, without ingesting it (P37-18). This is a NEW capability (Reach growth), the web counterpart of `--file`: `muse ask --url https://example.com "what is this domain for?"` fetches the page, extracts its readable text, grounds the answer on it cited `[from <host>]`, and an off-topic question honestly refuses rather than inventing page content. It reuses the existing SSRF-guarded `fetchReadableUrl` helper from @muse/mcp (the same one `muse notes ingest --url` already uses) ŌĆö it permits PUBLIC hosts only, re-checks the host after any redirect (so a redirect can't smuggle in a private/internal address), enforces a 15s timeout, and extracts readable text from HTML ŌĆö so there is no new fetch or egress machinery and the local-first posture is unchanged (the MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY gate governs LLM/voice egress, not reading a public web page the user explicitly asked about, which `outbound-safety.md` permits as "Muse may read the world freely"). - [Actuation] A BARE duration ŌĆö "2 hours", "30 minutes", "3 days", "2h", "a week" ŌĆö now parses as an offset from now across `remind`/`tasks`/`calendar`/`snooze`; the literal "in" is optional (P40-10). Probing the actuators surfaced a broad gap: `muse remind snooze <id> --in "2 hours"`, `muse remind add "30 minutes" "call mom"`, and `muse tasks add "review" --due "3 days"` ALL failed with "dueAt must be an ISO-8601 timestamp or a supported relative phrase" ŌĆö every bare duration was rejected, and ONLY the form WITH the literal word "in" ("in 2 hours") parsed. This is especially awkward for `--in "2 hours"`, where the word "in" is already in the flag name so repeating it ("--in 'in 2 hours'") reads wrong, and "in 2 hours" is one of the most natural ways a person states a reminder time. Root cause: the two duration handlers in packages/mcp/src/loopback-relative-time.ts ŌĆö the full-word "in N <unit>" form and the compact "in Nh/Nm/Nd/Nw" form ŌĆö both hard-required a leading `in\s+`. Fixed by making that prefix optional (`(?:in\s+)?`) in both regexes, so a bare "2 hours" / "30 minutes" / "3 days" / "a week" / "2h" / "90 mins" / "2w" now reads as that offset from the current time. The change is purely additive ŌĆö a bare duration was previously unrecognised, so nothing that parsed before changes ŌĆö and it preserves the existing disambiguation: a bare number with NO unit ("5") still means a 24-hour clock hour (today 05:00, not "5 of something"), and an unknown unit ("3 horses") still rejects, so there are no false positives. Proof: 4 new parser unit tests in packages/mcp/test/relative-time-period.test.ts (bare full-word durations 2 hours/30 minutes/3 days/a week and bare compact 2h/90m/2d/2w each equal their explicit "in ŌĆ”" form; "5" stays a clock hour; "3 horses" rejected) + the single mcp.test.ts assertion that had codified the OLD "a bare 1h is rejected" behavior updated to the new intended parse + the full @muse/mcp suite green (167 files / 1330 tests) + the cli remind/tasks suites green (38) + LIVE on the loop PC: `muse remind snooze <id> --in "2 hours"` ŌåÆ +2h, `muse remind add "30 minutes" t` ŌåÆ +30m, `muse tasks add "review" --due "3 days"` ŌåÆ +3 days, while "in 2 hours" and "5" (clock hour) are unregressed. mcp 167 files / 1330 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a user can now write a reminder/task time the way they actually say it ("remind me in 2 hours" ŌåÆ just "2 hours", or `--in "2 hours"`) instead of being forced to include the literal word "in" ŌĆö P40-10 bullet

- [Grounding edge/Perception] The feed and contact grounding markers now embed the canonical `[feed: ŌĆ”]` / `[contact: ŌĆ”]` citation, so the local model cites them correctly INLINE ŌĆö fixing the root cause that the P38-22 (contact) and P38-25 (feed) post-hoc normalizers had only patched on the buffered copy (P38-28). Tracing WHY the model kept citing feeds and contacts in non-canonical forms (`[feed 1]` by slot, `[from contact_<uuid>]` by raw id) revealed an inconsistency in how the grounding context is built: the task, event, reminder, memory, and commit markers each embed the exact canonical citation inside the marker (`<<event N ŌĆö provider>>\n<title>\n[event: <title>]\n<<end>>`), which the small local model then copies verbatim ŌĆö but the feed marker (`<<feed N ŌĆö name (date)>>\n<title>ŌĆ”`) and the contact marker (`<<contact N ŌĆö id>>\n<name> ŌĆö <fields>`) did NOT include the `[feed: ŌĆ”]` / `[contact: ŌĆ”]` line, so the model improvised a slot number or the raw id. Because the default `muse ask` (chat-only) path STREAMS the model's raw output token-by-token and only normalizes the BUFFERED copy afterward (for the gate + receipt), the user saw the ugly `[feed 1]` / `[from contact_<uuid>]` inline even though the receipts were correct ŌĆö the prior fixes never touched the streamed text. - [Proactivity/Felt] Muse now notices the most common way you voice a commitment in passing ŌĆö "I'll ŌĆ”" / "I will ŌĆ”" / "I'm going to ŌĆ”" / "I'm gonna ŌĆ”" ŌĆö not just "I need to / have to / should" (P35-11). The SF-confidant "anticipates what you said you'd do" quality runs on the deterministic rule engine `detectUserCommitments` in packages/agent-core/src/commitment-detector.ts, which both `muse commitments scan` and `muse checkins scan` use to read recent chat (`~/.muse/last-chat.jsonl`) for things the user said they'd do and offer to track them / schedule a check-in. Its rules caught "I need to ŌĆ”", "I have/got to ŌĆ”", "I should ŌĆ”", and the Korean ĒĢ┤ņĢ╝/ĒĢśĻĖ░ļĪ£ Ē¢ł forms ŌĆö but MISSED the single most common English way people state an intent: the future promise. A chat containing "I'll call the dentist tomorrow" or "I'm going to review the PR this afternoon" produced "No open commitments detected" ŌĆö Muse simply didn't see them. Fixed by adding two rules to the detector: `\bI(?:'ll|\s+will)\s+(ŌĆ”)` and `\bI(?:'m|\s+am)\s+(?:going\s+to|gonna)\s+(ŌĆ”)`, both mapped to a new `"will"` commitment kind at high confidence, with a small precision guard ŌĆö a `WILL_STATIVE_STARTERS` stoplist ({be, see, bet, say}) so a stative remark ("I'll be late", "I'll see", "I'll bet") is NOT mistaken for a task, and the existing interrogative filter still drops "Will I make it on time?" as a question. - [Proactivity/Actuation] A commitment's follow-up check-in now fires AFTER the timeframe you stated, instead of always tomorrow at 10:00 (P35-12). P35-11 made Muse NOTICE a commitment voiced in passing; this hardens the next stage ŌĆö the proactive follow-up that actually arrives in the user's channel. `muse checkins scan` reads recent chat for things the user said they'd do (via `detectUserCommitments`) and schedules a warm "how did it go?" nudge for each (delivered at its due time by `runDueCheckins`). This is exactly the real-world failure mode the human-directed focus calls a USER-FACING reliability defect (a proven-once actuator that misbehaves on a natural input), not inward churn. The follow-up timing is deterministic code (no model call ŌĆö the commitment detection is rule-only too), fail-safe (an unrecognised timeframe simply defaults to next-day, never drops the check-in). - [Grounding edge] The recall verdict's wrong-value escalation now catches a drifted EMAIL ADDRESS, not just a wrong number or named entity ŌĆö closing the most dangerous contact-data drift (P38-29). P38-2 made `verifyGroundingWithReverify` escalate a `grounded`-scoring answer that asserts a NUMBER ("MTU 9000" vs the note's 1380) or a capitalized NAMED ENTITY ("Dr. Lee" vs "Dr. Park") absent from the evidence to one fail-OPEN judge pass (claim-level grounding, since whole-answer coverage can't see a single wrong token). But an EMAIL ADDRESS escaped BOTH checks: the lexical tokenizer splits "jane@acme.com" into lowercase parts (jane/acme/com), so a drifted DOMAIN ("acme" where the note says "globex") is neither a pure digit nor a capitalized entity ŌĆö meaning a confident, high-coverage, fully-cited answer asserting a WRONG contact email read `grounded` and was handed to the user as fact (verified live: the wrong-email answer scores base verdict grounded at confidence 1.00 with NO gate). Scoped to emails (the clean, unambiguous, highest-value identifier; @handles/URLs deferred as noisier). - [Grounding edge] A source receipt's "open to verify" target is now REAL for an ad-hoc grounding source ŌĆö the actual page URL for a `--url` answer, and no fabricated path for a `--clipboard` answer (P38-31). Falsifying P38-30 surfaced the next integrity gap in the same flagship "shows its work" receipt: for an ad-hoc source (a fetched web page, the clipboard) the receipt's verify line was a FABRICATED local path. A `--url` answer's receipt pointed at `.muse/notes/example.com` and a `--clipboard` answer's at `.muse/notes/clipboard` ŌĆö neither file exists on disk (confirmed live: `ls` of the shown path returns "No such file or directory"), so the receipt's "(open to verify)" was a broken promise: it told the user to open a path that isn't there. Root cause: `formatSourceReceipts` computed the verify path as `join(notesDir, <cited-source-label>)` for any non-absolute source, blind to the fact that a URL host or the literal "clipboard" isn't a note under the notes directory. The fix can't key on `existsSync` (the existing unit tests legitimately assert path lines for synthetic paths that don't exist in the test sandbox), so the handler ŌĆö which KNOWS each source's type ŌĆö now records an `adHocVerifyTargets` map: the REAL `fetched.finalUrl` for a `--url` source (a link the user can actually open in a browser to verify the page the answer came from) and `null` for the ephemeral `--clipboard` source (nothing to open). `formatSourceReceipts` takes an optional `verifyTargets: ReadonlyMap<string, string | null>`: a present non-null value is rendered as the verify line (the URL), a present `null` renders the labelled snippet with NO path line, and an ABSENT entry ŌĆö every note and every `--file` ŌĆö falls through to the exact prior local-path logic (preferring the matched chunk's real absolute path), so notes and files are completely unchanged and no existing receipt test regresses. - [Actuation] A user can now set a reminder / task / event for a bare DAY-OF-MONTH ŌĆö "remind me on the 25th to pay rent", "add a task due the 15th", "rent is due the 1st" ŌĆö across `muse remind` / `tasks` / `calendar` / `snooze` (P40-11). Probing the natural-language date parser (`resolveRelativeTimePhrase` in packages/mcp/src/loopback-relative-time.ts) showed that "the 25th" / "on the 25th" / "the 1st" / "on the 15th at 3pm" ALL returned undefined and were rejected at the actuator with "dueAt must be an ISO-8601 timestamp or a supported relative phrase", even though "next monday" / "end of the month" / "in 2 weeks" worked ŌĆö yet a bare ordinal day-of-month is one of the most common ways people state a date ("rent is due on the 1st", "the meeting is the 15th"). The month-NAME date parser (`resolveAbsoluteMonthDate`) only handles "June 25" / "25 June"; a bare ordinal had no handler and fell through to undefined. Added a day-of-month handler: the regex `^(?:on\s+)?the\s+(\d{1,2})(?:st|nd|rd|th)(?:\s+(?:at\s+)?(.+))?$` resolves the phrase to the NEXT occurrence of that day-of-month ŌĆö this month if it hasn't passed yet (time-aware, so "the 25th at 9am" when 9am already passed today rolls to next month, never schedules in the past), otherwise next month; a day that doesn't exist in the current month (e.g. "the 31st" in a 30-day month) rolls onto the next month that has it via a getDate() guard; an impossible day ("the 99th" / "the 0th") is rejected outright rather than producing a silently rolled-over date; the time defaults to the same 9am bare-day hour every other date phrase uses, and an explicit "at 3pm" / "at 9am" is parsed via the shared `parseTimeOfDay`. The change is purely additive ŌĆö a bare ordinal was previously unrecognised, so nothing that parsed before changes (verified: "next monday" still lands on a Monday, "in 2 weeks" still +14 days, "next mango" still undefined). Proof: 6 new parser unit tests in packages/mcp/test/relative-time-period.test.ts (a still-ahead day ŌåÆ this month with getDate/getMonth/future assertions; a past day ŌåÆ next month; an explicit "at 3pm" ŌåÆ 15:00; the 9am default; "the 99th"/"the 0th" ŌåÆ undefined; and weekday/duration non-regression) + the full @muse/mcp suite green (167 files / 1338 tests, including mcp.test.ts's 357 ŌĆö the other consumer of the parser, unregressed) + LIVE round-trips on the loop PC: `muse remind add "on the 25th" "pay rent"` ŌåÆ "Added [rem_ŌĆ”] pay rent ŌĆö due 2026-06-25 09:00" and `muse tasks add "submit report" --due "the 15th"` ŌåÆ "due 2026-06-15 09:00", with `muse remind list` confirming the reminder landed at 2026-06-25 09:00 (both phrasings were REJECTED before this slice). mcp 167 files / 1338 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a user can now schedule against the way they actually say a monthly date ("on the 25th") instead of being forced to write a full ISO timestamp or name the month ŌĆö P40-11 bullet
- [Actuation] A user can now schedule against a MONTH-QUALIFIED date ŌĆö "remind me on the 15th of next month", "task due the 1st of next month", "file taxes by end of next month" ŌĆö across `muse remind` / `tasks` / `calendar` / `snooze` (P40-12). P40-11 taught the parser the bare "the 25th" (the next occurrence of that day-of-month), but the natural way to pin a SPECIFIC relative month ŌĆö "the 15th of next month", "the 1st of this month", "end of next month" ŌĆö still returned undefined and was rejected at the actuator with "dueAt must be ŌĆ” a supported relative phrase". Unlike a bare day, this form has NO offset alternative: you cannot say "in N days" for "the 15th of next month" without knowing today's date and counting, so it is the higher-value half of the day-of-month story. Added two handlers in packages/mcp/src/loopback-relative-time.ts: (1) `^(?:on\s+)?the\s+(\d{1,2})(?:st|nd|rd|th)\s+of\s+(this|next)\s+month(?:\s+(?:at\s+)?(.+))?$` resolves the ordinal day within the named relative month (offset 0 for "this", +1 for "next"); it is placed BEFORE P40-11's bare "the Nth" handler because that handler's trailing `(.+)` time slot would otherwise greedily swallow "of next month", parse it as an invalid time, and fail the whole phrase ŌĆö ordering is load-bearing. An explicit month is honoured literally (so "the 1st of this month" returns this month's 1st even though it has passed ŌĆö the user named the month deliberately), and a getDate() guard rejects a day that doesn't exist in the target month (e.g. "the 31st of a 30-day month") rather than silently rolling it into the following month. (2) The existing "end of [the|this] month" handler was extended to also accept "next" (capturing the qualifier and applying a +1 month offset), so "end of next month" lands on the following month's last calendar day. Both default the time to the same 9am bare-day hour and honour an explicit "at 3pm". The change is purely additive ŌĆö these phrasings were previously unrecognised ŌĆö and the bare "the 25th", "end of the month", weekday, and duration phrases are all unregressed (verified). Proof: 6 new parser unit tests in packages/mcp/test/relative-time-period.test.ts (a next-month pin ŌåÆ July with getDate/getMonth assertions; a this-month literal even when past; an explicit "at 3pm" ŌåÆ 15:00; "end of next month" ŌåÆ July 31; "the 99th of next month" ŌåÆ undefined; and bare-day-of-month / "end of the month" non-regression) + the full @muse/mcp suite green (167 files / 1344 tests, including mcp.test.ts's 357 ŌĆö the parser's other consumer, unregressed) + LIVE round-trips on the loop PC (reference 2026-06-03): `muse remind add "the 15th of next month" "quarterly review"` ŌåÆ "Added [rem_ŌĆ”] quarterly review ŌĆö due 2026-07-15 09:00" and `muse tasks add "file taxes" --due "end of next month"` ŌåÆ "due 2026-07-31 09:00" (both REJECTED before this slice). mcp 167 files / 1344 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a user can now name the month a date falls in ("the 15th of next month", "end of next month"), the one common date phrasing that has no relative-offset shortcut ŌĆö P40-12 bullet
- [Proactivity/Felt] A user can now CANCEL a proactive check-in ŌĆö `muse checkins cancel <id>` ŌĆö so the daemon stops asking "how did it go?" about something already done or unwanted (P35-13). P35-11/12 taught Muse to notice a commitment the user voiced in passing and schedule a warm follow-up nudge (`muse checkins scan` ŌåÆ a due-windowed "Following up ŌĆö you mentioned you'd 'ŌĆ”'. How did it go?" the daemon later delivers). But there was NO way to SILENCE one: if you'd already called the dentist, or never wanted the nudge, the check-in would still fire ŌĆö and a proactive system you can't opt out of is a nag, not a confidant. The `"cancelled"` status already existed in `CheckinStatus` and was honoured by `runDueCheckins` (it fires only `status === "scheduled"`) and `scheduleCheckins` (a cancelled source doesn't block a future re-mention), but nothing could SET a check-in to cancelled from the CLI, and `muse checkins list` didn't even display the id you'd reference. Added a pure exported `cancelCheckin(checkins, idOrPrefix)` in packages/mcp/src/commitment-checkin.ts: it matches by exact id OR a UNIQUE id prefix (the convenience, since list now shows the full id), refuses an AMBIGUOUS prefix rather than cancelling the wrong check-in, and returns a structured reason (not-found / ambiguous / already-fired / already-cancelled) instead of silently pretending to succeed; on success it returns the updated list with that one check-in flipped to `cancelled`. Wired as `muse checkins cancel <id>` (reads the store, calls the helper, writes back only on a real change, with a clear success/explanatory message and a `--json` form), and `muse checkins list` now prints `  ŌĆó [<id>] <question> (<when>)` so the id is visible to cancel by. Because `runDueCheckins` already fires only scheduled check-ins, a cancelled one is deterministically excluded from delivery ŌĆö the daemon will not ask about it. Proof: 4 new unit tests in packages/mcp/test/commitment-checkin.test.ts (cancel by exact id flips only that one, leaving a sibling scheduled; cancel by a unique prefix resolves to the right id; an ambiguous prefix returns reason "ambiguous" with the match count and mutates nothing; not-found / already-fired / already-cancelled each report without mutating, and an empty needle is not-found) + the full @muse/mcp suite green (167 files / 1348 tests) + the full @muse/cli suite green (168 files / 1808 tests) + a LIVE end-to-end round-trip on the loop PC: seeding `~/.muse/last-chat.jsonl` with "I need to call the dentist" + "I have to renew my passport", `muse checkins scan` schedules both, `muse checkins list` shows each with its `[chk_ŌĆ”]` id, `muse checkins cancel <dentist-id>` prints "Cancelled check-in [chk_ŌĆ”] ŌĆö 'ŌĆ”' won't fire.", the scheduled list afterward shows ONLY the passport check-in (the dentist one is gone from scheduled), and `muse checkins cancel chk_nope` prints "No scheduled check-in matches 'chk_nope'. Run `muse checkins list` to see ids." mcp 167 files / 1348 tests + cli 168 files / 1808 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a user can now dismiss a proactive nudge for something they already handled instead of being asked about it, which is the opt-out that makes Muse's proactivity calm rather than naggy ŌĆö P35-13 bullet
- [Proactivity/Felt] A user can now SNOOZE a proactive check-in ŌĆö `muse checkins snooze <id> <when>` ŌĆö deferring "how did it go?" to a later time instead of only cancelling it (P35-14). P35-13 added cancel (silence a nudge forever); the natural complement is "ask me LATER, not now" ŌĆö a check-in for something you haven't gotten to yet shouldn't have to be killed, just pushed. Added a pure exported `snoozeCheckin(checkins, idOrPrefix, newDueAtIso)` in packages/mcp/src/commitment-checkin.ts that bumps the matched check-in's `dueAtIso` while keeping it `scheduled`, returning the updated list to persist (or a structured reason when nothing changed). To avoid duplicating the addressing logic, the id-matching (exact id OR a unique id prefix, refusing an ambiguous prefix rather than guessing) and the "only a scheduled check-in is mutable" status guard (reporting already-fired / already-cancelled) were extracted into one shared `matchCheckin` + `mutableStatusReason` that both cancel and snooze now use ŌĆö so the two commands address a check-in identically and the P35-13 cancel behaviour is unchanged (behaviour-preserving refactor, verified by its existing tests staying green). - [Proactivity/Felt] A user's morning brief (`muse brief`) now surfaces the follow-ups they're DUE on ŌĆö things they said they'd do whose check-in has come due ŌĆö so the proactivity payoff reaches the pull surface, not only the background daemon (P35-15). P35-11..14 built the full commitment ŌåÆ check-in arc: detect what the user voiced in passing ("I need to call the dentist"), schedule a warm "how did it go?" follow-up, and cancel/snooze it.
