- [Grounding edge/Reach] `muse ask --url` (and `muse notes ingest --url`) now REFUSE to ground on a non-text resource ŌĆö a PDF / image / binary URL ŌĆö instead of reading its garbled bytes and hallucinating a confident, cited answer from them (P38-32). The shared web-read core `fetchReadableUrl` in packages/mcp/src/fetch-readable-url.ts (behind both the `--url` ask grounding and the `--url` notes ingest) read EVERY response body via `response.text()` with NO content-type check, then ran HTML tag-stripping over it. So a URL pointing at a PDF, an image, or an application/octet-stream decoded its binary bytes to garbled text, which the local model would then ground on, invent plausible-sounding content from, and cite to the URL ŌĆö exactly the fabrication the edge exists to prevent, and for the ingest path a way to poison the notes corpus with garbage. Fixed by adding a pure exported `isReadableContentType(contentType)` that gates on the response's declared `content-type`: text/* , application/xhtml+xml, application/xml, anything ending `+xml` (RSS/Atom/XHTML), and application/json (incl. ld+json) are groundable text; a declared binary type (application/pdf, image/*, application/octet-stream, audio/*, video/*, font/*, application/zip) makes `fetchReadableUrl` return `{ ok: false, error: "not a readable text page (content-type: <type>)" }`. A MISSING content-type is not trusted blindly ŌĆö it falls through to a binary-content sniff backstop (a NUL byte, or >10% U+FFFD replacement chars in the first 4KB of the decoded body, mirrors the `--file` binary refusal) so a binary body served under a wrong/absent content-type is still refused. No CLI change was needed: the `muse ask --url` branch already renders an `!ok` fetch result as "muse: could not fetch --url ŌĆ” (<error>) ŌĆö I won't ground on it", so the new refusal flows straight to the user. Proof: 6 new tests in packages/mcp/test/fetch-readable-url.test.ts exercising the REAL fetchReadableUrl path with only the network faked (contract-faithful per outbound-safety.md): a PDF content-type refuses with "application/pdf" in the message; an image/png refuses; an application/json and a text/plain response are allowed and their text grounded; a binary body (NUL bytes) served as text/html is caught by the sniff with "binary content"; and `isReadableContentType` allows the whole text family plus an empty type while refusing 8 distinct binary types ŌĆö plus the existing SSRF / redirect / retry tests all still green + the full @muse/mcp suite green (167 files / 1359 tests) + a LIVE round-trip on the loop PC against a REAL URL: `muse ask --url https://arxiv.org/pdf/2310.11511 "what is this paper about?"` now prints "could not fetch --url https://arxiv.org/pdf/2310.11511 (not a readable text page (content-type: application/pdf)) ŌĆö I won't ground on it", whereas `muse ask --url https://example.com` still fetches and grounds on the HTML page. mcp 167 files / 1359 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a user who points Muse at a PDF, image, or other binary URL now gets an honest "I won't ground on it" instead of a confident answer fabricated from binary garbage, and the same protection keeps a binary URL from poisoning the corpus on ingest ŌĆö P38-32 bullet
- [Actuation/Reliability] A rate-limited outbound reminder/notice (HTTP 429 + Retry-After) is now actually DELIVERED instead of silently dropped ŌĆö the send-retry layer waits the server-mandated Retry-After rather than burning its 3 fixed attempts in ~1 second (P41-1). `sendWithRetry` in packages/mcp/src/messaging-retry.ts is the single retry path behind EVERY outbound firing loop ŌĆö reminders, follow-ups, pattern notices, proactive notices, situational briefings, standing-objective sends, ambient nudges, and web-watch alerts (one helper, eight surfaces). It used a fixed `[0, 200, 800]ms` backoff ladder, and its catch only inspected `cause.retryable` ŌĆö it NEVER read the server's `Retry-After`. So when Telegram/Slack/Discord/LINE answered a send with `429 + Retry-After: 30`, the retry fired again at 200ms then 800ms, was throttled all three times, and the message was DROPPED ŌĆö the user simply never received their 9am reminder, with no error they'd see. `MessagingProviderError` (packages/messaging/src/errors.ts) carried `status` but had no retry-after field, and its own doc-comment acknowledged "429 + Retry-After ŌĆ” retry-with-backoff is the right response" even as the send path ignored the hint. Fixed end-to-end: (1) a new `retryAfterMs?` field on `MessagingProviderError` (validated finite & non-negative); (2) populated at all four HTTP providers' send-failure throws ŌĆö telegram/slack/discord/line ŌĆö via a new exported `retryAfterMsFromResponse(response, bodyRetryAfterSeconds?)` that prefers a provider's body `retry_after` (Telegram returns the wait in the body `parameters.retry_after`, in seconds) and otherwise parses the `Retry-After` response header through a renamed/clarified `parseRetryAfterMs` (the old `parseRetryAfterSeconds` already returned ms despite its name); (3) `sendWithRetry` now, on a caught retryable `MessagingProviderError` carrying `retryAfterMs`, sleeps that server-mandated delay ŌĆö capped at 30s so a hostile or absurd hint can't hang a firing loop ŌĆö instead of the ladder value, and falls back to the unchanged `[0,200,800]` ladder when no hint is present so a plain transient 5xx is completely unregressed; the `sleep` is injectable so the test asserts the delay with no real wall-clock wait. This is the human-directed "harden the one-of-each actuators into daily-reliable integrations against rate-limit / transient-5xx" mandate, classified as outward reliability work, not churn. Proof (fully deterministic ŌĆö contract-faithful HTTP fakes + injected sleep spy per outbound-safety.md, ZERO dependence on the local model): 4 new tests in packages/mcp/test/messaging-retry.test.ts (a 429 carrying retryAfterMs=3000 makes sendWithRetry sleep 3000 ŌĆö not BACKOFFS_MS[1]=200 ŌĆö then deliver on the next attempt; a 1-hour hint is capped to 30000; a hint-less 503 still uses the [200,800] ladder unchanged; a non-retryable 400 still short-circuits with no sleep) + a Discord provider test (a 429 response with `Retry-After: 7` header ŌåÆ the thrown MessagingProviderError carries retryAfterMs===7000 and retryable===true) + a Telegram provider test (a 429 with body `parameters.retry_after: 12` ŌåÆ retryAfterMs===12000) + 2 helper tests for parseRetryAfterMs (numeric seconds ŌåÆ ms, garbage/missing ŌåÆ undefined) and retryAfterMsFromResponse (body wins over header, header fallback, neither ŌåÆ undefined) + the existing send/retry/runDueReminders tests all still green + the full @muse/messaging suite (368 tests) and @muse/mcp suite (168 files / 1363 tests) green + cli build green. mcp 168 files / 1363 tests + messaging 368 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a user whose reminder or proactive notice hits a provider rate limit now receives it a tick or two later, on every outbound surface, instead of silently losing it ŌĆö P41-1 bullet
- [Actuation/Safety] `muse messaging send` is now draft-first, fail-closed, and action-logged ŌĆö an ungated autonomous third-party send is closed (P41-2). The CLI's `messaging send --local <provider> <destination> <text>` (Telegram / Discord / Slack / LINE) called `registry.send(...)` DIRECTLY ŌĆö no draft-first confirmation, no approval gate, no action-log entry ŌĆö even though the sibling `muse email send` was fully draft-first/confirm-gated/logged. That is precisely the autonomous send to a third party that `.claude/rules/outbound-safety.md` and CLAUDE.md classify as never-allowed ("Outbound to a third party ŌĆ” is fail-close & draft-first ŌĆ” never an autonomous send"); the gap was that the already-built and already-tested `sendMessageWithApproval` helper (packages/mcp/src/message-send.ts ŌĆö draft-first, fail-closed gate, mandatory action-log of sent OR refused) had been wired into the agent tool (loopback-messaging.ts) but NEVER into the human CLI surface. Fixed in apps/cli/src/commands-messaging.ts: the `--local` send now routes through `sendMessageWithApproval` with a default terminal approval gate that prints the EXACT draft ("Send via <provider> ŌåÆ <destination>: <text>") and proceeds only on an explicit confirm; every outcome is appended to the personal action log (a `refused` entry on denial, a `performed` entry on send) so the send is on the record and subject to undo/veto like any other action; a new `--user <id>` option tags the log entry; and the default gate FAIL-CLOSES when no interactive terminal is present (a non-TTY / piped / scripted / CI context returns "no interactive terminal to confirm the send" and refuses, rather than hanging on stdin waiting for input or ŌĆö worse ŌĆö sending unconfirmed). A `deps` seam (approvalGate / registry / actionLogFile) injects the gate and a fake registry for deterministic testing. The API (non-`--local`) path is unchanged ŌĆö it is gated server-side by the runtime tool-approval gate. Also exported `sendMessageWithApproval` (+ its types) from the @muse/mcp index, which had been import-only. Proof: 3 new deterministic tests in apps/cli/src/commands-messaging-send.test.ts driving the REAL CLI command over a recording fake registry + an injected gate (a contract-faithful fake, never a stubbed registry, per outbound-safety.md; zero model or network dependence): a DENIED gate leaves the recording registry untouched (NOTHING sent), prints "Not sent (denied)", exits non-zero, and appends a `refused` action-log entry with `what: "message via telegram to chat123"`; a gate that THROWS is treated as a denial (still no send ŌĆö fail-closed); an APPROVED gate sends exactly `{ destination, text }` and appends a `performed` entry ŌĆö plus the existing program.test.ts `--local` round-trip updated to assert that a non-TTY send now fail-closes ("Not sent", zero provider API calls) instead of sending unconfirmed. cli 169 files / 1811 tests + mcp 168 files / 1363 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a user (or a stray script) can no longer fire a message to a third party from the Muse CLI without seeing and confirming the exact content first, and every send or refusal is recorded ŌĆö P41-2 bullet
- [Knowledge] A user can now `muse notes rename <from> <to>` and have every `[[wiki-link]]` pointing at that note automatically rewritten across the whole corpus ŌĆö renaming a note no longer silently breaks its backlinks (P42-1). `muse notes` had list / read / search / save / append / delete but NO rename or move, while Muse already builds a note link graph (`buildNoteLinkGraph`), surfaces backlinks, and AUDITS for broken links (`auditNoteGraph`) ŌĆö yet offered no remedy, so moving or renaming a note orphaned every `[[link]]` pointing at it (and `auditNoteGraph` would then just report them as broken). Added a pure exported `rewriteWikiLinkReferences(body, oldTarget, newTarget)` in apps/cli/src/notes-links.ts that rewrites the TARGET portion of each `[[ŌĆ”]]` reference, preserving any `|alias` and `#section` suffix, matching the target case-insensitively (the same key rule `extractWikiLinks` uses), and never on a partial match (`[[ideabank]]` is left alone when renaming `ideas`); plus a `renameNoteWithLinkRewrite(notesDir, fromPath, toPath, dryRun)` orchestration and a `muse notes rename <from> <to> [--dry-run] [--json]` command. The command renames the file, walks the entire notes tree rewriting `[[<basename>]]` references to it, refuses a missing source or an existing destination (no silent clobber) and any path that escapes the notes directory (a `..` traversal guard), counts how many links across how many notes were rewritten, and `--dry-run` reports exactly what WOULD change without touching anything. The link target is the renamed note's basename without `.md` (the bare `[[note]]` convention); the operation is local-only (a direct corpus mutation, no API/model). Proof: 5 new deterministic tests ŌĆö 2 for `rewriteWikiLinkReferences` in apps/cli/src/notes-links.test.ts (it rewrites the target while preserving `|alias` and `#section`, is case-insensitive, leaves an unrelated `[[other]]` and a longer `[[ideabank]]` untouched; returns the body unchanged with count 0 for a non-matching or blank target) and 3 for `renameNoteWithLinkRewrite` in apps/cli/src/commands-notes.test.ts over a real temp corpus (it moves the file ŌĆö gone at the old path, present at the new ŌĆö and rewrites both `[[ideas]]` and `[[ideas|my ideas]]` in another note to `[[concepts]]` / `[[concepts|my ideas]]` while leaving `[[tasks]]` alone; `--dry-run` reports linksRewritten=2 but moves nothing and edits no note; a missing source errors with "no note at ŌĆ”" and an existing destination errors with "already exists" leaving the original file intact) + the full @muse/cli suite green (169 files / 1816 tests) + LIVE round-trips on the loop PC: `muse notes rename ideas.md concepts.md` over a corpus where another note links `[[ideas]]` and `[[ideas|the idea note]]` prints "Renamed ideas.md ŌåÆ concepts.md, rewrote 2 link(s) across 1 note(s)", the file is actually moved, and the links become `[[concepts]]` and `[[concepts|the idea note]]` (alias preserved); `--dry-run` prints "Would rename ŌĆ” (N link(s) ŌĆ” would be rewritten)" without changing anything, and renaming onto an existing path prints "ŌĆ” already exists ŌĆö refusing to overwrite". cli 169 files / 1816 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a user can now rename or reorganise a note and keep their entire [[wiki-link]] graph intact, instead of silently orphaning every backlink to it ŌĆö P42-1 bullet
- [Grounding edge/Felt] The morning brief (`muse brief`) is now grounded against your schedule ŌĆö it can't tell you about a meeting TIME that isn't on your calendar without flagging it, extending the fabrication=0 gate to the one surface that lacked it (P38-33). The brief was the only `muse ask`-style surface with NO grounding gate: its JARVIS-style summary is model-composed prose streamed straight to stdout from a deterministic fact sheet (tasks / events / reminders / due check-ins), so the local model drifting or inventing an appointment time ŌĆö "don't forget your dentist at 5pm" when nothing is at 5pm ŌĆö would pass as fact on the flagship felt surface a user reads first thing each morning. Added a pure exported `unscheduledTimesInBrief(briefProse, factSheet, nowMinutes)` in apps/cli/src/commands-brief.ts that extracts clock times from BOTH the composed brief and the fact sheet and returns any time the brief asserts that appears on neither the schedule nor the current clock. It is format-robust: an internal `clockTimesToMinutes` normalises 12-hour ("3pm", "3:30 p.m.", "7:45am") and 24-hour ("15:00", "09:30") forms to minutes-since-midnight (with a negative lookahead so "3:30 pm" isn't double-counted as a bare 03:30), so a faithful time the model rendered in EITHER format matches the fact sheet's 24-hour times ŌĆö the property that makes the check safe to run on the flagship surface. The allowed set is the fact sheet's times plus the current clock (so an "it's 9:30am" greeting is never flagged). The brief action runs the gate on the streamed-then-collected answer and, if any unscheduled time is found, appends a stderr warning ("ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ This summary mentions a time not on your schedule (ŌĆ”) ŌĆö double-check it against your calendar before relying on it"); the gate is FAIL-OPEN (it warns, never blocks or regenerates the brief) and deliberately ZERO-false-positive ŌĆö a time it can't parse, a relative phrase ("in 2 hours"), a scheduled time in any format, and the current clock are all allowed, because a false warning on the morning briefing would erode trust worse than the original gap. It catches a wholly-fabricated time (one nowhere on the schedule); a drift to a time that happens to be elsewhere on the schedule (e.g. an event's end time) is the accepted precision trade for the zero-false-positive guarantee. Proof: 5 new deterministic tests in apps/cli/src/commands-brief.test.ts (a brief echoing scheduled 12h/24h times + the current clock + a relative "in 2 hours; 3 tasks open" flags NOTHING; "dentist at 5pm" and "standup at 7:45am" ŌĆö neither on the schedule ŌĆö are flagged; an invented "call at 2pm" on an EMPTY schedule is flagged while "it's 9:30, nothing scheduled" is not; repeated "5pm ŌĆ” 5 pm" dedupes to one) + the full @muse/cli suite green (169 files / 1821 tests) + a LIVE round-trip on the loop PC (qwen3:8b): seeding a reminder due at 17:42, `muse brief` opened "Good afternoon. You have a dentist appointment scheduled for 17:42." with NO time warning ŌĆö the model echoed the real 17:42 and the gate correctly stayed silent (zero false positive end-to-end on a real faithful brief). cli 169 files / 1821 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö Muse's morning briefing now plugs into the same fabrication=0 grounding edge as recall, reflection, and council, so it can't quietly tell you about a meeting you don't actually have ŌĆö P38-33 bullet
- [Grounding edge] The end-of-session episode summary is now gated against its own transcript ŌĆö a fabricated "decision" the conversation never contained is DROPPED instead of persisted as a citable memory, closing the edge's last ungated surface and its first INGEST one (P38-34). Every OUTPUT surface that emits a claim about the user's world ŌĆö recall (`muse ask`), reflection, swarm council, and the morning brief ŌĆö already passes through the deterministic grounding+citation gate, but the one INGEST surface did not: when a chat session ends, `captureEndOfSessionEpisode` (apps/cli/src/chat-end-session.ts) calls `summariseSession` ŌĆö whose `SUMMARISER_SYSTEM_PROMPT` explicitly asks the local model for "WHAT the user decided or where the matter stands" and "ANY explicit follow-up the user asked for" ŌĆö and then persisted that model-written free text via `upsertEpisode` after ONLY re-scrubbing credential shapes, with NO faithfulness check against the transcript. That summary later becomes a citable `[session: ŌĆ”]` source that `enforceAnswerCitations` and the recall stack trust as ground truth, so a hallucinated decision in the summary (e.g. the model writing "the user decided to book a flight to Tokyo on Friday" for a session that only discussed a Q3 budget memo) would later be served back to the user as a CITED fact ŌĆö a fabrication entering through the back door, behind every output gate. Fixed with a pure exported `summaryGroundedInTranscript(summary, turns, floor)` in packages/agent-core/src/episodic-summariser.ts that measures the fraction of the summary's content tokens ŌĆö via `lexicalTokens`, the exact tokeniser the recall gate uses ŌĆö that occur anywhere in the transcript turns, returning false when it falls below the floor (i.e. the summary talks about things the session never did); `captureEndOfSessionEpisode` now calls it after summarising and DROPS the episode ("summary not grounded in the session transcript ŌĆö dropped to avoid persisting a fabricated memory", status skipped) rather than writing it. The floor (`DEFAULT_EPISODE_GROUNDING_FLOOR = 0.25`) is deliberately LENIENT: a faithful paraphrase adds framing words ("decided", "discussed") absent from the transcript so its coverage sits well below 1, and silently dropping a real memory is worse than keeping a borderline one (the recall gate still applies downstream when it is recalled), so the floor only has to be high enough to reject a WHOLESALE fabrication (which scores ~0 coverage) and low enough never to drop a real but terse summary. This is the edge's FIRST gate on ingest rather than output ŌĆö extending "one deterministic grounding gate under EVERY surface" to the memory-write path. Proof (fully DETERMINISTIC ŌĆö no live model is involved in the check, the model's summary is the INPUT being gated): 4 new unit tests in packages/agent-core/test/episodic-summariser.test.ts (a faithful Q3-budget-memo/Notion summary whose content is drawn from the transcript ŌåÆ grounded=true; the "book a flight to Tokyo" fabrication over that same transcript ŌåÆ false; an empty transcript is un-groundable ŌåÆ false and an empty summary asserts nothing ŌåÆ true; an explicit stricter/looser floor is honoured) + a new surface assertion on the EXISTING captureEndOfSessionEpisode harness in apps/cli/test/program.test.ts (a stub provider returning a fabricated Tokyo-travel summary over a Q3-memo transcript is DROPPED with status "skipped" and reason containing "not grounded", and the on-disk episodes.json stays at exactly one entry ŌĆö the fabricated episode never lands), while the existing happy-path capture and the secret-scrub test both stay green (the scrub test's seeded transcript enriched so its summary remains grounded, since that test is about scrubbing not grounding) + the full @muse/agent-core suite green (112 files / 1405 tests) + the full @muse/cli suite green (169 files / 1821 tests). agent-core 112 files / 1405 tests + cli 169 files / 1821 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö Muse can no longer quietly remember, and then cite back to you, a decision or follow-up you never actually made ŌĆö P38-34 bullet
- [Perception] A user can now `muse ask --file <message>.eml` (or `muse read` it, or include it in a folder ingest) and ground on the saved email's DECODED subject + readable body, instead of raw RFC822/MIME (P37-20). `muse read` / `muse ask --file` already handled PDFs (parsed), HTML (readable text), and plain text, but a saved email file (`.eml`) fell through to `bytes.toString("utf8")` ŌĆö so the local model was handed the raw message: RFC822 headers, `multipart/alternative` boundaries, and a `quoted-printable` or `base64` body (`Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable` ŌĆ” `drop by 5=25 before Friday`), which buries the actual content under transport encoding and makes a grounded answer cite mangled text. A full RFC822/MIME parser already existed in the codebase ŌĆö `parseHeaders`, `extractBody` (multipart ŌåÆ first text/plain part, quoted-printable/base64 decoded, HTML stripped), and `decodeHeaderValue` (RFC2047 encoded-word `=?UTF-8?B?ŌĆ”?=` subjects) in apps/cli/src/mbox-ingest.ts ŌĆö but it was wired only into the `--mbox` chat ingest, never the `--file` grounding path. Added two small functions to apps/cli/src/document-reader.ts that REUSE that parser: `isEmlDocument(filePath)` (extension-based, `.eml`) and `emlToText(rawEml)`, which emits the decoded `Subject:` / `From:` / `Date:` header lines followed by the decoded readable body. `extractDocumentText` (the shared `muse read` / `--file` extractor) now routes a `.eml` through `emlToText` right after the PDF check and BEFORE the binary-refusal check (an .eml's text headers never trip the binary heuristic, and a base64 part inside is exactly what the parser decodes), the `muse ask --file` branch in commands-ask.ts does the same, and `.eml` was added to `SUPPORTED_DOC_EXT` so a directory of saved emails ingests too. Nothing else changed ŌĆö PDF/HTML/text/binary handling is untouched. Proof: 3 new unit tests in apps/cli/src/document-reader.test.ts (`isEmlDocument` matches only `.eml` case-insensitively; `emlToText` on a multipart message decodes the `=?UTF-8?B?UTMgYnVkZ2V0IOKAlCByZXZpZXc=?=` subject to "Q3 budget ŌĆö review", picks the text/plain part over the text/html part, unwinds `5=25`ŌåÆ`5%`, joins a soft line break, and turns `headcount=3F`ŌåÆ`headcount?` with no raw `=3F` or HTML left; `extractDocumentText` returns one page of clean text carrying "Q3 budget" and no "Content-Transfer-Encoding") + the full @muse/cli suite green (169 files / 1824 tests) + a LIVE round-trip on the loop PC (qwen3:8b): a `.eml` whose quoted-printable body says "The Q3 budget must drop by 5=25 before Friday. - [Knowledge] A user can now run `muse notes fix-links` to repair broken `[[wiki-links]]` across their notes ŌĆö each broken/typo'd link is snapped to its unique closest existing note, while ambiguous or genuinely-missing ones are safely left alone (P42-2). Muse's note link graph already DETECTS broken links (`auditNoteGraph` returns a `brokenLinks` list of `[[target]]` references that resolve to no note) but only ever PRINTED them ŌĆö there was no remediation, so a typo'd `[[concpets]]` or a link left dangling after a manual edit / import stayed broken and the user had to hunt and fix each by hand. Added a pure exported `planLinkFixes(brokenTargets, existingIds, maxDistance)` in apps/cli/src/notes-links.ts that, for each broken target, finds existing note ids within `maxDistance` edits (reusing the existing `levenshteinDistance`) and snaps it to the match ŌĆö but ONLY when there is EXACTLY ONE candidate at the closest distance; a target with two equally-close notes (an ambiguous typo) or no near match is returned as `unresolved` rather than silently mis-linked to the wrong note (the wrong-snap is the one real risk of a fuzzy repair, so it is fenced off by construction). The default `maxDistance` is 2 (catches a transposition or a one/two-character slip), case-insensitive, with deduped targets. A `fixBrokenLinks(notesDir, dryRun, maxDistance)` orchestration builds the corpus link graph, audits it, plans the fixes, and applies them via the P42-1 `rewriteWikiLinkReferences` (which preserves any `|alias` / `#section`); and a `muse notes fix-links [--dry-run] [--max-distance N] [--json]` command lists each applied fix as `[[from]] ŌåÆ [[to]]` and separately reports the links it left unresolved so the user knows what still needs a human. `--dry-run` plans and previews without writing a single note. The operation is local-only and fully deterministic (no model). Proof: 4 new `planLinkFixes` unit tests in apps/cli/src/notes-links.test.ts (a unique typo "concpets" at distance 2 ŌåÆ fixed to "concepts"; an ambiguous "foop" with both "food" and "fool" at distance 1 ŌåÆ left unresolved with NO fix; a no-match target unresolved + a case-insensitive dedupe of repeated targets; a tighter `maxDistance` 1 correctly refuses the distance-2 snap) + 3 new `fixBrokenLinks` tests in apps/cli/src/commands-notes.test.ts over a real temp corpus (a journal linking `[[concpets]]` and `[[totallymissing]]` against a `concepts.md` note ŌåÆ the typo is rewritten to `[[concepts]]` and the genuinely-missing link is left untouched; `--dry-run` returns the same plan but edits nothing on disk; an all-resolving corpus reports no fixes and no unresolved) + the full @muse/cli suite green (169 files / 1831 tests) + a LIVE end-to-end round-trip on the loop PC: `muse notes fix-links --dry-run` then `muse notes fix-links` over that corpus print "Fixed 1 broken link(s) across 1 note(s): ŌĆó [[concpets]] ŌåÆ [[concepts]]" and "1 link(s) left unresolved (no unique close match): [[totallymissing]]", with journal.md afterward reading "See [[concepts]] for the idea, and [[totallymissing]] too." ŌĆö the typo repaired, the missing link deliberately untouched. cli 169 files / 1831 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a user can now repair a whole corpus of broken wiki-links in one command (completing the link-maintenance toolkit alongside `muse notes rename`), with the only real hazard ŌĆö snapping to the wrong note ŌĆö eliminated by the unique-match guard ŌĆö P42-2 bullet
- [Autonomy] A user running `muse daemon` now has the corrections they made in past chat sessions distilled into learned strategies UNATTENDED ŌĆö on the daemon's idle tick, with NO manual `muse playbook distill` ŌĆö closing the first slice of the autonomous self-development loop (P43-1 slice 1). The self-development mechanisms already existed but only as manual CLI (`muse playbook distill` / `consolidate`, `skills consolidate`) and the `apps/api` server tick (`tick-daemons.ts` wires `startConsolidateTick` + `distillQueuedCorrections`); the process the user actually runs on their Mac ŌĆö `muse daemon` (apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.ts) ŌĆö drove proactive / reminder / followup / ambient / web-watch / objectives / briefing / reflection ticks but NO learning-from-corrections tick, so a correction enqueued (`enqueueLearnEvent`) at correction time sat untouched until the user manually distilled it: the self-improvement loop was open exactly where it matters. Fixed WITHOUT forking the grounding-fenced drain: moved `distillQueuedCorrections` (+ `DistillQueuedDeps`) from apps/api into `@muse/autoconfigure` (the one package that depends on BOTH `@muse/agent-core` ŌĆö the distiller ŌĆö and `@muse/mcp` ŌĆö the learn-queue + playbook ops), with apps/api/src/distill-queue.ts now a byte-identical re-export so the server tick + its tests are unchanged, and the CLI daemon importing the SAME implementation (one source of truth, no duplicated grounding fence). Wired a `selfLearnTick` into `muse daemon`'s `runTick`, mirroring the existing reflection ("dreaming") tick: gated by `MUSE_SELFLEARN_ENABLED` (off by default) AND a resolved model, interval-throttled (`MUSE_SELFLEARN_INTERVAL_MS`, default 5 min), and BRAKE-FIRST ŌĆö the learning-pause kill switch (`isLearningPaused`) is checked inside the drain so a paused user gets zero writes and the queue is left intact for a later resume; at most one distill per tick (the LLM call is the cost); every unattended write lands on PROBATION (recorded + visible via `muse learned` but NOT injected into prompts until a real reinforce graduates it ŌĆö the self-confirmation guard) with `origin: "grounded"` carrying the real correction as its source; fail-soft (a throwing distiller/embedder never breaks the daemon); a new `--status` line reports `self-learn: enabled/disabled`. The grounding floor is preserved end-to-end ŌĆö a queued event with no real correction text, or a distiller that returns nothing, writes ZERO strategies (a non-corrective signal never fabricates a lesson). - [Autonomy] A user running `muse daemon` now has stale, unused learned strategies automatically FADE toward neutral on the daemon's idle tick ŌĆö the forgetting half of continuous RL over the memory bank, so a one-off thumbs-up can't keep steering the agent forever (P43-1 slice 2). Slice 1 gave the daemon the ADDING half (distill corrections ŌåÆ probation strategies unattended); but the user's actual runtime had no FORGETTING ŌĆö `decayStalePlaybookRewards` (every positive-reward, non-probation strategy not reinforced within the 30-day stale window loses a step toward NEUTRAL 0, never below ŌĆö disuse fades trust, it does not punish) ran ONLY in the `apps/api` server tick (`tick-daemons.ts`), never in `muse daemon` (the process the user launches on their Mac), so a strategy they thumbs-upped once and stopped using stayed at its old reward forever and kept being injected into every relevant prompt as stale advice. Wired a `selfLearnDecayTick` into the daemon's `runTick` (apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.ts) under the SAME `MUSE_SELFLEARN_ENABLED` switch as distill (one switch = "autonomous self-development on": the bank both grows from corrections and fades from disuse), BRAKE-FIRST ŌĆö it checks the learning-pause kill switch (`isLearningPaused`) before touching anything, so a paused user's bank is frozen and a later resume catches up ŌĆö model-free (pure time+file, so it runs without a resolved model) on a slow daily cadence (`MUSE_SELFLEARN_DECAY_INTERVAL_MS`, default 24h), fail-soft, logging `decay: N stale strategŌĆ” faded toward neutral` only when it actually fades something. Probation, neutral, and already-negative entries are untouched (decay only sinks earned-positive-but-now-stale strategies; a real correction is still what drives a strategy negative). - [Reliability/Actuation] `muse calendar add` (and the agent's calendar-create/move/cancel tool) against Google Calendar now SURVIVES a 429 rate-limit on the write ŌĆö it retries honouring the server's Retry-After instead of dropping the event ŌĆö closing the calendar actuator's transient-failure gap toward all-actuator reliability (P43-2 slice 1). Messaging dispatch already retried transient failures (`sendWithRetry`: 3 attempts, honours `MessagingProviderError.retryAfterMs`, short-circuits permanent errors), but the calendar actuator did NOT: `GoogleCalendarProvider.request` retried ONLY idempotent GETs (`maxRetries = method === "GET" ? this.retries : 0`) ŌĆö every write (POST createEvent / PATCH updateEvent / DELETE deleteEvent) failed outright on a transient status, so a Google burst-quota 429 (the most common transient failure for Calendar writes) silently dropped the user's event when created via `muse calendar add` or the agent calendar tool (loopback-calendar.ts). Fixed SAFELY ŌĆö the hard part of retrying a state-changing send: a WRITE now retries ONLY a 429 rate-limit, honouring `Retry-After` (parsed per RFC 7231 ŌĆö delta-seconds or HTTP-date, junk rejected ŌĆö clamped to CALENDAR_RETRY_AFTER_CAP_MS=30s, else exponential backoff), because a 429 is rejected by Google BEFORE the mutation is applied (no event created) so retrying can't double-create; a write 5xx OR a mid-flight network reject is AMBIGUOUS (the insert may have committed) and is NEVER retried (the existing "no double-create" guarantee is preserved). GET reads keep retrying 429/5xx + network rejects as before. Added `parseRetryAfterMs` + `CALENDAR_RETRY_AFTER_CAP_MS` to packages/calendar/src/errors.ts (mirroring the messaging/model Retry-After contract; calendar can't import @muse/mcp's copy ŌĆö wrong dependency direction) and exported them from the calendar barrel. Proof: contract-faithful HTTP fake (never a stubbed provider) in packages/calendar/test/google-provider.test.ts ŌĆö a write that returns 429+`Retry-After: 2` then 200 retries once and succeeds, sleeping exactly 2000ms (honoured the server hint, NOT the 250ms backoff); a 429 with no Retry-After falls back to 250ms exponential backoff; the 429 retry budget exhausts to a thrown HTTP_429 after initial+2 retries (no infinite loop); a 500 on a write is STILL never retried (single attempt, no double-create) ŌĆö plus 6 new `parseRetryAfterMs`/`isRetryableCalendarStatus` unit tests in packages/calendar/test/errors.test.ts (delta-seconds, HTTP-date relative-to-now clamped at 0, junk/decimal/negative rejected) + the full @muse/calendar suite green (12 files / 135 tests) + calendar tsc clean + `pnpm check` green across all workspaces (after restoring the goal-227 byte-hygiene gate in a separate fix) + pnpm lint 0/0. - [Self-improve/Retrieval] A user can now enable `MUSE_PLAYBOOK_EMBED_RANK=true` so `muse ask` ranks the learned-strategy playbook (ACE / ReasoningBank) by SEMANTIC similarity to the question instead of pure lexical token-overlap ŌĆö a strategy the user phrased DIFFERENTLY from the current query now surfaces and gets applied, where token-overlap ranking surfaced the wrong (merely word-sharing) one (a research-validated small-model lever: for a FROZEN local model, retrieval quality dominates output ŌĆö "experience-following"). The playbook ranker (`scoreStrategy`/`rankPlaybookStrategies`, packages/agent-core/src/playbook.ts) was pure lexical ŌĆö `rankOverlap(query tokens, strategy tokens)` + reward + reflected-penalty ŌĆö with nomic embeddings used only in the merge/distill gates, never in per-query strategy surfacing; its own comment even flagged the scorer as "the swap-point for an embedding ranker later". Added a model-agnostic `rankPlaybookStrategiesByRelevance(strategies, queryText, embed, options)` that blends `EMBED_RANK_WEIGHT(5) * cosine(query, strategy)` into the existing score: `embed` is a duck-typed `(text) => Promise<number[]>` param (agent-core stays vendor-free ŌĆö the caller passes a local embedder), only eligible (non-avoided, non-probation) strategies are embedded, and any strategy whose embedding throws degrades to its pure-lexical score (a flaky embedder never drops a strategy). The sync `rankPlaybookStrategies` and the new async path now share one `rankEligible` helper, so the top-K + recency-floor + avoidance/probation exclusions are identical across both (behaviour-preserving for the lexical path ŌĆö all existing ranking tests unchanged). Wired into the `muse ask` chat-fast-path (apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts, where a nomic embedder + cosine are already in scope) behind `MUSE_PLAYBOOK_EMBED_RANK` (OFF by default ŌĆö it adds one local nomic pass per strategy, so it stays opt-in with no latency regression to the default ask; `MUSE_PLAYBOOK_EMBED_MODEL` overrides the embed model), fail-soft back to the lexical ranker. - [Grounding edge/Retrieval] A user can now enable `MUSE_RECALL_BM25=true` so personal-knowledge recall ranks the lexical half of its hybrid retrieval by Okapi BM25 (IDF-weighted, length-normalised) instead of raw token-overlap ŌĆö a query's RARE discriminative term (a name, an ID, an error code) now outranks a chunk that merely shares a corpus-common term, fewer/better passages being the single biggest precision lever for a weak local generator (research-backed). `rankKnowledgeChunks(hybrid:true)` (packages/agent-core/src/knowledge-recall.ts) already fused a cosine ranking with a LEXICAL ranking via Reciprocal Rank Fusion (+ MMR), but the lexical signal was `lexicalOverlap` ŌĆö a raw COUNT of shared content tokens that weights every term equally and ignores chunk length, so a chunk sharing one common term ties (or beats) one sharing a rarer, more discriminative term. Added an exported `bm25Scores(queryTokens, chunks, key)` implementing Okapi BM25 ŌĆö IDF (`ln(1 + (NŌłÆdf+0.5)/(df+0.5))`) ├Ś saturating TF (k1=1.5) with document-length normalisation (b=0.75) over the candidate chunk set as the corpus ŌĆö and refactored the tokeniser so `lexicalTokens` (the de-duped Set) and BM25 (which needs the term-frequency multiset + document length) share one `lexicalTokenList` filter (behaviour-preserving: `lexicalTokens` now `new Set(lexicalTokenList(text))`, identical output). A new `bm25?: boolean` option on `RankKnowledgeOptions` (default OFF ŌĆö the raw-overlap behaviour is unchanged) swaps the fusion's lexical RANKING to BM25 when on, while the overlap-based citation FENCE (a passage earns a citation only with cosine Ōēź threshold OR any lexical overlap) is left exactly as-is ŌĆö BM25 > 0 iff overlap > 0, so the fabrication=0 guard is untouched and only the ORDER among already-eligible passages changes. Wired into the two production recall paths in autoconfigure (knowledge-corpus.ts: the ambient "Related:" lookup + the knowledge_search corpus) behind `MUSE_RECALL_BM25` (opt-in, no default-path latency/behaviour change). Proof: 2 new deterministic tests in knowledge-recall-agent.test.ts (no live model) ŌĆö `bm25Scores` ranks a chunk matching the rare "zephyr" (df=1, high IDF) strictly ABOVE one matching the corpus-common "report" (df=3, low IDF) where raw overlap ties both at 1; and `rankKnowledgeChunks(hybrid:true, bm25:true)` with a cosine-neutralising zero embed surfaces the rare-"zephyr" chunk at the top where the same call WITHOUT bm25 leaves a common-"report" chunk leading ŌĆö plus the full @muse/agent-core suite green (112 files / 1410 tests, the existing hybrid/RRF/MMR + lexical-tokeniser tests unchanged by the refactor), @muse/autoconfigure tsc clean, apps/cli tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE regression touch on the loop PC: `pnpm eval:self-improving` 18/18 batteries green on local Ollama qwen3:8b (the cited-recall / recall-citation-gate / rubric-gate / faithfulness / claim-grounding / proactive-recall-gate WEDGE + grounding batteries all still pass ŌĆö the default recall path is unchanged and the tokeniser refactor regressed nothing). agent-core 112 files / 1410 tests + eval:self-improving 18/18 + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö Muse's personal recall can now key on the discriminative rare term (a name / ID / code) a small model most needs grounded, where raw token-overlap drowned it under common-word matches ŌĆö small-model retrieval-precision lever (memory: project_small_model_maximization)
- [Grounding edge] A correctly WEB-grounded `muse ask --with-tools` answer is no longer false-flagged "not backed by your notes" ŌĆö the agent-path grounding verdict now scores the answer against the agent's OWN tool outputs (the evidence it was actually shown), not a notes-only set, closing a deterministic false-positive on the identity surface. The output-side rubric VERDICT (`groundingVerdictNotice` ŌåÆ `verifyGrounding`/RGV) already ran under BOTH the chat-only AND the `--with-tools` agent path (so the backlog's "#1 --with-tools RGV" was already delivered ŌĆö verified, not rebuilt), and it scored against `scoredMatches` = notes + cited-note augmentation + structured data (contacts/tasks/events/episodes/memory/feeds). But it had NO access to what the AGENT retrieved via web_search / non-note tools, so a correct web answer ("The capital of France is Paris") scored ~zero coverage against the notes-only evidence and tripped the "ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ this answer's claims aren't fully backed by your notes ŌĆö treat as unverified" warning ŌĆö a deterministic false-positive on the exact surface where a spurious "I'm not sure" erodes trust worst. Surfaced the agent's read-tool outputs end-to-end: added `groundingSources?: { source, text }[]` to `AgentRunResult` (packages/agent-core/src/types.ts); `createRunResult` (runtime-internals.ts) now derives them from `execution.toolResults` (each tool's non-empty text output, capped at 4000 chars so a large web page can't bloat the reverify prompt; empty outputs like an actuator's "sent" are skipped) and `agent-runtime.ts` passes `execution.toolResults` through at the main call site; the `muse ask --with-tools` path (commands-ask.ts) captures `result.groundingSources` and adds them to the verdict's `scoredMatches` as `tool: <name>` evidence (cosine 1 ŌĆö the agent deliberately fetched them, so the verdict rests on COVERAGE). Still fabrication-safe: ONLY real tool outputs are added, so a claim backed by NEITHER the notes NOR any tool result stays uncovered ŌåÆ ungrounded (the zero-fabrication property is preserved ŌĆö this only PREVENTS a false "ungrounded", never causes a false "grounded"). Proof: 3 new deterministic tests (no live model) ŌĆö `createRunResult` derives `groundingSources` from a web_search tool's text output and SKIPS an empty actuator output, and omits the field entirely on a chat-only / actuator-only run (packages/agent-core/test/runtime-internals.test.ts); and `groundingVerdictNotice` WARNS on "The capital of France is Paris" against notes-only evidence but is SILENT once the agent's web-tool output is in the evidence set (apps/cli/src/commands-ask-grounding-verdict.test.ts) ŌĆö plus the full @muse/agent-core suite (112 files / 1412 tests) + @muse/cli suite (169 files / 1839 tests) green, agent-core + cli tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE regression touch: `pnpm eval:self-improving` 18/18 batteries green on local Ollama qwen3:8b (cited-recall / recall-citation-gate / rubric-gate / faithfulness / claim-grounding / reflection + council RGV all still pass ŌĆö the additive `groundingSources` field regressed nothing and the default chat path is unchanged). agent-core 112 files / 1412 tests + cli 169 files / 1839 tests + eval:self-improving 18/18 + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö the `--with-tools` agent answer is now verified against the evidence the agent actually used, completing "one grounding gate under EVERY surface" so a correct web answer no longer carries a spurious unverified warning ŌĆö grounding-edge false-positive fix (memory: project_small_model_maximization)
- [Reliability/Actuation] A rate-limited Gmail send via `muse email send` (and the agent's email tool) now SURVIVES a 429 ŌĆö it retries honouring the server's Retry-After instead of dropping the email ŌĆö extending the safe all-actuator transient-retry to the flagship OUTBOUND actuator (P43-2, ACT axis; messaging + calendar already retried, email did not). `GmailEmailProvider.sendEmail` (packages/mcp/src/email-provider.ts) did a single POST and threw on any non-2xx ŌĆö it DELIBERATELY did not retry, because a send is non-idempotent (Gmail has no client idempotency key) and a retried POST could deliver the message twice (the irreversible harm `outbound-safety.md` guards). Refined that to the SAFE subset: a SEND now retries ONLY a 429 rate-limit, honouring Retry-After (parsed per RFC 7231 via the shared `parseRetryAfterMs`, clamped to 30s, else exponential backoff), because Gmail rejects a 429 BEFORE queuing the message ŌĆö nothing was delivered, so retrying cannot double-send; a 5xx OR a mid-flight network reject is AMBIGUOUS (the message may have been accepted) and is STILL never retried (the no-double-send guarantee is preserved), and a 401/403 auth error still fails fast. Reuses the provider's existing `retryOptions` (retries/baseDelayMs/sleep/maxRetryAfterMs) ŌĆö the same seam the idempotent read path uses ŌĆö so the read retry is untouched. Proof: 5 new contract-faithful tests (a real Gmail send fake that routes only messages/send, asserts the Bearer + POST, and COUNTS the POSTs so a double-send shows as an extra call; never a fake registry, per outbound-safety.md) in packages/mcp/src/email-provider.test.ts ŌĆö a 429+`Retry-After: 2` retries once and succeeds, sleeping exactly 2000ms (honoured the hint, not the 250ms backoff); a no-hint 429 falls back to 250ms backoff; a 503 is NEVER retried (single attempt ŌåÆ throws HTTP_503, no double-send); a network reject is never retried and a 403 fails in one attempt; the 429 budget exhausts to a thrown HTTP_429 after initial+2 retries (no infinite loop) ŌĆö plus the full @muse/mcp suite green (168 files / 1368 tests), mcp tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0. This is an HTTP-actuator reliability slice (no model), so the contract-faithful fake is the surface check, not smoke:live. mcp 168 files / 1368 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a user no longer loses an email to a transient Gmail rate-limit, with the irreversible double-send hazard fenced off by construction (429-only); P43-2 stays `[ ]` until home/web actuators reach retry parity + the plan-execute verify/replan loop carries a 2+-step task to a verified done through an injected failure ŌĆö P43-2 (ACT-axis actuator retry, email)
- [Reliability/Actuation] A Home Assistant action (lock the door, set the thermostat, turn off a light) via Muse now SURVIVES a transient 429 rate-limit ŌĆö the idempotent `call_service` retries honouring Retry-After instead of failing ŌĆö COMPLETING the all-actuator transient-retry the human focus named (messaging + calendar + email + home now retry; a non-idempotent web submit stays correctly single-shot), P43-2 ACT axis. The home WRITE path went through the shared `performWebActionWithApproval` executor (web-action.ts), which was deliberately single-shot ("No retry ŌĆö a retried POST can double-act") ŌĆö correct for a generic non-idempotent web submit (a booking/form), but it meant a Home Assistant `call_service` (which is IDEMPOTENT ŌĆö setting a state) also dropped on a transient 429. Added a `retryOn429?: boolean` option (default OFF) to the executor that, when set, retries ONLY a 429 rate-limit honouring Retry-After (parsed per RFC 7231, clamped 30s, else exponential backoff), wrapping ONLY the transmit ŌĆö the draft-first approval gate runs ONCE before the loop and a 429 retry NEVER re-approves; a 5xx OR a network/timeout reject is AMBIGUOUS (the action may have applied ŌĆö a toggle/script could have run) and is STILL never retried; the action log records the single FINAL outcome. `performHomeActionWithApproval` (smart-home.ts) sets `retryOn429: true` because a 429 is rejected by Home Assistant BEFORE the service executes (nothing happened, so a retry can't double-act) ŌĆö safe for every HA service including toggle/press. A generic web action leaves the flag off ŌåÆ its single-shot non-idempotent-safe behaviour is byte-unchanged. Proof: 5 new contract-faithful tests (real Response sequences, counting transmits so a double-act shows as an extra call, never a fake registry) ŌĆö in web-action.test.ts: `retryOn429` retries a 429+`Retry-After:2` then performs (sleeping 2000ms, approving ONCE), a 5xx is NEVER retried (single attempt), and WITHOUT the flag a 429 is single-shot (a web submit never auto-retries); in smart-home-action.test.ts: `performHomeActionWithApproval` survives a 429 (retries honouring Retry-After, approves once, performs) and does NOT retry a 5xx ŌĆö plus the full @muse/mcp suite green (168 files / 1373 tests, the existing single-shot 500/403 web-action tests UNCHANGED), mcp tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0. - [Self-improve/Autonomy] When you correct Muse about the SAME thing more than once, the unattended distiller now CONSOLIDATES it ŌĆö `muse learned` shows the lesson with a "raised N├Ś" badge instead of cluttering the bank with paraphrase duplicates ŌĆö and (the safety fix) a repeated correction NEVER silently graduates a guessed strategy into the injected `[Learned Strategies]` block; promotion stays bound to your explicit approval (P43-1 slice 3a, the SAFE consolidation half; ACT/self-improve axis). The idle distill consumer (`distillQueuedCorrections`) checked the suppressed-lessons veto but NOT the playbook bank ŌĆö `recordPlaybookStrategy` only dedups by `id`, so every re-derived lesson from a repeated correction wrote a fresh probation entry (paraphrases of one lesson piling up), and worse, N independent probation entries could EACH later graduate, amplifying a single guess. A 10-voter reassessment panel found the originally-held "graduate a probation strategy when a repeated correction matches it" design UNSAFE ŌĆö a repeated correction is a NEGATIVE signal (the attended path scores a correction DECAY ŌłÆ1, only an APPROVAL REINFORCE +1; `adjustPlaybookReward` graduates only on net-positive reward) and `strategyTextSimilarity` is CJK-aware Jaccard TOPIC-overlap (can't tell "use a warm sign-off" from "STOP using a warm sign-off"), so graduating on a repeat would INVERT the user's signal and autonomously inject a contradicted directive ŌĆö a fabrication-class regression on the action surface. Shipped the SAFE slice the panel ratified instead: (1) `bumpPlaybookObservation(file, id)` (personal-playbook-store.ts) increments a new `timesObserved` counter ONLY ŌĆö it deliberately does NOT touch `reward`, `probation`, or `lastReinforcedAt` (pure observability, sign-safe); (2) `distillQueuedCorrections` (distill-queue.ts), before recording, queries the user's bank and if a freshly-distilled lesson's `strategyTextSimilarity` to an existing entry is Ōēź `dedupThreshold` (default 0.7) it bumps that entry's observation count and SKIPS the duplicate write (no graduation); (3) `muse learned` (commands-learned.ts) renders ` ┬Ę raised N├Ś` on a probation strategy with `timesObserved Ōēź 2` so a repeatedly-raised point reads as worth reinforcing WITHOUT auto-promoting it. Graduation stays exactly where it was ŌĆö `adjustPlaybookReward` clearing probation on a POSITIVE user act (approval) ŌĆö untouched.
