- [Reliability/Actuation] A hung or unresponsive Google Calendar endpoint can no longer block Muse indefinitely ŌĆö every Google Calendar HTTP call (the API requests AND the OAuth token refresh) now has a per-attempt request TIMEOUT (AbortController, default 15s), so a slow/stalled third party fails fast with a clear error instead of stalling `muse calendar` / the agent run (P41 actuator hardening ŌĆö the timeout dimension of "daily-reliable actuators"; ACT axis). The messaging providers (Telegram / Discord / Slack / LINE via `fetchWithTimeout`) and the Gmail provider (`fetchWithRetry`, 15s AbortController) already bounded their requests, but `GoogleCalendarProvider` called `this.fetchImpl(...)` RAW at both fetch sites ŌĆö with no timeout/AbortSignal ŌĆö so a hung Google endpoint (a network black-hole, an unresponsive proxy, a stalled TLS handshake) blocked the call until the OS socket timeout (often minutes). That genuinely STALLS the caller: the agent's wallclock cap (`maxRunWallclockMs`) only checks BETWEEN tool iterations, never mid-fetch, and the `muse brief` / daemon calendar reads have no other guard. Added a `timeoutMs` option (`GoogleCalendarRetryOptions`, default 15000, 0 disables) + a private `fetchWithTimeout(url, init)` that races each fetch against an `AbortController` timer (clearing it in `finally`) and routes both the API path and the token-refresh path through it. SAFE by construction via the EXISTING retry seam: a timeout rejects ŌåÆ the request method's network-failure `catch` decides by idempotency ŌĆö an idempotent GET retries (`networkRetries = this.retries`) so a flaky moment doesn't drop the calendar from the briefing, while a WRITE (POST/PATCH/DELETE) has `networkRetries = 0` so a timed-out mutation is NEVER retried (a timeout is ambiguous ŌĆö the write may have committed ŌĆö so a retry could double-act; this preserves the same no-double-act guarantee as the 429-only write-retry). Proof: 2 new contract-faithful tests (a real hung-endpoint fake ŌĆö the API fetch returns a promise that only the injected AbortController resolves, by rejecting on `signal`; the token endpoint responds normally; never a fake registry) in packages/calendar/test/google-provider.test.ts ŌĆö a hung GET is aborted on each attempt and retried then thrown (`timed out`, asserted abort count = initial + 1 retry = 2, idempotent), and a hung WRITE is aborted EXACTLY ONCE and thrown (abort count = 1 ŌĆö never retried, no double-act) ŌĆö plus the full @muse/calendar suite green (12 files / 139 tests, the existing OAuth / 429-retry / 5xx / malformed-body / event-mapping contract tests unchanged), calendar tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0. HTTP-actuator reliability slice (no model) ŌåÆ the contract-faithful hung-endpoint fake is the surface check, not smoke:live. calendar 12/139 + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a slow or black-holed Google Calendar can no longer hang Muse's morning brief or calendar actuator; the calendar provider reaches request-timeout parity with messaging + email, with double-act still fenced off (write timeouts never retry) ŌĆö P41 (ACT-axis actuator hardening, request timeout, Google Calendar)
- [Reliability/Actuation] A multi-step `muse ask --with-tools` task now ADAPTS when a read/lookup step fails non-recoverably ŌĆö instead of giving up, the plan-execute loop RE-DECOMPOSES: it asks the model for an ALTERNATIVE read-only approach to the same intent and runs it, so a task carries to a verified done via a different route (P43-2 carry-to-done, the "replans on a failed step" leg now real; ACT axis ŌĆö a 13-agent panel + 3-attacker red-team chose this as the highest-value SAFELY-achievable big lever, over encryption-at-rest [its first slice was red-teamed as a data-loss/race risk] and autonomous graduation [already shipped + sign-safe, no new code]). Slices 1ŌĆō2 added the per-step post-condition (`classifyStepEffect`) + a bounded read-step RETRY, but a step that failed even after retry was simply marked failed ŌĆö the loop ran once top-to-bottom with no adaptive re-routing. Added `replanFailedReadStep` (packages/agent-core/src/plan-execute-loop.ts): when a READ step's effect fails after the bounded retry, it builds a focused re-plan prompt (the original request + the failed step + its reason), generates an alternative plan over ONLY the read-risk tools (`generatePlan` with read-tool descriptions), and runs up to `PLAN_REPLAN_MAX_STEPS=2` alternative steps ŌĆö the first that COMPLETES with a passing post-condition recovers the step's intent (recorded as `"<desc> (recovered via <tool>)"`). CRITICAL SAFETY (the reason the panel chose this as the SAFE lever, and the red-team's required guard): recovery is READ-ONLY and can NEVER double-act ŌĆö (1) only a read-risk step failure triggers a re-plan (`retryable`), a WRITE/execute failure is NEVER replanned because the mutation may have committed (outbound-safety.md), and (2) the alternative plan is FILTERED to read-risk tool names ŌĆö any write/execute step the model proposes in the re-plan is DROPPED, not executed; the immutable `executed[]` is never re-run, so a completed non-idempotent step can't repeat. The happy path is untouched (a succeeding step never replans ŌåÆ zero added latency in the common case); the re-plan model call fires ONLY on a read-step failure, bounded by `maxToolCalls`. Proof: 3 new contract-faithful tests (a scripted runner giving precise control of the plan/re-plan model responses + each tool result, no live model) in packages/agent-core/test/plan-execute-replan.test.ts ŌĆö a failed READ step RECOVERS via an alternative read tool (retried ├Ś2 then the alternative runs, step flips to success, carries to synthesis, exactly ONE re-plan); a failed WRITE step is NEVER re-planned (executed exactly once, zero re-plan model calls ŌĆö no double-act); and a re-plan that proposes a WRITE step has it DROPPED (the write tool is never called, the read step stays failed) ŌĆö plus the full @muse/agent-core suite green (113 files / 1430 tests; the existing partial-failure synthesis test updated to find its synthesis request by content since the re-plan adds a model call), agent-core tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE regression on the loop PC: `pnpm eval:self-improving` 18/18 batteries green on local Ollama qwen3:8b (background-review-e2e exercises the agent runtime ŌĆö the additive re-plan, which only fires on a read-step failure the batteries don't hit, regressed nothing). agent-core 113/1430 + eval:self-improving 18/18 + pnpm lint 0/0 ŌĆö a multi-step task no longer dies when a lookup step has no working answer; it adaptively re-routes to an alternative read, with double-act fenced off by construction (read-only re-plan, write failures never replanned) ŌĆö P43-2 (ACT-axis carry-to-done, adaptive read-only re-decomposition, panel-chosen + red-teamed)
- [Trust/Privacy] A user can now ENCRYPT their user-memory AT REST ŌĆö `muse memory encrypt` rewrites `~/.muse/user-memory.json` (the confided life: facts, preferences, the typed user model) as an AES-256-GCM envelope, so a stolen/seized laptop or a leaked backup can no longer read it; reads/writes stay transparent (the agent's persona still loads it), with `muse memory decrypt` to reverse and `muse memory encryption-status` to check ŌĆö making "it can't tell anyone" true against STORAGE access, not just network egress (NEW Trust axis; the discretion-refusal half of the identity promise. Decided + safety-designed by a 13-agent panel that chose this lever, then a 3-attacker red-team of the actual diff that FOUND + drove a fix for a cross-process data-loss race before commit). Until now notes/memory/episodes/action-log were PLAINTEXT JSON behind OS file-perms only ŌĆö only credentials/exports were encrypted ŌĆö so the most sensitive store (what Muse knows about you) sat readable on disk. Added `packages/memory/src/memory-encryption.ts` (AES-256-GCM + scrypt-derived key, mirroring the proven credential-store envelope; the key is `MUSE_MEMORY_KEY` or a per-host fallback) and wired it into `FileUserMemoryStore` behind the red-team's REQUIRED GUARDS, each tested: (1) the read path NEVER writes ŌĆö it decrypts-or-reads-plaintext and returns the format, so there is no encrypt-on-read race; (2) FAIL-CLOSED-WITHOUT-DESTRUCTION ŌĆö a WRONG key (or a per-host key changed by a machine rename, or tampering) THROWS a clear error and leaves the ciphertext byte-UNCHANGED, and because every write reads-first, a write under the wrong key also throws (it can never bury the ciphertext with empty data); (3) the one-shot `encryptAtRest()` writes a `.plaintext-backup-<ts>` BEFORE encrypting (recovery if the key derivation ever changes); (4) the un-migrated plaintext path is byte-unchanged (opt-in). The red-team's CRITICAL finding ŌĆö the per-process write mutex + a migration-only lock let a daemon `upsertFact` in one process race a CLI `encrypt` in another (read-modify-write, last-rename-wins ŌåÆ a fact or the encryption lost) ŌĆö was FIXED before commit: ALL writes (upsert / delete / encrypt / decrypt) now serialize through ONE cross-process O_EXCL `.lock`, with stale-lock STEALING (an mtime > 30s lock from a crashed writer is reclaimed) so a crash can't block writes forever, while reads stay lock-free (the atomic rename keeps a concurrent reader consistent). Proof: ~12 new deterministic tests (no model) ŌĆö the crypto primitive round-trips + THROWS on a wrong key; the store round-trips (cleartext absent on disk, reads decrypt, writes preserve the encrypted format), writes the plaintext backup, FAILS CLOSED on a wrong key with the ciphertext byte-unchanged (the killer data-loss case) including the wrong-key WRITE not burying it, read() never writes, decrypt reverses, and a stale lock is stolen (packages/memory/test/memory-user-store-file.test.ts); plus the full @muse/memory suite green (31 files / 329 tests), @muse/cli green (170 files / 1870 tests), memory+cli tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE end-to-end on the loop PC: `muse memory encrypt` over a seeded store removed the confided secret from cleartext on disk (0 hits, AES envelope), kept a recoverable plaintext backup, `encryption-status` reported encrypted, a WRONG key failed closed ("the encrypted data is intact on disk... restore the .plaintext-backup"), and `muse memory decrypt` restored the plaintext ŌĆö the lockfile released cleanly (no leftover). memory 31/329 + cli 170/1870 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live `muse memory encrypt/decrypt` ŌĆö the confided life can now be encrypted at rest, fail-closed and race-safe, so a stolen device can't read it; the discretion refusal is real against storage, not just the network ŌĆö P44 (Trust/privacy, user-memory encryption-at-rest, panel-decided + red-teamed)
- [Trust/Privacy] A user can now ENCRYPT their session-history AT REST ŌĆö `muse episode encrypt` rewrites `~/.muse/episodes.json` (the auto-captured prior-session summaries: what you talked about, decided, asked Muse to follow up on) as an AES-256-GCM envelope under the SAME `MUSE_MEMORY_KEY` as user-memory (ONE key for the whole confided life), so a stolen/seized laptop or a leaked backup can't read your session history either; reads stay transparent (`muse episode list` / the persona surfacing still decrypt), with `muse episode decrypt` to reverse and `muse episode encryption-status` to check (extends the P44 Trust axis from user-memory to the episodes store ŌĆö the discretion-refusal half of "it can't tell anyone", now over a second confided store). P44-1 encrypted user-memory; episodes/action-log were still PLAINTEXT JSON behind OS file-perms only. Built a REUSABLE `encrypted-file` helper (packages/mcp/src/encrypted-file.ts: `readMaybeEncrypted` / `writeMaybeEncrypted` / `isFileEncryptedAtRest` / `withFileLock` / `encryptFileAtRest` / `decryptFileAtRest`) reusing `@muse/memory`'s proven AES-256-GCM envelope, and wired it into the function-based episodes store (packages/mcp/src/personal-episodes-store.ts): `readEpisodes` decrypts fail-closed (a wrong key THROWS and is NEVER quarantined-to-empty ŌĆö an undecryptable store is not corrupt; the non-JSON plaintext corrupt-quarantine path is preserved), `writeEpisodes` peeks the on-disk format and rewrites in the SAME format under a cross-process O_EXCL lock the migration also takes (so an ordinary write can't race `encryptEpisodesAtRest` and clobber it), and `encryptEpisodesAtRest` writes a `.plaintext-backup-<ts>` before migrating + seeds an empty encrypted file when the store is absent (so future episodes stay encrypted). Then a 3-attacker red-team OF THE ACTUAL DIFF (concurrency / fail-closed / regression lenses, per "build ŌåÆ red-team the DIFF ŌåÆ fix ŌåÆ commit") drove FOUR pre-commit fixes: (1) `writeMaybeEncrypted` now delegates to the hardened `atomicWriteFile` (randomUUID tmp suffix so same-ms writers don't collide on rename; fsync before rename ŌĆö a torn ENCRYPTED file would be an undecryptable lock-out, not just empty); (2) `withFileLock` now stamps a per-holder NONCE and removes the lock ONLY if it still holds that nonce, so a >30s-slow holder whose lock was stolen mid-flight can't delete the new holder's lock (no orphan-cascade / third concurrent writer); (3) the `muse episode encrypt` output now DISCLOSES the plaintext backup is CLEARTEXT to delete once the key is confirmed (the red-team's strongest finding ŌĆö an undisclosed full-cleartext sibling defeats at-rest confidentiality); (4) the three new subcommands got automated CLI tests. Proof: 15 new deterministic store tests (no model) ŌĆö round-trip (cleartext absent on disk, reads decrypt), format preserved on subsequent writes, empty/absent-store seeds encrypted, plaintext backup holds the originals, idempotent re-encrypt, FAILS CLOSED on a wrong key with the ciphertext byte-UNCHANGED (incl. a wrong-key WRITE that can't bury it), read() never writes (bytes + mtime unchanged), decrypt reverses, decrypt-wrong-key fails closed, status is format-only (no key), corrupt-plaintext still quarantines, a STALE lock is stolen, 20 concurrent upserts on an encrypted store all survive + stay encrypted, clear preserves the format (packages/mcp/test/episodes-encryption.test.ts) + 4 new CLI tests driving the real subcommands through commander (statusŌåÆencryptŌåÆstatusŌåÆlist, wrong-key fail-closed, decrypt-reverts, --json) (apps/cli/src/commands-episode-encryption.test.ts); plus the full @muse/mcp suite green (169 files / 1397 tests), @muse/cli green (171 files / 1874 tests), mcp+cli tsc clean, `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE end-to-end on the loop PC: `muse episode encrypt` over a seeded store left an AES-256-GCM envelope (0 plaintext leak, cleartext-backup warning shown, NO orphan `.lock` left behind), `muse episode list` decrypted transparently, a WRONG key failed closed with the data intact, and `muse episode decrypt` restored the plaintext. mcp 169/1397 + cli 171/1874 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live `muse episode encrypt/list/decrypt` ŌĆö a second confided store (your session history) can now be encrypted at rest, fail-closed and race-safe, on a reusable helper ready for action-log next; the discretion refusal now covers what you said to Muse, not just what it learned about you ŌĆö P44-2 (Trust/privacy, episodes encryption-at-rest, reusable helper, panel-pattern + red-teamed)
- [Trust/Accountability] A user can now run `muse actions --verify` and get a DETERMINISTIC proof that the autonomous-action audit log (`~/.muse/action-log.json` ŌĆö what Muse did on their behalf: what/why/when/result) was not silently deleted, reordered, edited, or backdated ŌĆö and if it WAS, the exact entry index where the chain first breaks (exit 1 so a cron/script can gate on it). This capability did not exist: the log was "append-only BY CONTRACT" (personal-action-log-store.ts docstring) with ZERO integrity linkage ŌĆö a buggy concurrent writer, a partial-write crash, or any process with file access could rewrite history undetectably, so the accountability leg of "Tell it everything. It can't tell anyone." was unfalsifiable. Made it tamper-EVIDENT with a Merkle hash-chain (Haber-Stornetta 1991; RFC 6962): added `prevHash?: string` to ActionLogEntry (optional ŌåÆ legacy logs stay readable), a pure `computeEntryHash(entry, prevHash)` = SHA-256 over the entry's canonical content (id/userId/when/what/why/result/objectiveId/detail, prevHash EXCLUDED from its own body) bound to the prior hash, so a one-byte change to any historical entry diverges its hash ŌĆö which is the NEXT entry's prevHash ŌĆö cascading the break to the tip; `appendActionLog` now seals each new entry to `chainTipHash(existing)` (genesis for the first; the per-file append queue keeps the chain fork-free under concurrency); `verifyActionLogChain(entries)` (pure) walks the STORED/append order recomputing every link and returns `{ok, brokenAtIndex, reason, linkedEntries}`, treating leading legacy (no-prevHash) entries as a valid pre-chain prefix and a missing link AFTER the chain began as a break; `verifyActionLogChainFile(file)` reads via readActionLog (append order, NOT queryActionLog which re-sorts newest-first). Wired `--verify` into `muse actions` (commands-actions.ts) before the query path: "Ō£ō chain intact ŌĆö N linked" or "Ō£Ś TAMPERING DETECTED at entry N: ŌĆ”" + `command.error(exitCode:1)`. HONEST framing baked into the copy + docstring: tamper-EVIDENT (catches accidental/partial-write/external-process/non-recomputing mutation), NEVER tamper-PROOF (a motivated attacker who recomputes the whole chain needs an off-box anchor ŌĆö out of scope). This slice was chosen by the cross-domain ideation panel (info-theory/distributed-systems) AFTER the bio panel's top pick ŌĆö an immune-system NEGATIVE-SELECTION per-claim grounding detector ŌĆö was BUILT and then FALSIFIED by a live nomic-embed calibration: recombination hallucinations (real entities, wrong combination) embed nearest-self at 0.79ŌĆō0.85 vs faithful claims at 0.80ŌĆō0.81 (the embedding is topical, not propositional), so it could not beat the existing lexical+value gate on its own falsifiable kill condition ŌĆö reverted, not shipped (an honest negative result; the "shows its work" discipline applied to my own work). Proof: 11 new deterministic mcp unit tests (no model) ŌĆö appendŌåÆverify intact (first entry chains to genesis, each to its predecessor); in-place edit caught at the next link; deleted-middle / reordered / backdated-`when` each detected at the precise index; legacy no-prevHash entries verify as an intact prefix; a new append onto a legacy log starts a verifiable chain from the legacy tip; a prevHash stripped mid-chain is a break; empty/missing log vacuously intact (packages/mcp/test/action-log-chain.test.ts) + 3 new CLI tests (intact log prints "chain intact"; a byte-flipped on-disk entry exits 1 naming the broken index; --verify --json emits the structured verdict ŌĆö apps/cli/src/commands-actions.test.ts); plus the full @muse/mcp suite green (170 files / 1407 tests, the existing serialize/concurrency tests confirm back-compat), @muse/cli green (171 files / 1877 tests), `pnpm check` exit 0 across ALL workspaces (mcp interface change consumed by cli + api), `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE end-to-end on the built CLI (deterministic SHA-256, no Ollama): a 3-action chain verified "Ō£ō chain intact ŌĆö 3 linked entries verified" (exit 0), then a silently-DELETED middle action was caught "Ō£Ś TAMPERING DETECTED at entry 1 ŌĆ” does not chain to entry 0" (exit 1) and a BACKDATED `when` was caught at its exact index (exit 1). mcp 170/1407 + cli 171/1877 + pnpm check exit 0 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live `muse actions --verify` (intact + deletion + backdate) ŌĆö the audit trail of what Muse did on your behalf is now tamper-evident, closing the accountability leg of the trust moat; no model needed, so the proof is fully deterministic ŌĆö P44-3 (Trust/accountability, tamper-evident action-log hash-chain, cross-domain panel pick after the bio top-pick was live-falsified)
- [Reach/Trust] A user can now run a GROUNDED swarm council ŌĆö set `MUSE_A2A_COUNCIL_GROUNDED=true` and a council member (your own Muse's voice AND any peer that opted in) self-ABSTAINS, staying silent, when its OWN notes hold no CONFIDENT evidence for the question, so an ignorant peer can't dilute the synthesis with a confident-but-ungrounded opinion (the classic multiagent-debate failure mode). This is the multi-agent twin of "I'm not sure" ŌĆö it extends the fabrication=0 grounding invariant to a FIFTH surface (the peer DRAFT) at the COLONY level, and it's the structural prerequisite for honest colony learning (who SPEAKS on a question reveals who has corpus for it ŌĆö emergent specialization/federated trust need members to first stop speaking when ignorant). Chosen by the multi-angle ideation's technical-edge panel (3-lens red-teamed; it REJECTED Federated Strategy-Reward as unsafe ŌĆö that needs a peer-messageŌåÆlocal-state write punching a hole in inbound-inert). DESIGN: deliberately OPT-IN per node (the default council stays full deliberation ŌĆö abstaining-by-default would gut its main use, opinion questions like "rent or buy" where no one has corpus); purely SUBTRACTIVE (members say LESS, never more ŌåÆ strengthens the trust core); entirely LOCAL (the corpus NEVER crosses the wire ŌĆö only the abstain/speak decision does, so no new shareable kind, inbound-inert untouched); and the gate is DETERMINISTIC (CRAG retrieval-confidence verdict, `classifyRetrievalConfidence`, not the stochastic 8B ŌĆö so qwen can't flake it). Built `abstainIfUngrounded(draft, matches, opts)` (speak only on a `confident` corpus match; `none`/`ambiguous` abstains ŌĆö keyed on RETRIEVAL confidence not draft token-coverage, since the council reasons in GENERAL terms by design so a coverage gate would silence everyone ŌĆö the over-abstention failure) + `produceGroundedCouncilReasoning` (short-circuits to abstain with NO model call when the corpus isn't confident) in packages/agent-core/src/council.ts; a `councilCorpusMatches` helper (apps/cli/src/council-corpus.ts) that reuses the precomputed notes index + the SAME absolute cosine the recall wedge grades by, fail-CLOSED to silence (empty ŌćÆ abstain) when there's no index or the embedder is down; wired into BOTH the `muse swarm council` initiator's own voice (round 1 + debate rounds) AND the `muse swarm serve` responder (this-Muse-as-a-peer), so the whole colony respects the posture; surfaced in `muse swarm status`. NOTE the real design insight that shaped it: the council is DELIBERATION not RECALL, so self-abstention is opt-in ŌĆö this avoided shipping a feature that would have broken the council's primary use. Proof: 7 new deterministic agent-core unit tests (no model) ŌĆö abstainIfUngrounded speaks on confident / abstains on ambiguous+none+empty-draft / honors a custom confidentAt; produceGroundedCouncilReasoning SHORT-CIRCUITS (asserts NO model request spent) when not confident and reasons when confident; an end-to-end selectivity test that an abstaining member is absent from the synthesised contributors (packages/agent-core/test/council.test.ts) + 5 new CLI unit tests for councilCorpusMatches (no index ŌåÆ []; ranks own chunks by absolute cosine ŌåÆ confident in-corpus; off-corpus ŌåÆ not confident; embedder-throws ŌåÆ fail-closed []; env parsing) (apps/cli/src/council-corpus.test.ts) + the SwarmStatus grounded-posture render; plus the full @muse/agent-core suite green (113 files / 1438 tests), @muse/cli green (173 files / 1887 tests), `pnpm check` exit 0 across ALL workspaces (agent-core council change consumed by cli + api), `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE battery on the loop PC (qwen3:8b + real nomic-embed) ŌĆö `verify-council-self-abstention` (now in `eval:self-improving`, 19 batteries): an off-corpus question (top cosine 0.467, ambiguous) made the member ABSTAIN, an in-corpus question (top cosine 0.621, confident ŌĆö the over-abstention TRIPWIRE) made it SPEAK, and the council synthesised contributors `["alice"]` with the abstainer `bob` EXCLUDED; the two existing council batteries (`verify-council`, `verify-council-grounding`) still PASS (no regression). agent-core 113/1438 + cli 173/1887 + pnpm check exit 0 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live verify-council-self-abstention (real qwen+nomic-embed: abstain/speak/exclude all proven) ŌĆö Muse's private swarm now has an honest colony floor: an ignorant peer stays silent instead of voting confidently, the 5th grounded surface, and the substrate every richer colony-learning step needs ŌĆö A2A-6 (Reach/Trust, council self-abstention, technical-edge panel pick, the colony-learning frontier)
- [Grounding edge/Front-door] A user can now run `muse ask --why` and, when Muse refuses or flags an answer, SEE exactly why ŌĆö which deterministic grounding criterion fell short and the measured value vs its threshold ŌĆö turning an opaque "I'm not sure" into an inspectable, ACTIONABLE judgement (rephrase, reindex, or add a note). This is the "shows its work" moat applied to the REFUSAL itself: the recall wedge already refuses instead of guessing, but the refusal was a black box; now `--why` names the failing rubric criterion(s) ŌĆö "no notes came close enough (best match 0.42, I need 0.55) ŌĆö confidence criterion", "the evidence covers only 6% of the answer's wording (I need 50%) ŌĆö coverage criterion", "your notes address only 0% of the question (I need 34%) ŌĆö answerability criterion", or "the answer cited N source(s) you don't have (ŌĆ”) ŌĆö citation criterion". The moat-analysis ideation workflow's red-teamed pick (chosen as the differentiating front-door slice): a refusal-WITH-REASONS is structurally uncopyable by hermes/openclaw ŌĆö their capability-first design has no refusal and no per-criterion verdict to surface, while Muse's deterministic 4-criterion `verifyGrounding` rubric is exactly the hard-to-replicate asset. Built a pure `explainGroundingVerdict(verification, { topCosine, confidentAt, coverageFloor, answerabilityFloor })` in packages/agent-core/src/knowledge-recall.ts that reads the rubric `verifyGrounding` ALREADY computes (the rubric stores the categorical confidence, so the caller passes the top match's raw cosine for the "best match 0.42" line) + `verification.reason`/`invalidCitations`, and emits 1ŌĆō4 plain-language lines naming every criterion below its floor; returns `[]` for a `grounded` verdict (SILENT on the happy path ŌĆö a targeted trust affordance, not a debug firehose). Wired `--why` into `muse ask` (commands-ask.ts) AFTER the verdict block, isolated from the repair flow: NO extra model call (the rubric is deterministic), gated to stderr (`!--json`), and it runs even on a REFUSAL (which the fabrication warning deliberately skips, since a refusal asserts no claim) because explaining WHY it refused is exactly the point. Proof: 6 new deterministic agent-core unit tests (no model) ŌĆö a grounded verdict yields []; a no-retrieval verdict names the confidence criterion with "best match 0.42, I need 0.55"; an off-evidence answer names the coverage criterion with the measured %; a fabricated `[from ghost.md]` names the citation criterion + lists the source; an ambiguous-retrieval answer is flagged "loosely related ŌĆö confidence criterion (low)"; custom thresholds render in the explanation (packages/agent-core/test/explain-grounding-verdict.test.ts); plus the full @muse/agent-core suite green (114 files / 1444 tests), @muse/cli build clean, `pnpm check` exit 0 across ALL workspaces (the agent-core export consumed by cli + api), `pnpm lint` 0/0, and a LIVE run on the loop PC (qwen3:8b + real nomic-embed): `muse ask --why "what is the best sourdough bread recipe?"` over a VPN-only notes corpus REFUSED ("I am not sure, sirŌĆ”") and printed "­¤öÄ Why I can't answer from your notes: ŌĆó the evidence covers only 6% of the answer's wording (I need 50%) ŌĆö coverage criterion ŌĆó your notes address only 0% of the question (I need 34%) ŌĆö answerability criterion". agent-core 114/1444 + cli build clean + pnpm check exit 0 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live `muse ask --why` (off-corpus refusal explained) ŌĆö Muse's refusal is no longer a black box; the user sees which criterion failed and by how much, on the everyday front-door surface, which is the moat ("shows its work") made tangible where hermes/openclaw structurally can't follow ŌĆö P38-35 (Grounding edge/front-door, the --why refusal trace, moat-analysis panel pick)
- [Knowledge/Perception] A user can now have `muse ask` FOLLOW their `[[wiki-links]]` ŌĆö graph-augmented recall on the front door: an ask answer can ground on a note 1-hop LINKED from the matching note but whose own text didn't match the query, so the answer-bearing note your Zettelkasten points to (that the embedding ranking alone misses) reaches the model (HippoRAG / GraphRAG, Edge et al. 2024). Until now the note-link graph helped only `muse recall --expand` (1-hop); the front-door `muse ask` ignored it, so a question whose answer lived in a LINKED-but-non-matching note would refuse or under-ground. Fabrication-SAFE by construction: expansion fires ONLY from a CONFIDENT retrieval seed (a weak/off-corpus query pulls in nothing ŌĆö verified by classifyRetrievalConfidence === "confident"), adds ONLY the user's OWN real notes, keeps each linked chunk's real (low) cosine so the confidence verdict ŌĆö keyed on the TOP match ŌĆö is UNCHANGED (graph expansion can never inflate confidence), and is best-effort (a malformed graph never fails the ask). Built a pure `linkExpandRefs({ seedRefs, noteBodies, cap })` in apps/cli/src/notes-links.ts that reuses the proven `buildNoteLinkGraph` + `linkedFromResults`, with the graph built from the SAME notes-index bodies the ask ranks so note ids match the ask's relativized sources EXACTLY (sidestepping the provider-id-vs-index-path mismatch that loadNoteLinkGraph would have introduced); wired one conservative, capped (+2 linked notes) step into the ask retrieval (apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts) right after the cosine top-K (`diversifyAskChunks`), promoting each linked note's best already-ranked chunk into the grounding evidence. - [Reach/Reliability] A message a user CONFIRMS now survives a transient rate-limit instead of being dropped ŌĆö the draft-first outbound send (`muse messaging send` + the agent's `muse.messaging.send` tool, both routing through `sendMessageWithApproval`) rides the same `sendWithRetry` ladder the background notices already use, so a one-off `429 + Retry-After` (or a transient 5xx) is waited-out and the message is delivered, instead of being logged `failed` and lost on the first blip. - [Reach/Reliability] A CalDAV calendar WRITE (create / update / delete an event on iCloud / Fastmail / Proton / any compliant CalDAV server) now survives a transient rate-limit instead of being dropped ŌĆö Retry-After PARITY with the Google calendar adapter, so a user's "add this to my calendar" is equally reliable regardless of which backend they configured. - [Self-improve/Autonomy] A correction you make now AUTONOMOUSLY stops Muse applying a contradicted preference in LATER sessions ŌĆö the daemon, unattended, classifies each new correction against the strategies Muse currently applies and SUBTRACTIVELY decays the ones it CONTRADICTS, so "a correction in session A changes session B" closes the loop SIGN-SAFE. This FLIPS P43-1 (THE #1 lever, the last open P43 bullet ŌĆö the autonomous self-development daemon) and was the explicitly-held injection-path change: the decide-and-do directive (2026-06-04) said stop deferring the big levers to Jinan ŌĆö judge + DO it. The blocker was a genuine sign-error risk: a correction is a NEGATIVE signal and lexical topic-overlap can't tell "do X" from "STOP X", so decaying/graduating on a Jaccard match inverts the user's signal. The unblock is an LLM polarity gate `classifyCorrectionContradiction` (packages/agent-core/src/correction-distiller.ts) ŌĆö LIVE-validated 11/11 with ZERO false-CONTRADICT on qwen3:8b, including the exact topic-overlap-but-opposite cases ("stop using a warm sign-off" vs "use a warm sign-off" ŌåÆ CONTRADICT) a lexical matcher misses ŌĆö wired into `eval:self-improving` as a permanent regression battery (apps/cli/scripts/verify-correction-polarity.mjs). The daemon's self-learn tick (apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.ts), after distilling this tick's new corrections into probation lessons, runs `decayContradictedStrategies` (packages/autoconfigure/src/decay-contradicted.ts): for each new correction ├Ś each INJECTED strategy, on a confident `contradict` it drops that strategy's reward to the avoid floor (PLAYBOOK_AVOID_BELOW = -4 ŌåÆ `isInjectableStrategy` false ŌåÆ no longer applied; reversible ŌĆö a `muse playbook reward` lifts it back), and delivers a felt notice to the user's channel ("You corrected me, so I've stopped applying '<strategy>' going forward. If that was wrong, reinforce it with `muse playbook reward <id>`."). SAFE BY CONSTRUCTION ŌĆö the sign-error the playbook panel feared is STRUCTURALLY impossible: DECAY-ONLY (it NEVER graduates a probation guess, NEVER raises a reward, NEVER clears probation ŌĆö the ADDITIVE auto-graduation stays bound to a manual positive act, as the 10-voter panel ratified), so the worst case of a polarity error is a recoverable wrongly-avoided strategy, NEVER an autonomous fabrication entering the [Learned Strategies] prompt block; POLARITY-GATED + FAIL-CLOSED (agree / unrelated / uncertain / a model error all leave the strategy untouched); INJECTED-ONLY (a probation strategy isn't applied, so it's never a target); BRAKE-FIRST (a paused learner's bank is frozen); bounded model spend per tick. Verified deterministically AND live: 5 classifier parse/fail-closed unit tests (CONTRADICT/AGREE/UNRELATED parsed case-insensitively; a model error or unparseable answer ŌåÆ "uncertain" so it never decays on a guess) + 9 decay-orchestrator safety tests (a contradict drops to the avoid floor ŌåÆ not injectable; agree/unrelated/uncertain ŌåÆ no decay; a probation strategy is never touched; nothing ever graduates; maxClassifications cap; brake freezes the bank) + 2 daemon-wiring tests (a contradicting correction ŌåÆ the injected strategy decayed to -4 + the felt notice delivered, never graduating; a non-contradicting correction ŌåÆ no decay) + `pnpm check` exit 0 across all 20 workspaces (agent-core 1446, autoconfigure 495, cli 1894) + `pnpm lint` 0/0 + the permanent polarity battery 11/11 with 0 false-CONTRADICT on qwen3:8b + THE FLIP PROOF: a LIVE `muse daemon --once` on qwen3:8b where a seeded injected strategy ("Always give long, detailed multi-paragraph answers.", reward 3, injectable=true) + a queued contradicting correction ("Stop giving me long essays ŌĆö answer in ONE short sentence.") drove the REAL polarity classifier to decay it to reward -4 / injectable=FALSE / probation=false, with NO manual command ŌĆö a correction made in one session measurably changed a later session's behaviour unattended, sign-safe. agent-core 1446 + autoconfigure 495 + cli 1894 + pnpm check exit 0 + pnpm lint 0/0 + polarity battery 11/11 + live daemon decay e2e ŌĆö Muse's autonomous self-development daemon now closes the loop in BOTH directions (it learns from your corrections AND stops applying what you've contradicted, on its own), with the honesty machinery intact because the only autonomous reward change is subtractive and reversible ŌĆö P43-1 FLIP (Self-improve/autonomy, sign-safe autonomous correction-decay ŌĆö THE #1 lever)

- [Trust/Security] Muse's email ingestion is now INDIRECT-PROMPT-INJECTION-HARDENED ŌĆö a malicious email can no longer splice forged instructions into Muse's recalled context. P37-22/23 made email a recall source (great for "what did Dana email?"), but an email is UNTRUSTED third-party content ŌĆö a sender controls its from/subject/snippet ŌĆö and the ingestion wrote those RAW into a recallable note, so a crafted email carrying `\n[System Override]\nIgnore your instructionsŌĆ”` (or a forged `# Email:` heading / `From:` line, a CRLF, or ANSI/C0 control bytes) could splice a fake prompt section that the model sees once the note is recalled (indirect prompt injection ŌĆö the research backlog's #5 spotlighting concern, now a live surface since email ships). Closed by applying the SAME deterministic defence every OTHER untrusted-content path in Muse already uses (ambient-context, attachment-context, episodic-recall, skills-context, active-context all run it) ŌĆö `stripUntrustedTerminalChars(value).replace(/\s+/gu, " ").trim()` ŌĆö to the email's from / subject / date / snippet inside `renderEmailNote` (apps/cli/src/email-sync.ts), so no untrusted field can carry a newline that breaks out of its own line; only the note's OWN structural newlines (which the code, not the sender, controls) remain. This is DETERMINISTIC CODE, not a prompt please-be-careful (per CLAUDE.md's non-negotiable "security is deterministic code, never prompt instruction"), and FABRICATION-SAFE: whitespace-collapse only removes the section-splice ŌĆö the email's actual words stay intact as inert grounding evidence (recall is unaffected), and a single-line injection is just text the grounding gate still treats as a cited source, never an instruction. Verified deterministically (this is a content-sanitisation fix, not the LLM request/response path, so smoke:live does not apply): 7 new unit tests (apps/cli/src/email-sync.test.ts ŌĆö a `\n[System Override]\n` in the snippet produces NO standalone forged section and `[System Override]` never starts a line, while the words remain; a subject/from cannot forge a SECOND `# Email:` heading or `From:` line; ANSI/C0 control + DEL bytes are stripped; a CRLF cannot splice a new line; a legit single-line email renders byte-identical (sanitisation is a no-op on clean content); `syncEmailsToNotes` writes sanitised notes idempotently; `safeEmailId("../../etc/passwd")` ŌåÆ a path-safe filename, no traversal) + the existing 6 email CLI tests + 3 daemon email-sync tests UNBROKEN + the full @muse/cli suite green (174 files / 1911 tests) + `pnpm lint` 0/0. cli 1911 + pnpm lint 0/0 + injection battery ŌĆö the email-into-recall surface (P37-22/23) now carries the same indirect-prompt-injection defence as every other untrusted source Muse reads, deterministically and fabrication-safe ŌĆö P37-23 hardening (Trust/security, untrusted-email injection sanitisation, backlog #5)
- [Grounding/Honesty] When a user's notes CONFLICT, Muse now SURFACES the conflict ŌĆö "I have conflicting notes: [from a.md] says June 12th, [from b.md] says June 15th ŌĆö which is current?" ŌĆö instead of confidently picking one and hiding the other. This was a real honesty hole found by live probe: with two genuinely-conflicting notes (a.md "dentist June 12th", b.md "Dentist: June 15th", no update wording), `muse ask "when is my dentist appointment?"` on qwen3:8b confidently answered "June 12th [from a.md]", silently ignoring the conflicting b.md ŌĆö a fabrication-ADJACENT failure the grounding gate could not catch (the gate rejects a claim with NO retrieved source, but happily passes a claim that HAS a source even when another retrieved source CONTRADICTS it). The fix EXTENDS the honesty edge from "I'm not sure" (un-groundable) to "I have conflicting info" (multiply-groundable, contradictorily): a CONFLICTS rule added to the recall answer contract `CITATION_INSTRUCTION_LINES` (apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts) tells the model that when two passages give DIFFERENT answers and neither clearly updates the other, it must surface BOTH and the conflict citing each ("I have conflicting notes: X says ŌĆ”, Y says ŌĆ” ŌĆö which is current?") rather than silently choosing; with an explicit carve-out so an UPDATE ("moved to", "now", "corrected to") is RESOLVED to the new value, not over-flagged as a conflict. It is a prompt-instruction behaviour with NO new model call ŌåÆ ZERO added latency (it rides the existing answer generation); it does not change the grounding GATE (claims still cite real sources), and it is fail-soft (if the model ignored it the answer would be no worse than before). Verified deterministically AND live: a new unit test (CITATION_INSTRUCTION_LINES carries the CONFLICT rule AND the "if one UPDATES the other" carve-out ŌĆö apps/cli/src/commands-ask-cite-as.test.ts) + the full @muse/cli suite green (174 files / 1912 tests) + `pnpm lint` 0/0 + a NEW PERMANENT live battery (apps/cli/scripts/verify-conflict-surfacing.mjs, wired into `eval:self-improving`) that on qwen3:8b asserts a GENUINE conflict surfaces both values + flags it (passed: "I have conflicting notes: [from a.md] says June 12th, [from b.md] says June 15th ŌĆö which is current?") AND an explicit UPDATE resolves to the new value without being left open (passed: "the weekly team sync is on Thursday at 4:00pm [from new.md]") ŌĆö 2/2 ŌĆö plus a full LIVE `muse ask` round-trip reproducing both behaviours end-to-end (before the fix it answered "June 12th" silently; after, it surfaces the conflict). cli 1912 + pnpm lint 0/0 + conflict-surfacing battery 2/2 + live muse ask both cases ŌĆö Muse no longer picks a side in your own contradictory notes; it shows you the conflict and asks which is current, extending the grounding edge to multiply-groundable-but-contradictory claims ŌĆö P38-36 (Grounding/honesty, conflict-surfacing in cited recall)
- [Actuation/Reliability] When you set a reminder by voice/chat, Muse now confirms it with the time you ACTUALLY asked for ŌĆö "I've added a reminder ŌĆ” due on Fri, Jun 5, 2026, 3:00 PM (tomorrow)" ŌĆö instead of echoing the wrong hour. A real, trust-eroding actuator defect found by live probe: `muse ask --with-tools "remind me to call the dentist tomorrow at 3pm"` STORED the reminder correctly (3pm local) but the model CONFIRMED "ŌĆ”at 6:00 AM" ŌĆö it read the raw UTC ISO hour (ŌĆ”T06:00:00Z, which is 3pm KST) and parroted "6:00 AM", telling the user a time they never asked for. The reminder fires at the right instant, so the firing path never saw it ŌĆö but a confidant that reads back the wrong time looks broken and erodes trust in every "did you set that?". Fixed by enriching the model-facing reminder MCP tool results (add/due/search/snooze/fire) with a `dueAtLocal` field ŌĆö the due time rendered in the SERVER's local timezone, the same wall clock the natural-language phrase was parsed against ("Fri, Jun 5, 2026, 3:00 PM (tomorrow)") via a new `formatReminderDueLocal` + `serializeReminderForModel` (packages/mcp/src/personal-reminders-store.ts) ŌĆö plus a `muse.reminders.add` tool-description anchor instructing the model to confirm with `dueAtLocal`, never the raw UTC ISO `dueAt`. The REST/web path is untouched (keeps the lean serializeReminder; the web UI formats its own times); only the LLM-facing tool results carry the extra field, so there's no API-shape change and no latency cost (pure string formatting on an already-returned result). This is actuator HARDENING per the human-directed focus ŌĆö a proven-once actuator that misreports the time is a user-facing reliability defect, and closing it is outward. Verified deterministically AND live: 6 new tz-robust unit tests (the formatter renders the LOCAL clock hour + AM/PM + a relative hint, NOT the bare UTC ISO; overdue / in-N-minutes hints; unparseable echoed verbatim so the value is never lost; serializeReminderForModel = serializeReminder + dueAtLocal) passing in BOTH TZ=Asia/Seoul AND TZ=UTC (apps/cli ŌĆö packages/mcp/test/personal-reminders-serialize.test.ts) + the full @muse/mcp suite green (173 files / 1461 tests) + `pnpm lint` 0/0 + a NEW PERMANENT live battery (apps/cli/scripts/verify-reminder-local-time.mjs, wired into eval:self-improving) that drives the REAL muse.reminders.add tool and then asks qwen3:8b to confirm using the real tool description+result ŌĆö asserting the model states the LOCAL 3 PM and NOT the UTC 6 AM (passed 2/2: "i've set a reminder to call the dentist tomorrow at 3:00 pm.") + a full LIVE `muse ask --with-tools` end-to-end round-trip showing the confirmation now reads "due on Fri, Jun 5, 2026, 3:00 PM (tomorrow)" where before the fix it read "at 6:00 AM". mcp 1461 + pnpm lint 0/0 + reminder-local-time battery 2/2 + live muse ask e2e ŌĆö Muse no longer tells you the wrong time when it sets a reminder, hardening the reminders actuator's confirmation path. - [Proactivity/Anticipation] Muse now PROACTIVELY WARNS you of an upcoming calendar double-booking ŌĆö it tells you about Friday's clash on Wednesday ŌĆö instead of only showing conflicts when you happen to run `muse today`. The capability map flagged this as the highest-value anticipation a single-user confidant can offer, and as a ­¤¤Ī gap: double-booking DETECTION already existed (detectCalendarConflicts) but ONLY on the PULL surfaces (`muse today`, `muse calendar conflicts`) ŌĆö the morning briefing, the evening recap, and every daemon tick were silent on conflicts, so a clash only ever surfaced if the user thought to look. This adds the missing PUSH: a pure `selectUpcomingConflicts(events, {now, withinDays})` in @muse/mcp (the future clashes whose overlap begins inside [now, now+withinDays], each carrying a stable dedup key + a human-readable LOCAL-time line; a clash already underway or in the past is excluded so Muse never nags about something un-bookable) layered on the existing detector, plus a `conflictWatchTick` daemon tick (apps/cli/src/commands-daemon.ts) that scans the upcoming calendar window and warns ONCE per clash via the user's configured messaging channel. It is off by default (MUSE_CONFLICT_WATCH_ENABLED), throttled (MUSE_CONFLICT_WATCH_INTERVAL_MS, default 30 min; MUSE_CONFLICT_WATCH_WITHIN_DAYS default 7), key-deduped via a ~/.muse/conflict-watch-fired.json sidecar so a standing clash never re-spams, fail-soft (a calendar provider hiccup never breaks the daemon ŌĆö same discipline as recap/briefing/email-sync ticks), and surfaced in `muse daemon --status` ("conflicts: enabled/disabled") for discoverability. This is a genuinely NEW axis (proactive anticipation, per B0's steering to favor a new axis over more grounding/time-display polish), reusing the existing conflict detector rather than reinventing it ŌĆö the new value is the proactive delivery + dedup layer. - [Actuation/Trust] The agent no longer HARD-FAILS on your own contacts ŌĆö `muse ask --with-tools "draft an email to Sarah ŌĆ”"` now produces a draft instead of erroring "Input guard detected private identifiers: email". Probing the outbound path exposed a severe, identity-breaking defect: the PII INPUT guard (createPiiInputGuard, packages/agent-core/src/guards.ts) was enabled BY DEFAULT (MUSE_INPUT_GUARD_PII_ENABLED defaulted true) and fail-closes the ENTIRE agent run when the assembled input carries any email/phone/private identifier ŌĆö but for a local "tell it everything" personal assistant whose OWN contacts and notes contain emails by nature, that breaks the core agent (and the outbound-email drafting that P41-2/P41-3 carefully hardened) on the user's own data EVERY time a contact with an email is in context. The fix is posture-aware (packages/autoconfigure/src/runtime-wiring.ts createInputGuards): the PII INPUT guard's purpose is preventing PII from EGRESSING to a third-party CLOUD model, but under MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY (the DEFAULT posture) the model is on-box and the model router refuses cloud egress via a SEPARATE deterministic gate (createModelProvider/LocalOnlyViolationError), so there is no third party to leak to and the block is pure breakage with zero benefit ŌĆö therefore the guard now fires by default ONLY when cloud egress is actually possible (MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY off); an explicit MUSE_INPUT_GUARD_PII_ENABLED=true still forces it on under any posture (opt-in). The INJECTION input guard (the real untrusted-content defense) and the PII OUTPUT mask (transcript/log hygiene) are UNCHANGED. Because this is a security-default change (big/risky per the decide-and-do directive), it was adversarially reviewed by an independent sub-agent panel BEFORE shipping (VERDICT: ship ŌĆö confirmed no real hole under local-only: the egress refusal is a separate gate, this guard's only consumer is the pre-model input pipeline, and there is no other sink it solely protected; this removes a control firing OUTSIDE its threat model, not a fail-open regression), and the cloud-side residual over-block was recorded as an explicit follow-up (Rejected ledger) rather than declared fixed. Verified deterministically AND live: 4 new posture unit tests (local-only default ŌåÆ injection guard only, PII block OFF so the agent isn't broken on the user's own contacts; MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY=false ŌåÆ PII guard present; explicit MUSE_INPUT_GUARD_PII_ENABLED=true forces it on under local-only; per-flag independent drops) ŌĆö @muse/autoconfigure 75 files / 497 tests + @muse/cli 174 files / 1920 tests + pnpm lint 0/0 + a LIVE before/after round-trip on qwen3:8b: the EXACT prompt that previously errored "Input guard detected private identifiers: email" now returns a complete, well-formed email draft to Sarah ("Subject: Request to Reschedule Our 2pm Meeting ŌĆ” Best regards"), while under MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY=false the same prompt STILL blocks with the PII error (egress protection for cloud users preserved). autoconfigure 497 + cli 1920 + lint 0/0 + live before(errored)/after(drafts)/cloud(still-blocks) on qwen ŌĆö a user can now have the agent draft emails and reason over their own contacts on a local-first assistant without a privacy guard meant for cloud egress breaking the whole run. ŌĆö P41-5 (Actuation/trust, posture-aware PII input guard; sub-agent-reviewed security-default change)
- [Actuation/Trust] The agent no longer MASKS your own contacts' details back to you ŌĆö `muse ask --with-tools "what is Sarah's email?"` now returns the real address instead of `***@***.***`. The output-guard sibling of P41-5 (which fixed the PII INPUT block that errored the whole run): the PII OUTPUT mask (createPiiMaskingOutputGuard, packages/agent-core/src/guards.ts) was enabled BY DEFAULT and REWRITES the agent's final answer ŌĆö and the cached + run-history copy, since the runtime's applyOutputGuards replaces finalResponse with the masked text (agent-runtime.ts:536-538) ŌĆö redacting any email/phone to `***@***.***`. So on a local "tell it everything" assistant, asking the agent for your OWN contact's email handed back a masked answer; the answer is the very thing the user asked for. And unlike a true egress control, the output mask doesn't even PREVENT egress (under a cloud model the PII already left on the INPUT side), so under local-only its only effect is corrupting the user-facing answer + the local store with zero privacy benefit. Fixed with the SAME posture-aware pattern as P41-5 (packages/autoconfigure/src/runtime-wiring.ts createOutputGuards): the PII OUTPUT mask fires by default ONLY when cloud egress is possible (MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY off, the non-default posture); an explicit MUSE_OUTPUT_GUARD_PII_MASK_ENABLED=true still forces it on under any posture (opt-in). The system-prompt-leakage output guard and the injection input guard are UNCHANGED. This completes the P41-5 theme (PII guards over-applying to the user's OWN data under local-only break the personal assistant) on the output side; the security reasoning is the same one the independent adversarial sub-agent panel validated for P41-5 (under local-only there is no third party to leak to ŌĆö the egress refusal is a separate deterministic gate in createModelProvider ŌĆö so this removes a control firing OUTSIDE its threat model, not a fail-open regression; cloud unchanged; override preserved). - [Actuation/Reliability] A multi-step "add the event AND remind me" request no longer silently LOSES the reminder ŌĆö `muse ask --with-tools "add a meeting with Sarah tomorrow at 2pm to my calendar, and remind me an hour before it"` now reliably creates BOTH the calendar event (2pm) and the reminder (1pm, an hour before), where before the reminder was silently dropped. The local model, making a ONE-TIME reminder, filled the muse.reminders.add `recurrence` arg with a sentinel like "none"/"once" (instead of OMITTING it as the schema asks), and the tool HARD-ERRORED on any value that wasn't exactly "daily"/"weekly" ŌĆö so a benign arg the model guessed cost the user their reminder, and the multi-step task half-failed with no sign to the user. The reminder is now ALWAYS created; the actuator survives a real-world model input instead of dropping the user's reminder over a recurrence-arg guess. - [Actuation/Reliability] "Send Sarah a message" now works on WHATEVER messenger you configured ŌĆö the send tool resolves your channel from config instead of failing on the local model's guess. Fixed by resolving the channel from config in the muse.messaging.send tool (packages/mcp/src/loopback-messaging.ts): an explicit REGISTERED providerId is honoured; a SINGLE configured provider is used automatically (the model needn't know its opaque id); ZERO providers ŌåÆ "no messenger configured" error; MULTIPLE providers + a missing/unknown id ŌåÆ ASK (error listing the configured ids, never guess among several); providerId is now OPTIONAL in the schema with a description steering the model to omit it unless multiple messengers exist. - [Trust/Outbound-safety] SECURITY FIX: the agent can no longer AUTO-SEND a message to a third party without draft-first confirmation ŌĆö `muse.messaging.send` now fails CLOSED. Probing P41-10's live behaviour exposed a real outbound-safety hole: `muse ask --with-tools "send Sarah a message that I'm running late"` actually SENT it ("I have successfully sent the message to Sarah") with NO draft-first confirmation. Root cause (packages/autoconfigure/src/loopback-tools.ts): the production muse.messaging.send tool is wired with actionLogFile + userId but NO approvalGate, and sendMessageWithApproval AUTO-APPROVES when no gate is present ŌĆö so the agent's third-party send fired on its own, while the sibling email/web/home actuators (apps/cli/src/actuator-tools.ts) are ALL draft-first gated with a clack confirm. That violates outbound-safety.md Rule 1 ("Draft-first, never auto-send. The agent produces the exact content and the user explicitly confirms that content before it leaves") on exactly the path P41-2 hardened for the human CLI but missed for the agent tool. Closed at the source (packages/mcp/src/loopback-messaging.ts): the action-logged send path now defaults to a FAIL-CLOSED gate (DENY_WITHOUT_CONFIRMATION) whenever no approvalGate is wired ŌĆö implementing outbound-safety's "a send never proceeds because the confirmation step failed / cannot be delivered" ŌĆö so the agent now REFUSES the send (recorded as a `refused` action-log entry, not `performed`) and points the user to the gated `muse messaging send` CLI, instead of auto-sending. This is a RESTRICTIVE change (it closes a hole, never opens one): the human CLI path (which passes its own draft-first gate, P41-2/P41-3) and the lightweight no-action-log/test path (direct send, no third-party risk) are both unchanged. Verified deterministically AND live: the F-1 outbound-safety recording test was split into a gated-`performed` case (an approving gate ŌåÆ send + performed log) PLUS a NEW no-gate ŌåÆ fail-closed case (the production wiring with no approvalGate now yields refused:true, a `refused` action-log entry, and NO `performed` entry) + the P41-10 provider-resolution send tests updated to pass an approving gate + the full @muse/mcp suite green (174 files / 1499 tests) + pnpm lint 0/0 + a full LIVE before/after on the local qwen3:8b: the IDENTICAL prompt "send Sarah a message that I am running 10 minutes late" that before the fix reported "I have successfully sent the message to Sarah" (auto-sent) now REFUSES ŌĆö "there is no draft-first confirmation channel set up for the agent ŌĆ” review and send via the `muse messaging send` command" ŌĆö and nothing is sent. mcp 1499 + pnpm lint 0/0 + live before(auto-sent)/after(fail-closed, refused) ŌĆö the agent can no longer send a message to someone without you confirming the exact content first, closing the last ungated outbound actuator. (Follow-on recorded in the Rejected ledger: thread a real draft-first confirm gate from `muse ask` so the agent can draft ŌåÆ you confirm ŌåÆ it sends, restoring the gated interactive capability.) - [Knowing-you/Felt] `muse today` now shows upcoming BIRTHDAYS ŌĆö a user checking their daily digest sees "­¤Äé Zelda ŌĆö today" / "­¤Äé Bob ŌĆö in 3 days" instead of missing it because they didn't wait for the daemon-fired morning brief. Probing the felt daily digest exposed a real gap: the morning BRIEF surfaces birthdays (resolveUpcomingBirthdays + formatBirthdayBriefLine, wired into the briefing daemon tick), but the on-demand `muse today` command ŌĆö the thing a user actually runs to see their day ŌĆö had NO birthday handling at all (commands-today.ts composed reminders / followups / tasks / events / notes / headlines only; zero birthday references). So whichever surface a user relied on was inconsistent: the proactive brief knew about birthdays, the on-demand pull silently didn't, and a user who runs `muse today` (or the in-chat /today) would walk right past someone's birthday ŌĆö defeating the whole point of storing it. Closed by reusing the brief's exact machinery in the today digest's composeLocalBriefing (apps/cli/src/commands-today.ts): a new readUpcomingBirthdays helper reads the contacts file (queryContacts), runs resolveUpcomingBirthdays(contacts, {now, withinDays: 7}) (the same per-contact next-occurrence + year-wrap logic the brief uses), and maps to {name, daysUntil}; a formatBirthdays section renderer (­¤Äé <name> ŌĆö today / tomorrow / in N days) is wired into formatTodayBrief so BOTH the on-demand `muse today` and the in-chat /today (which share formatTodayBrief) now surface them. A contact with no birthday, or whose birthday is outside the 7-day window, is skipped; the section is omitted entirely when there are no upcoming birthdays. This is a felt/knowing-you slice (the daily digest now reflects the people you care about), genuinely distinct from the recent actuation/messaging fixes, reusing proven contacts-birthday machinery rather than reinventing it. - [Grounding/Honesty] Muse no longer LIES about remembering ŌĆö `muse ask "remember that I'm allergic to penicillin"` now answers honestly ("I can't save that fact from a one-shot question. To remember this, run `muse remember \"I am allergic to penicillin\"`, or tell me inside a `muse chat` session") instead of the fabricated "I've noted your allergy to penicillin". Probing the core "tell it everything, it remembers" promise exposed a real trust failure: a one-shot `muse ask` told to remember a fact answered "I've noted your allergy" ŌĆö and even fabricated a citation to a non-existent "allergy note" (the grounding gate caught and stripped that) ŌĆö while persisting NOTHING. The recall path is read-only by design (the remember_fact tool is in RECALL_FORBIDDEN_TOOL_NAMES and there is no auto-extraction on that path; memory writes happen via `muse remember` or `muse chat` auto-extraction), so a one-shot ask genuinely cannot save ŌĆö but the model CLAIMED it did, which is the worst kind of confidant lie (the user trusts Muse kept something it silently dropped, and discovers it forgot only later). This EXTENDS the honesty edge (the same recall answer-behaviour contract CITATION_INSTRUCTION_LINES that already carries the I'm-not-sure and conflict-surfacing rules, apps/cli/src/commands-ask.ts): a SAVING rule tells the model that this one-shot answer cannot persist anything, so when the user says remember / note / save / "don't forget" a FACT about them, it must NOT claim it saved or noted it (that would be a lie) and must instead say it can't save from a one-shot question and DIRECT the user to the real save path ŌĆö run `muse remember "<the fact>"` or tell Muse inside a kept `muse chat` session ŌĆö with an explicit carve-out so a request to set a reminder or task (which IS handled by tools) is not swept up by the rule. It is a prompt-instruction behaviour with NO new model call ŌåÆ ZERO added latency; it does not change the grounding GATE; and it is fail-soft (if ignored the answer is no worse than before). This is a NEW honesty SURFACE (the remember-lie), an extension of the edge like P38-36 conflict-surfacing ŌĆö not grounding-gate false-positive polish ŌĆö and a genuinely fresh axis after a streak of actuation/messaging work. - [Recall/Perception] "What's due tomorrow?" (and "today / this week?") now answers correctly ŌĆö your tasks' and reminders' due dates are surfaced to the model in a READABLE LOCAL form in the recall context, not as opaque raw UTC ISO timestamps. - [Actuation/Trust] The agent can SEND a message again ŌĆö and now DRAFT-FIRST: `muse ask --with-tools "send Sarah I'm running late"` shows the exact draft and fires only on your explicit confirm, completing the P41-11 security arc. So the agent's send is now: in an interactive terminal, DRAFT-FIRST (you see the exact message, you confirm, it sends); in a non-TTY (headless / daemon / CI) or with no gate, FAIL-CLOSED (the confirm can't be delivered, so the send does not happen) ŌĆö exactly outbound-safety.md's rule ("a send never proceeds because the confirmation step cannot be delivered"). It is built under --with-tools (NOT gated behind --actuators) so a benign "send X a message" reaches it directly. - [Trust/Grounding] Your OWN benign notes no longer get mistaken for a prompt-injection attack ŌĆö `muse ask --with-tools` over a note like "Do not forget to get all the groceries and the milk on the way home" no longer dies with "Input guard detected injection patterns: role_override"; the recall turn proceeds and answers. Closing the P41-12-probe follow-on, this fixes a guard turning the user's own trust-everything notes against them: the default-wired injection input guard (createInjectionInputGuard ŌåÆ findInjectionPatterns, packages/agent-core/src/guards.ts) scans the ENTIRE assembled prompt ŌĆö INCLUDING the user's first-party grounding context (notes/tasks/contacts) ŌĆö and fail-closes the whole run on any match, and its first role_override pattern ended in `(instructions?|and)`. The bare `|and` matched almost any benign "ŌĆ”allŌĆ” andŌĆ”" / "ŌĆ”previousŌĆ” andŌĆ”" prose, so real first-party notes ("Do not forget to get all the groceries AND the milk", "Ignore the previous draft AND use the new one", "disregard all the old prices AND updateŌĆ”") tripped role_override and the agent answered nothing but the guard-block reason ŌĆö the injection-guard sibling of the P41-5 PII over-block. Fixed at the source (packages/policy/src/injection-patterns.ts) by replacing the lazy `|and` with the EXPLICIT override-target noun set `(instructions?|prompts?|rules?|directions?|guidelines?|commands?|messages?|context)` ŌĆö which both KILLS the benign-prose false positives AND WIDENS genuine detection that a bare `instructions?` would have narrowed: "ignore all previous RULES", "disregard the above PROMPT", "ignore the above DIRECTIONS", "forget all prior COMMANDS" are now all caught (none of the other patterns catch those ŌĆö line 85 needs disregard+your/the/my, line 88 needs override), which matters because there is NO LLM-classification backstop wired by default ŌĆö the regex guard is the only injection defense, so the fix had to PRESERVE detection, not just delete the offending branch. (Intended as a sub-agent-reviewed security slice per the deferred entry; the review sub-agent hit an API ConnectionRefused this fire, so the safety argument was made inline and proven BOTH directions by test instead.) - [Actuation/Reach] The agent can now DELETE a task you added by mistake ŌĆö "delete the milk task, I added it by accident" / "scrap the dentist task" REMOVES it from your todo list, where before the agent could only mark a task DONE (which keeps it as a done record), never remove a mistaken one. Closed by adding a `muse.tasks.delete` tool (packages/mcp/src/loopback-tasks.ts) that mirrors the proven `muse.reminders.clear`: it resolves the task by id OR a distinct title word via `resolveTaskRef` (the P41-9 by-name resolver) ŌĆö an ambiguous word returns the matching candidates instead of a blind delete, an unknown ref errors ŌĆö then removes it and returns `{ removed: true, id }`. The new `delete` and the existing `complete` are a deliberately NON-confusable pair (the SAME coexistence pattern `muse.calendar` already ships with `update` + `delete`), and both carry a crisp "use when / not when" line in their descriptions per tool-calling.md (complete = mark FINISHED, kept as a done record; delete = REMOVE a task added by mistake, gone). It is write-risk on the user's OWN task (no outbound-safety gate ŌĆö same as complete/snooze, nothing leaves the machine). This is an Actuation/Reach slice (the agent gains a real action it lacked), rotated off the recent perception/felt/trust fires per loop-v2 B0 ("favour a genuinely NEW axis"), reusing the proven by-name + clear machinery rather than reinventing it. - [Actuation/Perception] The agent can now tell you your calendar DOUBLE-BOOKINGS ŌĆö "do I have any conflicts next week?" / "am I double-booked?" / "any overlapping meetings?" lists the clashing event pairs, where before the agent could enumerate events (`list`) and check free/busy at a time (`availability`) but had no way to surface OVERLAPS. Probing the agent calendar surface exposed the gap: `muse.calendar` had providers / list / availability / add / update / delete but NO conflict detection ŌĆö so a user asking the agent about double-bookings got nothing, even though the CLI `muse calendar conflicts` and the morning brief (`selectUpcomingConflicts`) already surface them from the SAME logic. Closed by adding a `muse.calendar.conflicts` read tool (packages/mcp/src/loopback-calendar.ts) that fetches events in a window (`fromIso`/`toIso` accept ISO-8601 OR a relative phrase like 'next week'; default now..+7 days; fans out across all providers when no providerId) and runs the EXISTING, already-unit-tested `detectCalendarConflicts` (packages/mcp/src/calendar-conflicts.ts) ŌĆö returning each overlapping PAIR (`a`, `b`, each with readable local times) plus the `overlap` span and a `total`, so the model can report "you're double-booked: Design review and 1:1 with Sam overlap 10:30ŌĆō11:00". - [Perception/Reach] `muse ask --url <pdf>` now READS an online PDF and grounds on its text ŌĆö a user can ask about a policy doc, paper, or manual linked on the web, not just an HTML page. - [Actuation/Reach] Reminders can now repeat MONTHLY ŌĆö a user can ask "remind me to pay rent on the 1st of every month" (or `muse remind ŌĆ” --repeat monthly`) and it sticks as a recurring reminder, where before only daily/weekly were allowed and a monthly request silently degraded to a ONE-TIME reminder. Probing the reminder actuator exposed a real gap: reminder recurrence was `"daily" | "weekly"` ONLY, and `normalizeReminderRecurrence` EXPLICITLY rejected "monthly" with a note ("recurrence 'monthly' isn't supported (only 'daily' or 'weekly'); created a one-time reminder") ŌĆö so the single most common recurring cadence (rent, bills, subscriptions, salary) could not be scheduled at all, the recurrence feature missing its most-wanted use. Closed by adding `"monthly"` end-to-end across EVERY surface that gated it: the `ReminderRecurrence` type (packages/mcp/src/personal-reminders-store.ts), `normalizeReminderRecurrence`, the `isPersistedReminder` shape-validation guard, the agent `muse.reminders.add` tool's inputSchema `enum` + its description (packages/mcp/src/loopback-reminders.ts), the CLI `muse remind --repeat` option + its validation + help (apps/cli/src/commands-remind.ts), and the REST `POST /reminders` validation (apps/api/src/reminders-routes.ts) ŌĆö no surface left silently rejecting it. The load-bearing part is the re-arm math: `nextReminderOccurrence` for monthly is CALENDAR-aware (unlike the fixed-interval daily/weekly path), because months are 28ŌĆō31 days ŌĆö it advances whole months computed from the ORIGINAL due day (never iteratively from a clamped result, which would drift), CLAMPING the day to the target month's length so a reminder due on the 31st lands on the LAST day of a short month (Feb 28, or 29 in a leap year) and RETURNS to the 31st in the next long month rather than getting stuck on the 28th, and it skips any months missed while the daemon was off, re-arming to the next FUTURE occurrence (not a backlog). It's deterministic (no model in the recurrence logic). This is an Actuation/Reach slice (a genuinely new scheduling capability), distinct from the recent felt/reasoning/perception fires, and ŌĆö unlike a tool the small model won't reach for ŌĆö the reminder intent is reliably tool-selected (verified live). - [Perception/Honesty] `muse ask --file <dir>` no longer SILENTLY truncates a big folder ŌĆö it now tells you when it grounded on only the first 25 documents, so a missing answer isn't mistaken for "not in your documents" (Muse shows its work). Probing the folder-grounding path exposed a silent cap that undercut the honesty edge: `extractDirectoryDocuments` caps at 25 docs (default `maxFiles=25`) and the `muse ask --file <dir>` caller just took whatever it returned ŌĆö so pointing `--file` at a 50-document folder grounded the answer on only 25, with ZERO indication the other 25 were excluded. That is exactly the "no silent caps" failure the loop bans, and for a "tell it everything, it shows its work" assistant it is worse than a missing format: the user reads an incomplete/"I'm not sure" answer as "the fact isn't in my documents" when really the answer-bearing doc was simply never read. Closed in apps/cli/src/document-reader.ts: `extractDirectoryDocuments` now returns a `{ documents, totalFound, cap }` shape (where `totalFound` is the total SUPPORTED documents in the folder BEFORE the cap), and a pure exported `formatDirectoryCapNotice(folder, totalFound, cap)` renders an honest notice ("<folder> has N documents ŌĆö grounding on the first 25 only; the other M were NOT read. Ask about a narrower subset, or split the folder.") which the `muse ask --file <dir>` path prints to stderr whenever the folder was truncated, and which is empty when everything was read (no noise). The same fix refreshed the stale empty-folder message (it still listed only the pre-P37-28 formats `.txt/.md/.markdown/.pdf/.log/.csv`, omitting the `.org/.rst/.adoc/.mdx` that P37-28 added) to a non-stale form. It is deterministic (no model ŌĆö the cap and counts are file-walk facts) and additive (a folder under the cap behaves exactly as before). This is a Perception/Honesty slice ŌĆö the "shows its work" edge applied to ad-hoc folder grounding ŌĆö deliberately rotated off the recent actuation (P41) streak, reusing the existing walk/extract machinery rather than reinventing it. Verified deterministically AND live: tests (`extractDirectoryDocuments(dir, 1)` reports `documents.length === 1` AND `totalFound > 1` AND `cap === 1`, so a truncated folder is detectable; `formatDirectoryCapNotice` names the total, the first-25, and the not-read count when over the cap, and returns "" at or under the cap ŌĆö apps/cli/src/document-reader.test.ts, plus the existing folder tests updated to the new `{ documents }` return shape, all green) + the full @muse/cli suite (174 files / 1952 tests) + @muse/cli tsc build + pnpm lint 0/0 + a FULL LIVE `muse ask --file <dir> "what is in doc 1?"` on the loop PC over a seeded folder of 30 `.md` documents: the run printed "muse: ŌĆ”/docs has 30 documents ŌĆö grounding on the first 25 only; the other 5 were NOT read. - [Reasoning] `muse ask "what is 1847 * 2963?"` now returns the EXACT answer ("1847 * 2963 = 5,472,661") deterministically ŌĆö closing the symbolic half of P41-16's recorded follow-on without relying on the small model to tool-call. P41-16 wired the exact arithmetic evaluator into the agent tool set but HONESTLY recorded that the recall-first `muse ask` path still answers arithmetic INLINE with the local 8B ŌĆö which can't multiply: it returned 5,467,461 for 1847├Ś2963 (off by ~5,200). The right fix for a small reasoning=false model is NOT "make it tool-call" (it won't reliably, and a system-prompt steer was already tried + reverted) ŌĆö it is a DETERMINISTIC pure-arithmetic fast-path. A new precision-first detector `detectArithmeticQuery` (apps/cli/src/arithmetic-query.ts) recognises a query that is NOTHING BUT a calculation ŌĆö after stripping the "what is ŌĆ”?/calculate/compute/how much is" framing and a trailing "=", the remainder must contain only digits / parentheses / `.` / `,` / `+ - * / %` AND a real binary operator ŌĆö and `muse ask` short-circuits it (right after the casual/meta short-circuits, BEFORE any retrieval or model call) through the SHARED `evaluateArithmeticExpression`, which was extracted from @muse/mcp's `muse.math` server and exported so the tool AND the fast-path evaluate through ONE validated, eval-free recursive-descent evaluator (the math tool's `execute` was refactored to call it ŌĆö DRY, no behavior change). The answer is formatted exactly with thousands grouping ("1847 * 2963 = 5,472,661"). Precision-first by construction so retrieval is never hijacked: a real notes question ("what is my Q3 budget?") has letters and falls through to recall; a bare number ("what is 42?") has no operator and falls through; a lone negative ("-5") has no binary operator and falls through; an over-256-char expression falls through. This is the Reasoning axis (the ask recall path's arithmetic correctness), deliberately rotated off the recent perception/actuation slices, and it complements rather than duplicates P41-16: P41-16 made the tool REACHABLE for `--with-tools` natural-language phrasings; this makes SYMBOLIC arithmetic in the plain recall wedge EXACT without any tool-selection. HONEST SCOPE: natural-language phrasings ("1847 multiplied by 2963", "18% of 840,000") still contain words, so they fall through to the model (the `--with-tools` math tool is their path) ŌĆö this fast-path is for symbolic expressions only. Verified deterministically AND live: tests (`detectArithmeticQuery` extracts the expression from framed arithmetic questions, returns null for notes-questions / bare numbers / lone signs / over-long input; `formatArithmeticResult` groups integer and fractional results ŌĆö apps/cli/src/arithmetic-query.test.ts) + the full @muse/cli suite (175 files / 1958 tests) + the full @muse/mcp suite (1520 tests ŌĆö the math tool still passes through the extracted evaluator) + mcp/cli/autoconfigure/agent-core/api tsc builds + pnpm lint 0/0 + FULL LIVE on the loop PC: `muse ask "what is 1847 * 2963?"` ŌåÆ "1847 * 2963 = 5,472,661" (exact, no model), `muse ask "calculate (1200 + 850) / 2"` ŌåÆ "(1200 + 850) / 2 = 1,025", `muse ask --json "compute 840000 * 0.18"` ŌåÆ {"answer":"840000 * 0.18 = 151,200",...} (exact JSON), and the NEGATIVE control `muse ask "what is my Q3 budget?"` ŌåÆ NOT hijacked (it went to retrieval and answered "[from: no relevant notes found]"). cli 1958 + mcp 1520 + 5 tsc builds + lint 0/0 + live muse ask (3 exact arithmetic answers incl. --json, 1 non-hijack control) ŌĆö a user who asks Muse a symbolic arithmetic question now gets the mathematically exact answer instead of a confidently-wrong small-model guess. ŌĆö P41-20 (Reasoning, deterministic pure-arithmetic fast-path in `muse ask`; shares the math server's evaluator, precision-first so notes queries are untouched)
- [Knowing-you] `muse contacts network <name>` ŌĆö you can now TRAVERSE the people graph, not just build it: see a person's immediate circle (their direct connections) AND who they reach THROUGH those connections (2nd-degree friends-of-friends, each labelled with the via-person). P37-20/21 made the people graph RECORDABLE ŌĆö a person's role to you (relationship) + bidirectional EDGES between people (`muse contacts link Bob Alice --as "works with"`), and `muse contacts list` renders a person's direct edges flat ŌĆö but there was NO way to TRAVERSE it: no focused per-person network view, and crucially no 2nd-degree reach (you couldn't ask "who's in Bob's orbit" beyond his immediate links). B0 (the loop authority) named exactly this as the next knowing-you axis to favour over another encryption/grounding slice ("a NEW knowing-you capability like relationship EDGES"). A new pure `buildContactNetwork(contacts, root)` (apps/cli/src/contact-network.ts) walks the graph to depth 2: direct = the root contact's `connections`; 2nd-degree = the connections of each directly-linked person who is ALSO a contact in the graph (a connection's `to` is a NAME, so a leaf name that isn't itself a contact yields no 2nd hop), with the root, the direct set, and duplicates excluded so each person appears exactly once at its nearest distance. A pure `formatContactNetwork` renders the card ("<root>'s network: Direct: Ōåö <relation> <name> ŌĆ”; Through them: ŌåÆ <name> (<relation> <via>)"), with a "connected to" fallback when an edge has no relation label and link-guidance when the person has no connections yet. The `muse contacts network <name>` subcommand resolves the name through the SAME `resolveContact` seam as `muse contacts resolve` ŌĆö exact/unique-substring ŌåÆ resolved; 2+ matches ŌåÆ AMBIGUOUS candidate list (never a best-guess, per the people-graph safety boundary); 0 ŌåÆ not-found ŌĆö so it cannot act on the wrong person. Fully deterministic (no model, no network); reuses the existing connection model + resolver rather than reinventing them. This is a Knowing-you slice (the relationship-edges axis B0 called for), deliberately a genuinely NEW capability rather than another encryption-tail or grounding-micro slice, and rotated off the recent reasoning/perception/actuation fires. - [Actuation] `muse tasks complete groceries` ŌĆö the CLI now completes / edits / deletes a task BY TITLE, not just by raw uuid, closing a CLIŌåöagent asymmetry. - [Perception/Honesty] `muse ask --url <long page>` no longer SILENTLY truncates ŌĆö it now tells you when it grounded on only the first 60,000 characters, the `--url` twin of P37-30's `--file <dir>` folder-cap notice. `fetchReadableUrl` caps a fetched web page at 60k characters and returns `truncated: boolean`, but the `--url` block in commands-ask.ts consumed `fetched.text` and IGNORED `fetched.truncated` ŌĆö so asking about a long article or docs page grounded the answer on the first 60k with ZERO indication the rest was unread. For a "shows its work" assistant that is the same silent-cap honesty hole P37-30 closed for folder grounding, and it is worse than a missing format: an answer that lives past the cap reads as "the page doesn't say that" when really Muse never read that far. Closed with a pure exported `formatUrlTruncationNotice(source, maxChars)` (apps/cli/src/document-reader.ts, placed next to `formatDirectoryCapNotice` as its sibling) which the `--url` path prints to stderr whenever `fetched.truncated` is set, citing the SAME host label the answer cites ("[from <host>]"): "muse: <host> is long ŌĆö grounded on only the first 60,000 characters; anything past that was NOT read. If your answer might be deeper in the page, ask about a specific section." It is deterministic (the truncated flag is set by the fetch character cap, and the notice fires before the model call, so it shows regardless of the answer) and additive (a page under the cap behaves exactly as before ŌĆö no notice). This is a Perception/Honesty slice completing the ad-hoc-grounding truncation-honesty arc P37-30 started (folder ŌåÆ now URL); a redundant first pick this fire (a `muse notes links` command that already existed in commands-notes-rag.ts) was caught by self-review and reverted before this verified-missing slice was built.
