- [Reach] `muse email reply <id>` ŌĆö Muse can now REPLY to an email you RECEIVED (draft-first, to the original sender, with a 'Re:' subject), not just compose a brand-new one. Reach was send-ONLY: `email_send` / `muse email send` compose a new email to a NAMED CONTACT (recipient resolved via the contacts graph), but there was no way to ANSWER a received message ŌĆö and a reply's recipient is the message's SENDER (an email address carried by the message), which the contact-name send path structurally can't target. This adds the reply across the whole stack while REUSING the proven outbound-safety gate rather than duplicating it: the draft-first "present the EXACT draft ŌåÆ send only on approval ŌåÆ action-log every outcome" core was extracted from `sendEmailWithApproval` into a shared `dispatchEmailDraft` (behavior-preserving ŌĆö the existing send tests stay green), and a new `replyEmailWithApproval` funnels through it with the recipient PRE-RESOLVED BY THE MESSAGE (never guessed; a missing/garbage reply address fails closed BEFORE the approval gate is even shown), plus a pure idempotent `replySubject` that adds 'Re:' once and never stacks it. The reply target is read from the original message via `EmailReader.getMessage` + `extractEmailAddress(message.from)`. It ships on TWO surfaces: a new `muse email reply --id <id> --body <text>` CLI command (the reliable, explicit surface: reads the message, drafts the reply to the sender, confirms, sends) AND an `email_reply` agent tool (execute-risk, armed with MUSE_GMAIL_TOKEN alongside email_send, gated by the same approval gate). - [Grounding edge] `muse ask --verify-claims` ŌĆö PER-CLAIM grounding (Self-RAG ISSUP, arXiv:2310.11511): a single fabricated clause in an otherwise-grounded answer is now flagged "I'm not sure about ŌĆ”" instead of riding through, where before the grounding gate was all-or-nothing per WHOLE answer. This closes the one place the project's defining functional edge ("Muse shows its work": cite-or-stay-silent, fabrication=0) was still whole-answer: `verifyGroundingWithReverify` (packages/agent-core/src/knowledge-recall.ts) ran ONE judge on the entire answer, so a multi-claim answer with a single fabricated value either PASSED (the wrong clause barely dented whole-answer lexical coverage ŌĆö the documented wrong-value hole) or got the ENTIRE answer refused (over-refusal, the exact lever that kept forcing escape-hatches); the only claim-level catch, `answerAssertsUnsupportedValue`, was VALUE-only (a drifted digit / email / capitalised named-entity) and blind to a fabricated relational/qualitative claim made of ordinary words. The direction was chosen by a 6-agent code-grounded direction-review workflow (5 lens-assessors + a synthesizer) as the highest-value strengthening of the CLAUDE.md-mandated core edge, and verified-not-built by grep + codegraph (no segmentClaims/perClaim/claimLevel anywhere; the sole judge was whole-answer). Added a pure exported `segmentClaims(answer)` that splits an answer into atomic claims on sentence terminators, semicolons, and clausal `and`/`but` ŌĆö CONSERVATIVELY: it only splits a conjunction when the right side is a real clause (carries a value or is Ōēź5 words), so "Mina owns pricing and the budget was 2,000,000 KRW" yields TWO claims while "Sarah and Bob report to Mina" stays ONE (under-segmenting only degrades to whole-answer checking; over-segmenting would risk dropping a true clause), with [citation] markers riding along ŌĆö and a pure `verifyGroundingPerClaim(answer, matches, query, reverify)` that runs the SAME one-shot judge on each atomic claim, KEEPS the cited true clauses verbatim, and DROPS only the unsupported ones, appending an honest "I'm not sure about: <dropped subjects>" note. It is wired as an OPT-IN `muse ask --verify-claims` flag (default OFF ŌåÆ zero regression risk) applied ONLY to an answer the whole-answer gate already passed as `grounded`. Safety is by construction ŌĆö because it refines an ALREADY-grounded answer it can only TIGHTEN (it can never manufacture a refusal from a passing answer), it FAILS OPEN per claim (a judge error KEEPS the claim, matching the existing value-escalation fail-open), a 0/1-claim answer is returned untouched without a judge call, and claims beyond a cap are kept verbatim (never dropped unchecked). This is a Grounding-edge slice ŌĆö the project's defining differentiator that CLAUDE.md mandates every iteration strengthen ŌĆö built in agent-core (diversifying off a long run of CLI slices). Verified deterministically AND live: 9 new agent-core unit tests (segmentClaims: clausal-and vs noun-list split, sentence split, citation-marker retention, empty/single; verifyGroundingPerClaim: drops-only-the-unsupported-clause with the disclaimer / a fully-supported answer untouched / a single-claim answer makes no judge call / a judge ERROR fails open and keeps the claim ŌĆö packages/agent-core/test/knowledge-recall-reverify.test.ts) + the full @muse/agent-core suite (114 files / 1455 tests) + the full @muse/cli suite (176 files / 1994 tests) + tsc builds + pnpm lint 0/0 + a FULL LIVE local-qwen3:8b battery (apps/cli/scripts/verify-claim-grounding.mjs, expanded to 8/8): the MIXED case "Mina owns pricing AND the budget was 2,000,000 KRW" returned dropped=1 with answer="Mina owns pricing\n\nI'm not sure about: the budget was 2,000,000 KRW." (fabricated clause dropped, supported clause kept), AND the FULLY-SUPPORTED over-refusal tripwire "Mina owns pricing and the team is three people" came back UNTOUCHED (dropped=0) ŌĆö proving the slice raises fabrication-catching WITHOUT raising false-refusal ŌĆö plus a live `muse ask --verify-claims "who owns pricing?"` over a seeded note ran clean (grounded, per-claim check silent since nothing to drop) and the flag appears in `muse ask --help`. agent-core 1455 + cli 1994 + lint 0/0 + live per-claim battery 8/8 (drops fabricated, keeps supported, no over-refusal) + live ask --verify-claims round-trip ŌĆö a user can now opt into per-claim checking so a single unsupported clause in a mostly-grounded answer is surfaced as "I'm not sure about that part" instead of silently riding through or nuking the whole answer. ŌĆö P38-38 (Grounding edge, muse ask --verify-claims per-claim ISSUP refinement; segmentClaims + verifyGroundingPerClaim in agent-core, opt-in, fail-open, only-tightens-a-grounded-answer; direction picked via a 6-agent code-grounded review workflow)
- [Trust/discretion] `muse privacy` ŌĆö SEE the "it can't tell anyone" half of Muse's contract: a read-only inventory of every confided store's at-rest state + whether the encryption key is strong. - [Felt] `muse week` ŌĆö your next 7 days at a glance, GROUPED BY DAY (events + due tasks + birthdays under each day's header), so you can plan the week instead of reading a flat next-24h brief. `muse today` is the today-framed brief (it leads with overdue, today's tasks, and the next-24h calendar); its `--lookahead-hours` flag widens only the CALENDAR window and still renders one FLAT "Upcoming (N)" list ŌĆö no command grouped the upcoming week BY DAY, and none pulled due tasks or birthdays under the day they fall on, so planning the week ("what does Wednesday look like?") meant scanning a flat dump and doing the date math. - [Knowledge] `muse notes related <note>` ŌĆö find notes SEMANTICALLY related to a given one (embedding similarity), discovering connections the explicit [[wiki-links]] missed. The note-link graph (P42-1..5) handled EXPLICIT links ŌĆö links/graph/backlinks/fix-links ŌĆö and the recall path does QUERYŌåÆnote search, but NOTHING surfaced NOTEŌåÆnote semantic relatedness ("what else is about this?"), so a Zettelkasten full of topically-related-but-unlinked notes had no way to discover those connections. Added a `muse notes related` command (apps/cli/src/commands-notes-rag.ts) that ranks the corpus by cosine similarity between each note's CENTROID embedding (the component-wise mean of that note's chunk embeddings) and the target note's centroid, over the already-built notes index ŌĆö the embedding-similarity complement to the explicit link graph (a GraphRAG / HippoRAG sibling: it finds the related notes the links missed). It composes three pure helpers: `rankRelatedNotes(index, targetPath, limit=5)` (excludes the target itself and any note with zero embedding overlap, returns the top-N by descending score), `resolveIndexNotePath(index, query)` (resolves a user note reference to an indexed file path by exact path, then basename stem, then a unique stem-substring ŌĆö extension-insensitive so 'b', 'b.md', and 'B.MD' all resolve), and `formatRelatedNotes(target, related, dir)` (renders each as a `NN%` score + folder-relative path, with a "stands alone" empty-state line). The command loads the EXISTING index (and hints to run `muse notes reindex` if it is absent), supports `--limit` and `--json`, and is read-only; the ranking itself is fully deterministic (cosine over stored vectors ŌĆö the only model involvement is the pre-existing reindex that produced the embeddings, not this command). This is a Knowledge slice (semantic note discovery, expanding the thin Knowledge axis the human-directed focus calls out) that complements rather than duplicates the link graph (explicit edges) and recall (query-to-note); before building, both notes command files were checked to confirm no prior related / note-to-note / similarity command existed. Verified deterministically AND live: 6 unit tests (rankRelatedNotes ranks by centroid cosine and excludes the target plus cosine-0 notes, honours the limit, and returns [] for an unknown/chunkless target; resolveIndexNotePath matches an exact path, a basename stem, a case-insensitive stem, and returns undefined on no match; formatRelatedNotes renders a % score with the relative path and a stands-alone line when empty ŌĆö apps/cli/src/commands-notes-rag.test.ts) + the full @muse/cli suite (178 files / 2009 tests) + @muse/cli tsc build + pnpm lint 0/0 + a FULL LIVE run on the loop PC: a three-note corpus (vpn.md about the office VPN / WireGuard / MTU, wireguard.md about WireGuard tunnel config, recipe.md about cooking pasta) was reindexed via `muse notes reindex` (Ollama nomic-embed-text, "3 embedded"), then `muse notes related vpn` printed "­¤öŚ Notes related to 'vpn.md':" with "63%  wireguard.md" ranked ABOVE "45%  recipe.md" ŌĆö the semantically-related WireGuard note surfaced higher than the unrelated recipe. cli 2009 + tsc + lint 0/0 + live semantic ranking (related note above unrelated) ŌĆö a user can now discover the notes topically related to any note, finding connections their explicit links never recorded. ŌĆö P42-7 (Knowledge, `muse notes related` semantic note discovery via centroid-embedding cosine over the index; pure rankRelatedNotes + resolveIndexNotePath + formatRelatedNotes, deterministic ranking, complements the [[link]] graph)
- [Trust/discretion] `muse doctor` now reports the AT-REST encryption posture ŌĆö the discretion ("can't tell anyone") half of Muse's identity surfaces in the STANDARD health command, not only the dedicated `muse privacy`. P44-7 added the inventory command, but `muse doctor` ŌĆö the command users actually run to check "is my setup healthy?" ŌĆö reported only the CLOUD-egress (MUSE_LOCAL_ONLY) posture, so a user whose confided stores are still plaintext, or are encrypted only under the weak DERIVABLE per-host fallback key, would never learn it unless they happened to run the separate `muse privacy`. Added a pure `atRestDoctorCheck(posture)` (apps/cli/src/commands-privacy.ts) that turns P44-7's `collectPrivacyPosture` inventory into a doctor health check with three outcomes: WARN when any existing encryptable store is plaintext (detail names the count + the specific stores + points at `muse privacy`), WARN when every store is encrypted but under the derivable fallback key (detail says to set MUSE_MEMORY_KEY), and OK when all existing sensitive stores are encrypted with an explicit MUSE_MEMORY_KEY (or when nothing sensitive has been created yet, so there is nothing to protect). It is wired into `runLocalDoctor` immediately after the existing local-only (cloud-egress) check, so the two halves of the identity ŌĆö "can't reach a cloud" and "can't tell anyone" ŌĆö appear together in one health view. Read-only and deterministic (it inventories file headers via the same isFileEncryptedAtRest sniff, no decryption, no key, no model). This is a Trust/discretion slice that makes P44-7's posture DISCOVERABLE in the place users look for setup problems ŌĆö the dedicated command alone reaches only users who already know to run it. Verified deterministically AND live: 4 unit tests (an existing plaintext store yields a warn naming "1/2 sensitive store(s) PLAINTEXT (contacts)" with the `muse privacy` pointer; all-encrypted-but-derivable-fallback-key yields a warn citing MUSE_MEMORY_KEY; all-encrypted-with-an-explicit-key yields ok; and no-sensitive-store-yet yields ok with "nothing to encrypt" ŌĆö apps/cli/src/commands-privacy.test.ts) + the full @muse/cli suite (178 files / 2013 tests) + @muse/cli tsc build + pnpm lint 0/0 + a FULL LIVE run on the loop PC: with MUSE_MEMORY_KEY unset and a plaintext contacts store seeded, `muse doctor --local` printed "  ┬Ę at-rest encryption: 1/1 sensitive store(s) PLAINTEXT (contacts) ŌĆö run `muse privacy`" as a warn line directly beneath the "Ō£ō local-only: ­¤öÆ on (default) ŌĆö cloud LLM + voice egress blocked" check. cli 2013 + tsc + lint 0/0 + live doctor at-rest warn ŌĆö a user running the standard `muse doctor` health check now sees whether their confided data is actually protected at rest and whether the key is strong, instead of that gap being invisible unless they sought out the privacy command. ŌĆö P44-8 (Trust/discretion, `muse doctor` at-rest encryption check via P44-7's collectPrivacyPosture; pure atRestDoctorCheck, deterministic, surfaces the discretion posture in the standard health command)
